Discussion Name: Is Feminism a Force For Good?

1. Feminism is a force for good in the world.
1.1. Pro: Feminist spaces are open and accepting places for political discussion.
1.1.1. Con: Various factions of feminism have previously attempted to deplatform and silence [other women](https://www.theatlantic.com/ideas/archive/2019/05/camille-paglia-uarts-left-deplatform/587125/)(“Camille Paglia should be removed from UArts faculty and replaced by a queer person of color,” an online petition declares. “If, due to tenure, it is absolutely illegal to remove her, then the University must at least offer alternate sections of the classes she teaches, instead taught by professors who respect transgender students and survivors of sexual assault.” Regardless, the students behind the petition want her banned from holding speaking events or selling books on campus. In their telling, her ideas “are not merely ‘controversial,’ they are dangerous.”) whose opinions they don't agree with, including others in the movement.
1.1.1.1. Pro: [Trans-Exclusionary Radical Feminists](https://www.vox.com/identities/2019/9/5/20840101/terfs-radical-feminists-gender-critical) \(TERFs\) limit discussion by gatekeeping feminist spaces, excluding trans and non-binary people.
1.1.1.1.1. Con: TERFs are a [minority](https://www.theatlantic.com/technology/archive/2020/12/reddit-ovarit-the-donald/617320/)(TERFs constitute “a minority of a minority of feminists,” says Grace Lavery, a UC Berkeley literature professor and writer. Nevertheless, this tiny group has attracted a disproportionate amount of attention in the past several years, in large part thanks to social-media platforms. Anti-trans feminists have a presence in many mainstream online spaces, including Twitter, “radfem” Tumblr, the Black women’s beauty forum Lipstick Alley, and the British parenting forum Mumsnet.) [actively decried](https://www.them.us/story/lesbians-join-the-fight-against-terfs) by many more progressive and younger feminist factions. Silencing within feminist movements is multidirectional and should not be attributed to a single group.
1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: TERFs often appeal to [right-wing](https://www.theguardian.com/news/2018/jul/26/the-free-speech-panic-censorship-how-the-right-concocted-a-crisis) fears of [identity politics](https://www.theguardian.com/education/2021/may/22/kathleen-stock-taboo-around-gender-identity-chilling-effect-on-academics)(Stock is at pains to say she is not a transphobe, and also that she is sympathetic to the idea that many people feel they are not in the “right” body. What she says she opposes, though, is the institutionalisation of the idea that gender identity is all that matters – that how you identify automatically confers all the entitlements of that sex. And she believes that increasingly in universities and the wider world, that is a view that cannot be challenged.\n\n“There’s a taboo against saying this, but it’s what I believe,” she says. “It’s fair enough if people want to disagree with me, but this is what I think.”), and political correctness gone wrong; when progressives note that TERF views may be damaging \([p. 692](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/pdf/10.1177/0038026120934713)(Charlotte Jones and Jen Slater show how the very spaces that gender\ncritical feminists politicise as safe for cis women become sites of danger for trans and non-binary people. They argue that trans-exclusionary politics and practices do nothing to improve toilet access, put trans people at a greater risk of violence, and contribute to a harmful homogenisation of ‘womanhood’.)\), TERFs assert their status as [victims](https://www.salon.com/2021/10/09/dave-chappelle-terf-transphobia-joyce-carol-oates/) closing off conversation.
1.1.1.1.1.2. Pro: TERF [academics](https://www.theguardian.com/education/2021/nov/03/kathleen-stock-says-she-quit-university-post-over-medieval-ostracism) in the UK have claimed that they were silenced for their "gender critical" beliefs, echoing a previous [trend](https://theconversation.com/four-centuries-after-galileo-was-silenced-uk-students-are-still-curbing-free-speech-54935) of no-platforming transphobic speakers by university student unions.
1.1.1.1.1.3. Con: [TERFs](https://www.vox.com/identities/2019/9/5/20840101/terfs-radical-feminists-gender-critical)(Earlier this year, Lavery decided to step into the debate because, as a tenured professor, she felt like she was one of the few trans academics in a position to push back on the growing anti-trans rhetoric she was seeing around her. After initially dipping her toe into the discourse, she wrote a piece that was critical of Stock. Two gender-critical journalists shared Stock’s response, and that’s when Lavery really started feeling the heat.\n\n“It led to a massive explosion of online harassment, which I just didn’t see coming at all,” she said. “People in the seemingly hundreds started trying to find me and just write insulting things about me. And that escalated to the degree that it was totally out of control. At one point, people were posting the names and contact details and photographs — not only of me but also of my colleagues at UC Berkeley — online.”) have protested, campaigned against, and [doxxed](https://www.csoonline.com/article/3572910/what-is-doxing-weaponizing-personal-information.html)(Doxing \(or doxxing\) is the practice of revealing personal information about someone online without their consent.) other feminists, keeping them silent for fear of reprisal. Such actions, along with their [relative power](https://www.vox.com/identities/2019/12/19/21029874/jk-rowling-transgender-tweet-terf)(Wednesday’s ruling has already been seized upon by the usual anti-trans voices who are propping it up as the latest example of the alleged suppression of free speech. It has become increasingly common for upper-class white people to express anti-trans views.), are likely to do a lot of harm.
1.1.1.1.2. Pro: TERFs have been [physically violent](https://www.transadvocate.com/that-time-terfs-beat-radfems-for-protecting-a-trans-woman-from-assault_n_14382.htm) towards trans women attending lesbian and bisexual visibility conferences and summits; this is a far more serious issue than the [cancelled talks](https://www.theguardian.com/education/2015/oct/23/petition-urges-cardiff-university-to-cancel-germain-greer-lecture) and beliefs they decry as [harming](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2020/sep/30/feminists-anti-trans-idea-sex-gender-oppression) feminism.
1.1.1.1.3. Pro: Though TERFs claim that they are not [trans-exclusionary](https://theconversation.com/why-the-words-we-use-matter-when-describing-anti-trans-activists-130990), they problematically include trans men in their definition of a woman and propagate attitudes that cause [harm](https://theconversation.com/transgender-hate-crimes-are-on-the-rise-even-in-canada-121541).
1.1.1.2. Con: Some feminists advocate for activisms that allow open conversation, frame conflict \(within reason\) as [productive](https://arsenalpulp.com/Books/C/Conflict-Is-Not-Abuse), and push the movement forward.
1.1.1.2.1. Pro: Whilst [historic feminists](http://www.bbc.co.uk/history/historic_figures/stopes_marie_carmichael.shtml) held highly [problematic](https://theconversation.com/marie-stopes-opened-the-uks-first-birth-control-clinic-100-years-ago-she-was-also-a-eugenicist-157182)(She was also a fierce advocate for eugenics. This is the practice or advocacy of controlled selective breeding to improve the “quality” of a population’s genetic composition. She called for the “hopelessly rotten and racially diseased” to be sterilised and was vehemently opposed to interracial marriage. While her more famous publications were relatively benign, the bulk of her writing reveals a woman preoccupied with the “unfit” who was convinced by the powers of birth control to improve the biological quality of Britain’s population.) views, feminism has demonstrated its commitment to evolution and inclusion by [distancing](https://www.theguardian.com/global-development/2020/nov/17/marie-stopes-charity-changes-name-in-break-with-founders-view-on-eugenics)(“We’re absolutely not trying to erase her from history, or what she did,” said Simon Cooke, MSI’s chief executive. “For me, she was an acknowledged family planning pioneer, an extraordinary women who broke down barriers … but we really need to look forward and not back. It’s the right moment for us.”\n\nCooke said the board began seriously discussing a name change in November last year, but that the events of 2020, particularly the Black Lives Matter movement, had propelled change. “The name of the organisation has been a topic of discussion for many years and the events of 2020 have reaffirmed that changing our name now is the right decision,” he said.) itself from these ideologies.
1.1.1.2.2. Con: Some [female figureheads](https://www.forbes.com/sites/maggiemcgrath/2021/10/13/why-call-her-daddy-host-alexandra-cooper-says-groupthink-has-spiraled/?sh=132ec754f5be)(After Forbes invited “Call Her Daddy” host and cofounder Alexandra Cooper to speak at the Forbes Under 30 Summit in Detroit, editors received notes from some of Cooper’s listeners urging a reconsideration. The messaging in Cooper’s podcast, they alleged, is unhealthy for young people; it promotes a toxic hook-up culture and is misogynistic.\n\n“I get that all the time,” Cooper said of this criticism from the Under 30 stage on Tuesday. “The concept, I think, in the beginning of cancel culture was, ‘Let's have it be accountability culture.’ I think unfortunately what’s happened is the concept of groupthink has spiraled, and so you have people who don’t have a large platform \[trying\] to take down people who have large platforms. I think they enjoy it, unfortunately.”) are targeted by a limiting groupthink that attempts to cancel them prior to any direct conflict or dialogue. This indicates that on balance, feminists may not push for open conversation.
1.1.1.3. Con: Some intolerance is [necessary](https://www.openculture.com/2019/03/does-democracy-demand-the-tolerance-of-the-intolerant-karl-poppers-paradox.html)(Unlimited tolerance must lead to the disappearance of tolerance. If we extend unlimited tolerance even to those who are intolerant, if we are not prepared to defend a tolerant society against the onslaught of the intolerant, then the tolerant will be destroyed, and tolerance with them.) in order to create a tolerant society; a group that sets no hard boundaries is likely to find itself undermined. As such, it is legitimate for feminists to occasionally deplatform others.
1.1.1.3.1. Pro: If feminists did not deplatform others, many women would be silenced. The boundaries feminists set are protective and ultimately facilitate better conversations.
1.1.1.3.2. Pro: Deplatforming serves as a [necessary](https://www.americanbar.org/groups/crsj/publications/human_rights_magazine_home/the-ongoing-challenge-to-define-free-speech/counterspeech-in-response-to-free-speech/)(In short, the Court’s foregoing decisions reflect its changing notions of free speech, which have expanded protection for both the messages that speech conveys and the media by which the speech is transmitted. In these lines of cases, the Court has consistently held that the constitutionally permissible response to speech conveying controversial, disfavored views is “counterspeech,” not censorship—more speech, not silence. And here is where some “changing notions of free speech in our society” can clearly be discerned: in the increasingly vigorous and widespread counterspeech that is being undertaken by so many members of our society. In recent years, we have witnessed a remarkable and bipartisan outpouring of speech and peaceful dem­onstrations that have denounced hateful ideologies while celebrating our nation’s renewed commitments to equality, inclusivity, and intergroup harmony.) means of curtailing dangerous speech outside of the use of state powers; it is the only middle ground that protects both individuals and civil liberties.
1.1.1.3.3. Con: The line between what is tolerable and what isn't may be incredibly difficult to discern, especially within an activist space that aims to consistently [evolve](https://harvardpolitics.com/evolution-feminism/) in its approach. As such, deplatforming should not be allowed.
1.1.1.3.4. Con: It is hypocritical for ostensibly open spaces to refuse entry to some based on their [political views](https://eu.usatoday.com/story/news/2018/03/06/can-you-conservative-feminist-experts-weigh/374061002/); such actions may have a greater chilling effect than any dissent that could otherwise occur.
1.1.1.4. Pro: [Pro-life women](http://www.slate.com/blogs/xx_factor/2017/01/17/pro_life_feminist_group_new_wave_feminists_removed_from_women_s_march_partnership.html) often find themselves excluded from mainstream feminist movements.
1.1.1.4.1. Con: Feminists [fight](https://www.calvertjournal.com/features/show/12847/first-feminist-activists-poland)(While Orzeszkowa would probably recognise many of the struggles facing Polish women today, she would also recognise such solidarity. In fact, for Polish women alive around the time of Orzeszkowa’s novel, the fight for women’s rights was equally active. Several influential early Polish feminists campaigned for women’s education, the right to vote, access to abortion, and supported sexual minorities long before these issues were widely known or accepted in society. And as a result, they had a significant and pioneering impact on Polish life and culture at the time.) for bodily autonomy; it is not in-fighting when one party acts directly counter to one of the major propositions of feminism.
1.1.1.4.1.1. Con: Feminism should be about the [empowerment](https://eu.usatoday.com/story/opinion/2018/09/05/pro-life-women-abortion-feminism-human-rights-supreme-court-column/1122263002/)(Young anti-abortion women today also push back on the idea that abortion is feminist. “There is nothing empowering about killing a child,” Allie Beth Stuckey, 27, told me. Stuckey, a conservative Christian pundit, added: “Too many women have been manipulated into believing the pro-choice movement is for them, when nothing could be further from reality.”\n\nFeminism's goal is women's empowerment and liberation. Why should we sacrifice millions of lives of some of the most vulnerable people in society to achieve these goals? Feminism is supposed to be about women living the lives they choose, not women ending lives.) of all women, not only the power to end the lives of unborn babies.
1.1.1.4.1.2. Pro: It is inherently impossible to be both pro-life and a feminist; a lack of reproductive bodily autonomy [subjugates](https://www.bustle.com/p/why-you-cant-be-pro-life-a-feminist-31056)(You can't be pro-life and a feminist because the pro-life movement inherently advocates for the subjugation of women, and there's no way to get around that fact.\n\nThe Women's March released an official statement regarding New Wave Feminists on Monday, saying that it was sorry for the "error" in including the pro-life group as one of its partners. "The Women's March platform is pro-choice and that has been our stance since day one," the organizers said in a post shared on various social media sites. "We look forward to marching on behalf of individuals who share the view that women deserve the right to make their own reproductive decisions.") women.
1.1.1.4.2. Pro: Pro-life feminist groups were denied partnerships with the Women's March on Washington 2017; several groups were [rejected](https://www.vox.com/identities/2017/1/22/14335292/womens-march-washington-abortion-pro-life-feminists) outright, and another that was initially approved was later [removed](https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2017/01/pro-lifers-womens-march/513104/)(On Monday afternoon, after the publication of this article, the Women’s March organizers removed the New Wave Feminists from their website and list of partners. “The Women’s March’s platform is pro-choice and that has been our stance from day one,” the organizers said in a statement. “The anti-choice organization in question is not a partner of the Women's March on Washington. We apologize for this error.”).
1.1.1.4.2.1. Con: Regardless of the official status or limited participation of pro-life feminist groups, [thousands](https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2017/01/pro-lifers-womens-march/513104/) of pro-life women marched in Washington.
1.1.1.4.3. Pro: Pro-life women frequently find their voices [crowded out](https://www.heritage.org/life/commentary/100-years-after-the-19th-amendment-pro-life-women-are-still-treated-unequal) of discussions regarding abortion and choose to avoid attending marches and similar types of events in protest.
1.1.1.5. Pro: [Sex workers](https://bostonreview.net/articles/me-too-deja-vu/)(The sex wars were not solely focused on pornography, however. Conflicts blazed over sex work, between those who wished to abolish it as sexual slavery \(e.g., Kathleen Barry, Female Sexual Slavery, 1979\), and those who advocated labor organizing to improve working conditions \(Sex Work: Writings by Women in the Sex Industry, 1987\).) are often [excluded](https://www.independent.co.uk/voices/sex-workers-prostitution-amsterdam-feminism-red-light-district-a8863926.html) from feminist spaces.
1.1.1.5.1. Con: Sex workers are more likely to be included in feminist spaces than patriarchal ones.
1.1.1.5.1.1. Con: Most of the countries that have legalized sex work have done so under the [political leadership of men](https://prostitution.procon.org/historical-timeline/#2000-present).
1.1.1.5.1.2. Pro: Evangelical women often simultaneously uphold the [patriarchy](https://www.cbeinternational.org/resource/article/mutuality-blog-magazine/how-american-evangelicalism-has-been-weaponized-against) and weaponise their gender to [harm](https://theconversation.com/evangelical-women-are-shaping-public-attitudes-about-sex-work-89129) sex workers.
1.1.1.5.1.3. Pro: Sex workers are often [presented](https://slutever.com/shaming-sex-work-hooker-with-a-heart-of-gold-pretty-woman/) in reductive and sexist ways in traditional media; feminist media is often more [respectful](https://www.intomore.com/film/lizzie-bordens-working-girls-gave-sex-workers-voice/).
1.1.1.5.2. Pro: Often feminists claim that enacting sex work negative legislature will protect the women working in the industry, despite [persistent refutations](https://www.opendemocracy.net/en/beyond-trafficking-and-slavery/the-false-feminism-of-criminalising-sex-workers-clients/)(So-called feminist arguments around sex work are harder to dismiss than religious fundamentalism, which condemns prostitution, abortion and all sex outside marriage. Some of the women putting forward those arguments have a reputation for speaking out against violence against women. But their exclusion of sex worker voices – and, usually, of trans women – calls that commitment into question. In the UK, feminist MPs in the Labour party like Sarah Champion and Jess Phillips, who are openly contemptuous of any sex worker who doesn’t fit their description of a ‘prostituted woman’, frame their arguments as feminist. And yet they are campaigning to increase the criminalisation of sex work via the criminalisation of clients. Such a development would worsen our situation and directly threaten our lives, as any sex worker-led organisation in the world will tell you. We have no choice but to deal with them.) of this claim \([p. 2](https://www.nswp.org/sites/nswp.org/files/sg_to_challenging_nordic_model_prf03.pdf)(The ‘Nordic Model’ is used to describe the approach – first promoted and implemented in Sweden – of criminalising the purchase of sex under a broader ideological framework that sees all sex work as violence. The Nordic Model aims to eradicate sex work both in the short term, via criminalisation and fines for buying sex, and in the long term, by creating an understanding of sex work as inherently harmful to both the individual and society. Under this framework all sex workers are viewed as victims lacking agency, and sex work is seen as something that is impossible to choose or to consent to. \(pg.2\))\).
1.1.1.5.3. Con: The feminist left is quite divided over sex work; some feminists find it acceptable, others [question](https://www.theatlantic.com/notes/2016/02/the-divide-over-prostitution-on-the-feminist-left/471168/) whether the women working in the industry have much of a choice.
1.1.2. Pro: Feminism adds a new perspective to conventional views on social and political issues.
1.1.2.1. Con: New perspectives are not necessarily good perspectives.
1.1.2.1.1. Pro: Innovation through new perspectives can be [reckless](https://m.economictimes.com/tech/ites/reckless-innovation-bigger-threat-to-tech-companies-than-rules/articleshow/68105010.cms) and [short-sighted](https://www.sparkts.net/post/can-you-inspire-innovation)(Because sometimes you have to sacrifice short-term goals to achieve long-term ones. Sometimes you have small failures on the road to success. And when those small failures or steps backward occur, that is okay because the important thing is the overall progress forwards towards something bigger.), driving people towards negative long-term outcomes. As such, new views should be approached with skepticism.
1.1.2.1.2. Pro: Traditions can be incredibly [comforting](https://www.bustle.com/articles/131377-why-we-love-traditions-according-to-science), offering a refuge in troubled times. When these are disrupted by new ideologies, people may feel more vulnerable.
1.1.2.1.3. Con: [Certain traditions](https://economictimes.indiatimes.com/news/politics-and-nation/traditions-are-not-bad-but-they-need-to-evolve-constantly/articleshow/56838173.cms) - maintained as part of the status quo - are jarring and can make people feel as uncomfortable as changes to society.
1.1.2.1.4. Con: Existing perspectives often exist due to [path dependency](https://www.investopedia.com/terms/p/path-dependency.asp)(Path dependency explains the continued use of a product or practice based on historical preference or use. A company may persist in the use of a product or practice even if newer, more efficient alternatives are available. Path dependency occurs because it is often easier or more cost-effective to continue along an already set path than to create an entirely new one.) and enshrine oppressive action by removing people's ability to push back; when new movements disrupt this, whilst initially causing unrest, the world is better overall.
1.1.2.2. Con: [Liberalism](https://users.drew.edu/~jlenz/br-liberalism-and-suffrage.html) predicates equality under the law, and has done so [outside](https://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/2021/09/francois-poulain-radical-feminism/619499/) of direct feminist influence.
1.1.2.2.1. Pro: Unlike liberalism, feminism focuses on a specific group. This switches the terms of the argument from universal to group-based recognition which, in the long run, may work against equality.
1.1.2.2.2. Con: The tenets of liberalism do not directly support women's emancipation such that it has been possible for liberal thinkers to [oppose](https://www.opendemocracy.net/en/liberalism-is-no-friend-of-gender-equality/) gender based equality.
1.1.2.3. Pro: Feminists offer cultural critiques on art, movies, television, and other cultural phenomena, helping us better understand them \([p. 180](https://www.lkouniv.ac.in/site/writereaddata/siteContent/202004150927005180nishi_showalter_fem_crit_wilderness.pdf)(Since then, the expressed goals have not been notably unified. Black critics protest the "massive silence" of feminist criticism about black and Third-World women writers and call for a black feminist aesthetic that would deal with both racial and sexual politics. Marxist feminists wish to focus on class along with gender as a crucial determinant of literary production. Literary historians want to uncover\na lost tradition. Critics trained in deconstructionist methodologies wish to "synthesize a literary criticism that is both textual and feminist." Freudian and Lacanian critics want to theorize about women's relationship to language and signification.)\).
1.1.2.3.1. Pro: Most celebrated works of art or literature prior to feminist criticism normalised patriarchal and androcentric standards \([p. 25](http://www.davidpublisher.com/Public/uploads/Contribute/567a405728df6.pdf)(The outlook of sexual difference at the genesis of feminist literary criticism moves from an appraisal of patriarchalism and androcentrism within some of the most revered male authors of the literary canon, to the profiling of a specific difference within a literary work created by women. But difference in feminism, which generates a theory of sexual difference, will appear above all in France and will make real inroads by the end of the 1970s.)\). Feminist writings offered the other side of the story.
1.1.2.3.2. Pro: Cynthia Enloe added a [feminist perspective](https://www.clarku.edu/departments/womens-and-gender-studies/people/professor-cynthia-enloe/) to international relations theory when she focused on the role of military bases, diplomats' wives, and backlashes to nationalism.
1.1.2.3.3. Pro: The [Venus of Willendorf](https://www.discovermagazine.com/planet-earth/what-did-the-venus-of-willendorf-originally-represent)(While male anthropologists of the past two centuries may have assumed these figures were made by men looking at women, McCoid says the shape of many of the figurines suggests they were likely self-portraits of the women that carved them. Given that mirrors hadn’t been invented yet, a woman carving her own shape would be looking down at her own body, resulting in the perspective of exaggerated breasts and bellies and narrower lower legs.\n...\nArchaeologists have only turned up a small number of statuettes that survived, and it's possible that greater numbers once existed and were used by women to depict the various stages of pregnancy and childbirth.) was originally assumed to be a fertility figure, meant to inspire men, until a woman noted that it was more likely to be a self-portrait.
1.1.2.3.4. Con: There are few feminist texts in school curricula, which denotes the lack of an ability to enact widespread understanding and change within society \([p. 110](https://www.jstor.org/stable/40003444)\).
1.1.2.3.4.1. Pro: Nearly [one-quarter](https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2021/09/21/who-doesnt-read-books-in-america/) of adults in the US did not read a book in 2020 and nearly [one-third](https://readingagency.org.uk/about/impact/002-reading-facts-1/) of adults in the UK do not read in their free time; if a feminist text is not part of required reading in the classroom, it is unlikely that it would ever be read.
1.1.2.3.4.2. Con: As reading is often [segregated](https://www.huffpost.com/archive/au/entry/men-and-women-dont-read-from-the-same-page-on-books_a_21652348) along gendered lines, male curriculum writers may be biased away from feminist texts. This does not mean that such perspectives are not valuable.
1.1.2.3.5. Con: Given the [unscientific](https://www.theatlantic.com/ideas/archive/2018/10/new-sokal-hoax/572212/)(Over the past 12 months, three scholars—James Lindsay, Helen Pluckrose, and Peter Boghossian—wrote 20 fake papers using fashionable jargon to argue for ridiculous conclusions, and tried to get them placed in high-profile journals in fields including gender studies, queer studies, and fat studies. Their success rate was remarkable: By the time they took their experiment public late on Tuesday, seven of their articles had been accepted for publication by ostensibly serious peer-reviewed journals. Seven more were still going through various stages of the review process. Only six had been rejected.) nature of feminist thought, regardless of the critiques offered, people may be skeptical when engaging with them.
1.1.2.4. Pro: Feminists have consistently been involved with campaigns for [healthier eating habits](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/226342486_Carol_J_Adams_The_Sexual_Politics_of_Meat_A_Feminist-Vegetarian_Critical_Theory_Tenth_Anniversary_Edition_Kathryn_Paxton_George_Animal_Vegetable_or_Woman_A_Feminist_Critique_of_Ethical_Vegetarianism_M)(Consequently, The Sexual Politics of Meat provides powerful arguments to suggest a convergence of interest between feminism and ethical vegetarianism. And it provides an overdue voice for the unheard concerns of feminist vegetarians about the contradiction between campaigning against one set of injustices while participating in another.), and have worked to reduce the desire to eat meat with every meal.
1.1.2.4.1. Pro: By pushing back against the overconsumption of meat, feminists have helped save countless people from [coronary artery disease](https://www.ox.ac.uk/news/2021-07-21-red-and-processed-meat-linked-increased-risk-heart-disease-oxford-study-shows) and other diseases.
1.1.2.4.2. Pro: A number of feminist icons began the fight for [animal rights and veganism](https://www.vegfest.co.uk/2019/09/01/women-pioneers-movement-rarely-shadows/) in the early 20th century.
1.1.2.4.3. Con: Campaigns for vegetarianism and veganism can often be [colonial](https://civileats.com/2020/08/26/is-the-vegan-movement-ready-to-reckon-with-racism/) and [ignore](https://www.mcgilldaily.com/2017/11/decolonizing-veganism/) sustainable indigenous food production practices in favour of a monolithic perspective on food. Feminist involvement therefore may not be positive.
1.1.2.5. Pro: [Feminism](https://www.bbc.com/worklife/article/20210818-what-does-sex-positivity-mean)(For some, like writer and producer Karley Sciortino, understanding sex positivity grew out of learning about feminism after someone called her London-based sex blog, Slutever, “feminist” in the early 2000s. She got interested in the writings of Camille Paglia, a “pro-sex feminist” who didn’t discriminate against sex workers, porn and women who wore make-up. To Paglia and Sciortino, sex and looking sexy represented power “instead of submission to the male gaze”, says Sciortino. In other words, Sciortino’s idea of sex positivity was about inclusion of sex workers and women who wore their sexuality on their sleeves, categories that have historically been discriminated against in feminist circles.) has helped women to express their [sexuality](https://www.healthline.com/health/healthy-sex/sex-positive-meaning) more openly and deconstruct the taboos encompassing nudity, sensuality, romance, and connectedness.
1.1.2.5.1. Pro: The modern [resurgence of burlesque](https://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/theatre-dance/features/life-cabaret-how-burlesque-went-seedy-sensational-9664407.html)(Some say it’s because burlesque, unlike stripping, is a feminist statement, with the performers very much in control of their bodies and their audience.) uses feminism to empower women, encouraging them to reclaim objectification and take control of their bodies and their audience's attitudes towards it.
1.1.2.5.2. Pro: Some feminists have readily [embraced](https://www.nytimes.com/2018/02/16/opinion/sunday/feminist-pursuit-good-sex.html)(These women were absolutely pro-sex, pro-pleasure and pro-freedom. “We’ve got to learn to sleep with people because we want them,” one woman said in a consciousness-raising session transcribed by the author of “The Dialectic of Sex,” Shulamith Firestone, in 1968. “Not to prove anything to them, not to make them feel better about their masculinity, not out of weakness or inability to say no, but simply because we want to.”\n\nBut they also understood that if rape and harassment were political, so was bad sex. In a 1980 essay, the radical feminist Alix Kates Shulman remembered that in those early sessions, “sex was a central and explosive subject to which we continually returned”; feminists “used their sexual discontents to help them understand the power relations between men and women.”) the topic of sex, evaluating how it is discursively mediated. This opens space to discuss all forms of sex and create more [just systems of desire](https://www.thenation.com/article/culture/amia-srinivasan-interview/)(A recognition that who is, and is not, considered sexually or romantically desirable is shaped in part by systems of oppression—heteronormativity, racism, ableism, and so on. There are lots of examples of this: the romantic and sexual marginalization of certain women of color, the sexual fetishization of East Asian women, the racial discrimination that South Asian and East Asian and femme gay men often face from other gay men. These are all examples of what a political philosopher would call the maldistribution of sexual desire. The goal shouldn’t be to make sure there’s a hierarchy of desirability that doesn’t cut across racial lines; we should just stop thinking of sex as having a hierarchy at all. It shouldn’t be thought of as a good that confers status, but as an activity that we do with other people.).
1.1.2.5.3. Con: Not all feminists have liberatory views of sex; historically, [radical anti-sex work feminists](https://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/1992/11/feminists-against-the-first-amendment/305051/)(Of course. while feminists blamed patriarchy for pornography, moral majoritarians blamed feminism and other humanist rebellions. The alliance between feminists and the far right was not ideological but political. In 1984 antiporn legislation devised by Andrea Dworkin and Catharine MacKinnon, defining pornography as a violation of women's civil rights, was introduced in the Indianapolis city council by an anti-ERA activist, passed with the support of the right, and signed into law by the Republican mayor, William Hudnut.) have paired with conservative politicians to censor pornography and limit conversations on its role in society.
1.1.2.5.3.1. Pro: Many feminists treat female [submissives](https://slate.com/human-interest/2012/04/masochism-and-feminism-is-submissive-sex-bad-for-equality.html) \(a.k.a. femsubs\) as [traitors to their cause](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2012/nov/16/twilight-not-feminist-sado-masochism).
1.1.2.5.3.1.1. Con: Female [submissiveness](https://www.cbr.com/what-happened-to-anime-catgirls/)(Besides translating to "cat", neko can also be a Japanese slang term for "submissive/bottom," which offers the assumption that catgirls exist for sex appeal and are linked to the BDSM community. Like any other domesticated animal, cats are obedient, loving and compliant. On opposite ends of the spectrum, there are the more vulnerable, submissive catgirls, and there are the top-heavy, dominatrix catwomen, although the former is more heavily represented in the media.) is often connected to troubling orientalising tropes that can have [real world harms](https://www.vox.com/22338807/asian-fetish-racism-atlanta-shooting). It is useful for a political movement to push back against this.
1.1.2.5.3.1.2. Pro: Submissive behaviour can be incredibly empowering; practitioners of [shibari](https://www.shape.com/lifestyle/sex-and-love/shibari-japanese-rope-bondage) [often](https://www.womenshealthmag.com/sex-and-love/a32146151/shibari-japanese-rope-bondage/) find it [therapeutic](https://www.vice.com/en/article/9kx9y5/i-tried-rope-bondage-as-a-coping-mechanism-for-my-anxiety). When feminists stigmatise sex on the grounds of politics, they often ignore considerable nuance.
1.1.2.5.3.1.3. Con: Few feminists seek to directly target practitioners, instead they critique the [increased](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/technology-56640178) normalisation of [BDSM](https://feminisminindia.com/2021/01/04/we-need-to-talk-about-normalisation-bdsm/). This activism amplifies complaints from [young people](https://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/2021/10/feminism-sex-clark-flory-srinivasan-angel/619822/)(Does porn silence women, making it harder for them to protest against unwanted sex, and harder for men to hear those protests? Yes, they said. Does porn bear responsibility for the objectification of women, for the marginalization of women, for sexual violence against women? Yes, they said, yes to all of it.) who often feel coerced into violent sex acts.
1.1.2.5.3.2. Con: Attempts to limit sex-positive feminist movements have largely [failed](https://law.jrank.org/pages/9281/Pornography-FEMINIST-PERSPECTIVES-ON-PORNOGRAPHY.html)(In the language of the proposed ordinance, subordination included images of women who "experience sexual pleasure in being raped" or in being "penetrated by objects or animals." Two provisions outlined the conditions under which a woman could bring suit: a plaintiff would have to prove that a pornographic work had harmed her in a specific way, or that it had harmed women in general. The hearings before the Minneapolis City Council galvanized debate and demonstrations. In one incident, a woman protesting pornography and its degrading aspects toward women, set herself on fire by a downtown news-stand.\n...\nThey filed a legal brief attacking the ordinance on the ground that it reinforced sexist stereotypes. In a strongly worded rebuttal, MacKinnon denounced the group as being apologists for male supremacists.\n\nThe Minneapolis antipornography ordinance twice failed to pass.).
1.1.2.5.4. Con: Many anti-abortion feminists continue to construct and reinforce [taboos](https://www.americamagazine.org/faith/2015/01/07/feminist-case-against-abortion-pro-life-roots-womens-movement) regarding impurity and sexual promiscuity.
1.1.2.5.4.1. Pro: One of the most famous American feminists, Susan B. Anthony, likened the [severity](https://www.thelily.com/was-susan-b-anthony-antiabortion-two-sides-are-dueling-over-the-answer-and-the-definition-of-feminism/)(The strongest evidence that Anthony was personally opposed to abortion, Foster said, can be found in writings that scholars widely agree were penned \(and signed\) by Anthony herself. In a speech on “social purity,” delivered in 1895, Anthony includes abortion in a list of societal ills, along with “wife murders” and “infanticides.” She also referenced abortion in an 1876 diary entry about her sister-in-law, who aborted a pregnancy at home and was bedridden for days afterward.\n\n“She will rue the day she forces nature,” Anthony writes.) of abortion to the murder of wives and infant children.
1.1.3. Pro: Feminism creates a space for women's views, concerns, and issues to be heard in what has traditionally been - and continues to be - a political environment very much [dominated by men](https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s12119-020-09810-9)(Nevertheless, women continue to be underrepresented in leadership positions, and this major issue needs to be tackled.).
1.1.3.1. Con: While the public face of politics may appear to be male-heavy, many platforms exist within the socio-political system that allow women's issues to be raised or tabled.
1.1.3.1.1. Pro: Women have the freedom of speech and many use it to make their voices heard through various forms of [media](https://www.mckinsey.com/industries/technology-media-and-telecommunications/our-insights/shattering-the-glass-screen)(There are a significant number of women in the media and entertainment industry compared with our overall benchmark for women’s representation in corporate America. Women make up 49 percent of the total workforce in media and entertainment, although most of these women are concentrated in entry-level positions \(Exhibit 1\).), [publishing](https://www.theguardian.com/books/2016/jan/27/us-study-finds-publishing-is-overwhelmingly-white-and-female)(Survey of workforce at 34 book publishers and eight review journals in US reveals 79% of staff are white and 78% female – with UK numbers still unmonitored), and [social media platforms](https://connectamericas.com/content/women-are-driving-social-media-revolution)(Women are more active on social media; they use it more and participate more than men. This is why it is believed that they will mark trends from now on, since they have typically adapted more and better to the technology.).
1.1.3.1.1.1. Con: Women experience sexism through [gendered censorship](https://reliefweb.int/report/world/populists-using-covid-19-pretext-clamp-down-rights-migrants-silence-women-s-free), meaning that they struggle to defend their rights. Feminism is necessary to fight this and reduce the potential for further oppressive action.
1.1.3.1.1.2. Con: Sexist harassment online may have a chilling effect on women's speech as it is both [rampant](https://www.pewresearch.org/internet/2021/01/13/the-state-of-online-harassment/)(While men are somewhat more likely than women to experience harassment online, women are more likely to be upset about it and think it is a major problem. Some 61% of women say online harassment is a major problem, while 48% of men agree. In addition, women who have been harassed online are more than twice as likely as men to say they were extremely or very upset by their most recent encounter \(34% vs. 14%\). Conversely, 61% of men who have been harassed online say they were not at all or a little upset by their most recent incident, while 36% of women said the same. Overall, 24% of those who have experienced online harassment say that their most recent incident was extremely \(10%\) or very \(14%\) upsetting.), and a [threat](https://www.theguardian.com/society/2020/oct/05/online-violence-against-women-flourishing-and-most-common-on-facebook-survey-finds) to their safety.
1.1.3.1.1.3. Pro: [Academic journals](https://www.brown.edu/campus-life/support/lgbtq/gender-sexuality-and-feminist-studies-journals), like [the Feminist Review](https://journals.sagepub.com/home/fer), promote feminist perspectives and ensure they are heard in academia.
1.1.3.1.1.4. Pro: Women often make ample use of social media platforms to share information relevant to them, including [political campaigns](https://www.voicesofyouth.org/blog/how-social-media-changing-story-womens-voices).
1.1.3.1.1.5. Con: Those who use social media for activism are already [likely](https://blogs.lse.ac.uk/usappblog/2020/07/13/using-digital-media-reinforces-inequalities-in-political-participation/)(In contrast to the common assumption that digital media use mobilizes new people to participate in political activity, our findings show stronger support for the opposite causal direction: that digital media use reinforces existing inequalities in patterns of participation; those who use social and digital media for political activity are already more likely to be doing this outside of the digital sphere.) to be politically engaged, so the platform [privileges](https://blogs.lse.ac.uk/europpblog/2019/10/25/are-men-really-more-interested-in-politics-than-women-or-are-we-just-asking-the-wrong-questions/) men who are already accepted by political systems and often appealed to as voters. As such, social media does not meaningfully expand speech for women.
1.1.3.1.2. Pro: There are many women's [organizations](https://seramount.com/articles/womens-organizations-you-need-to-know/) that operate under the banner of feminism, and also independent of feminism.
1.1.3.1.3. Con: [In many places](https://aceproject.org/ace-en/topics/ge/ge1/ge13)(Throughout the electoral cycle, women can face numerous barriers to their effective participation and the fulfillment of their electoral rights. Although this is not an exhaustive list, some of the obstacles that women in different capacities may encounter during the electoral process can be found below:...\n- Traditional gender roles, gender-based stereotypes and discriminatory attitudes and norms.\n- Lack of ID and documentation required for voter registration, registration centers that are not accessible, near or open in adequate time and lack of information and awareness about voter registration procedures.\n- Lack of information and awareness about voting, electoral processes, and overall political rights. \n- Insufficient targeted civic and voter education programs, or lack of access to existing ones.), women still face systemic and societal [barriers](https://graziadaily.co.uk/life/real-life/countries-where-women-can-t-vote/)(It’s important to understand just how prevalent this is, especially at times like this, where we’re celebrating just how far women have come in the UK. We might be benefiting from what former generations fought for, but there is still a fight to be had. Just take a look at these countries where it’s still really difficult for women to vote) to voting.
1.1.3.1.3.1. Pro: Changes to the [Voting Rights Act of 1965](https://www.archives.gov/legislative/features/voting-rights-1965) have [disenfranchised](https://americanprogress.org/article/100-years-19th-amendment-fight-womens-suffrage-continues/)(Despite the VRA, voter suppression efforts persist and disproportionately target voters of color, immigrant voters, LGBTQ voters, and disabled voters, and, as a result, many women living at the intersection of any of these identities. Such efforts include, but are not limited to, voter ID laws, inaccessible polling places, voter roll purges, voter intimidation efforts, limited access to early voting, and disinformation campaigns. The persistence of this discrimination is in large part due to the weakening of the VRA, particularly in light of recent events such as the 2013 U.S. Supreme Court decision Shelby County v. Holder—gutting key VRA voter protection provisions—and the lifting of a consent decree on the Republican National Committee in 2017, which voting rights advocates fear may result in more frequent instances of voter intimidation and suppression.) minority women and kept millions from voting in the US.
1.1.3.1.4. Con: Platforms for women's voices often privilege those with the time and money to be politically engaged; amongst poorer women, political engagement is [low](https://www.politico.com/news/2020/02/19/women-predominate-among-chronic-nonvoters-111770)(However, in general, unmarried parents with young kids have an especially difficult time participating in civic life, she added. The “second shift” — taking care of kids after work — cuts into time spent following up on news and eventually voting. Low-income nonvoters face housing and food insecurities too, exacerbated for women because of the gender pay gap.). This means fewer key issues may be heard in these spaces.
1.1.3.1.5. Pro: Even without the platform of feminism, women in most countries may engage politically by [voting](https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2020/10/05/key-facts-about-womens-suffrage-around-the-world-a-century-after-u-s-ratified-19th-amendment/)(In many countries, including the U.S., women often turn out to vote at higher rates than men.), participating in [ballot initiatives](https://ballotpedia.org/Ballot_initiative)(The ballot initiative is a means by which citizens may propose to create, amend, or repeal a state law or constitutional provision through collecting petition signatures from a certain minimum number of registered voters. Successful initiative petition efforts result in the proposal being presented to voters within a state or other local government jurisdiction. Ballot initiatives are also referred to as ballot measures, popular initiatives, voter initiatives, citizen initiatives, and propositions.), [lobbying](https://www.wikihow.com/Become-a-Lobbyist)(While every state has its own specific definition of the term, a lobbyist is usually defined as someone who attempts to influence government decisions on behalf of a person or organization.), supporting campaigns, and running for office.
1.1.3.1.5.1. Con: While legally women retain the right to vote in many places, due to inherent power imbalances, close male friends and relatives can heavily inform or dictate a woman's [political choices](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2018/nov/19/voter-intimidation-republicans-democrats-midterm-elections).
1.1.3.2. Con: It is unlikely that men in politics are wholly free from the influence of women; they probably advocate for the [women in their lives](https://warwick.ac.uk/fac/arts/history/students/modules/hi253/lectures/lecture15/)(Caine ack. \(sic\) JSM’s \[John Stuart Mill's\] importance and commitment to female suffrage but argued that:\n\nJSM ignored women activists, other than his wife and his step-daughter) whose interests they care about.
1.1.3.2.1. Pro: [Frederick Pethick-Lawrence](https://www.parliament.uk/about/living-heritage/transformingsociety/electionsvoting/womenvote/overview/male-sympathisers/), husband of socialist activist [Emmeline](https://www.brooklynmuseum.org/eascfa/dinner_party/heritage_floor/emmeline_pethick_lawrence), avidly supported suffrage and later became an MP in the UK. He is likely to have ensured his wife's perspective was integrated in his politics.

1.1.3.3. Pro: As women gain equal rights, societies become more [peaceful](https://www.inclusivesecurity.org/publication/why-women-inclusive-security-and-peaceful-societies/), making it more likely that the voices of others are considered in politics.
1.1.3.3.1. Pro: Conflicts are 35% more likely to be resolved, and remain peaceful for another 15 years, when there are [women involved](https://www.newsecuritybeat.org/2018/02/women-war-securing-peaceful-future/) in the formal [peace process](https://www.cfr.org/womens-participation-in-peace-processes/).
1.1.3.3.2. Con: As [TERFs](https://www.cosmopolitan.com/uk/love-sex/relationships/a28935330/terf-meaning/)(To put it not-so-simply, terf or TERF stands for 'trans-exclusionary radical feminist'. 1.1.3.4. Pro: Feminism keeps women's rights in popular discourse and at the top of people's minds.
1.1.3.4.1. Features such as feeds, profiles, and groups on social platforms provide global access to organizations that can promote and increase visibility by sharing and networking. 1.1.3.5. Pro: Feminism helps breed recognition and support for under-represented female leaders and ideas.

1.1.3.5.1.2. Con: Female leaders understand the specific problems facing women, from a first-person perspective, in a way that a male leader cannot. The average smartphone – 5.5 inches long – is too big for most women’s hands, and it doesn’t often fit in our pockets. Speech-recognition software is trained on recordings of male voices: Google’s version is 70% more likely to understand men. One woman reported that her car’s voice-command system only listened to her husband, even when he was sitting in the passenger seat. Women are more likely to feel sick while wearing a VR headset. Another study found that fitness monitors underestimate steps during housework by up to 74%, and users complain that they don’t count steps taken while pushing a pram.) women.
1.1.3.5.2. Pro: Female leaders can provide [inspiration](https://www.entrepreneur.com/article/321349) for other women who aspire to positions of influence.
1.1.3.5.3. For instance, female students are more likely to choose a major in STEM \(science, technology, engineering or math\) when they are assigned a female professor instead of a male one.) in a range of roles.
1.1.4. Pro: Since the introduction of the intersectionality framework in the 1990s, feminism has become increasingly [intersectional](https://www.cjr.org/language_corner/intersectionality.php)(“Intersectionality” was coined in 1989 by Kimberlé Crenshaw, a civil rights activist and legal scholar. In a paper for the University of Chicago Legal Forum, Crenshaw wrote that traditional feminist ideas and antiracist policies exclude black women because they face overlapping discrimination unique to them. “Because the intersectional experience is greater than the sum of racism and sexism, any analysis that does not take intersectionality into account cannot sufficiently address the particular manner in which Black women are subordinated,” she wrote in the paper. \(Emphasis added.\)), giving a voice to the oppressed, including minorities and immigrants of [all genders](https://www.unwomen.org/en/news/stories/2020/6/explainer-intersectional-feminism-what-it-means-and-why-it-matters)(“All inequality is not created equal,” she says. An intersectional approach shows the way that people’s social identities can overlap, creating compounding experiences of discrimination.\n\n“We tend to talk about race inequality as separate from inequality based on gender, class, sexuality or immigrant status. What’s often missing is how some people are subject to all of these, and the experience is not just the sum of its parts,” Crenshaw said.\n\nIntersectional feminism centres the voices of those experiencing overlapping, concurrent forms of oppression in order to understand the depths of the inequalities and the relationships among them in any given context.).
1.1.4.1. Pro: Non-Western women have had a [massive role](https://study.soas.ac.uk/diplomacy-gender-equality-non-western-women/) in the feminist movement.
1.1.4.1.1. Pro: A Brazilian woman, [Bertha Lutz](https://www.brooklynmuseum.org/eascfa/dinner_party/heritage_floor/bertha_lutz), was primarily responsible for bringing feminism to the UN.
1.1.4.1.2. Pro: [Kamla Bhasin](https://scroll.in/article/1006483/kamla-bhasin-a-life-woven-with-love-cheer-and-fun-even-in-the-face-of-adversity) broke vast ground in promoting feminism in South Asia and was involved in changes to rape legislature in India.
1.1.4.1.3. Con: Non-Western women have a diminished role on a global scale in that their efforts do not automatically equate to significant progress or any power-sharing agreements in their respective countries \([p. 1](https://www.jstor.org/stable/3346278)\).
1.1.4.1.4. Con: Western feminist movements frequently [position themselves as superior](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/abs/10.1177/1464700120987391)(I show how Western linear chronology positions Western women and previously colonised women in vastly different ways. I argue that if one considers the extent to which the denial of coevalness relies on colonial gender discourses, the erasure of indigenous sexuate knowledges that contradict the colonial gender discourses is not one erasure among many, but one of the key erasures that colonial temporality hinges on. A crucial implication of my analysis is that the process of undoing, deconstructing or dismantling the colonial denial of coevalness is also inherently a feminist project.) to non-Western movements; with a bigger spotlight, their efforts are more internationally recognizable.
1.1.4.2. Pro: The intersection of [feminism and climate justice](https://www.unwomen.org/en/news/stories/2020/1/i-am-generation-equality-majandra-rodriguez-acha-youth-leader-climate-justice) provides benefits for men and women alike, through initiatives to stem the consequences of climate change.
1.1.4.2.1. Con: Feminists do not inspire climate action; rather it has been a scientific [concern](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/science-environment-15874560)(1965 - A US President's Advisory Committee panel warns that the greenhouse effect is a matter of "real concern".) for years, and a [core issue](https://www.pewresearch.org/global/2021/09/14/in-response-to-climate-change-citizens-in-advanced-economies-are-willing-to-alter-how-they-live-and-work/)(A new Pew Research Center survey in 17 advanced economies spanning North America, Europe and the Asia-Pacific region finds widespread concern about the personal impact of global climate change. Most citizens say they are willing to change how they live and work at least some to combat the effects of global warming, but whether their efforts will make an impact is unclear.) for many.
1.1.4.2.1.1. Con: There are entire movements dedicated specifically to [climate feminism](https://www.nrdc.org/stories/what-climate-feminism), demonstrating that feminism can also be a driving force behind climate action.
1.1.4.2.2. Pro: Ugandan women harmed by climate change have organised a [movement](https://www.wired.co.uk/article/eco-feminists-climate-change)(Later, those formative experiences hardened into a resolve to act. Namanya is now the gender and food security officer for Uganda’s National Association of Professional Environmentalists \(NAPE\), a nongovernmental organisation that tackles environmental issues ranging from land-grabbing by extractive industries to ecosystem restoration; Namanya’s role is to investigate the gender dimension in each case. To do so, she’s built up a vast network of women activists, who are fighting to protect natural resources in a bid to also protect their own rights. “The violence that happens to nature equally happens to women,” Namanya says.) to fight for more considerate policy and ensure women are protected.
1.1.4.3. Con: Intersectional feminism [promotes the welfare](https://jewishjournal.com/commentary/columnist/294500/intersectionality-the-new-caste-system/) of non-white, non-heterosexual people over white, heterosexual men and women.
1.1.4.3.1. Con: Intersectionality has only existed for [30 years](https://www.vox.com/the-highlight/2019/5/20/18542843/intersectionality-conservatism-law-race-gender-discrimination). Yet, the welfare of white, heterosexual people has been the standard for the vast majority of human history; those that do not adhere to traditional norms deserve an equitable voice as well.
1.1.4.3.1.1. Pro: The concept of "whiteness" was first used to claim superiority of the "white race" in the 1600s when the British introduced the [concept of racism](https://www.theguardian.com/news/2021/apr/20/the-invention-of-whiteness-long-history-dangerous-idea)(Still, with only slightly exaggerated precision, we can say that one of the most crucial developments in “the discovery of personal whiteness” took place during the second half of the 17th century, on the peripheries of the still-young British empire. What’s more, historians such as Oscar and Mary Handlin, Edmund Morgan and Edward Rugemer have largely confirmed Du Bois’s suspicion that while xenophobia appears to be fairly universal among human groupings, the invention of a white racial identity was motivated from the start by a need to justify the enslavement of Africans. In the words of Eric Williams, a historian who later became the first prime minister of Trinidad and Tobago, “slavery was not born of racism: rather, racism was the consequence of slavery”.) to the Americas during the [trans-Atlantic slave trade](https://ldhi.library.cofc.edu/exhibits/show/africanpassageslowcountryadapt/introductionatlanticworld/trans_atlantic_slave_trade). Prior to that, intersectional thought would not have been necessary.
1.1.4.3.2. Pro: When integrated with activism, intersectionality enables people to centre minoritised communities in conversations, focusing on alleviating [complex combinations](https://www.womankind.org.uk/intersectionality-101-what-is-it-and-why-is-it-important/)(Without an intersectional lens, our efforts to tackle inequalities and injustice towards women are likely to just end up perpetuating systems of inequalities. Feminist writer Zoe Samudzi reminds us that “intersectionality is such a vital framework for understanding systems of power, because ‘woman’ is not a catchall category that alone defines all our relationships to power”. A black woman may experience misogyny and racism, but she will experience misogyny differently from a white woman and racism differently from a black man. The work towards women’s rights must be intersectional – any feminism that purely represents the experiences of white, middle class, able-bodied, heterosexual etc. women will fail to achieve equality for all.) of oppression - though this may [seldom](https://qz.com/quartzy/1265902/why-im-giving-up-on-intersectional-feminism/)(Sadly, the women who are in need of protest, protection, and sisterhood most, black women, are the ones who get it least. Even when a black woman creates a term and a concept to describe just how dangerous it is to be a black woman, white women take it, run with it, build over the fundamentals, and save no room for black women.) occur.
1.1.4.4. Pro: Feminism grew out of the [Civil Rights movement](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/lynn-yeakel/march-on-washington_b_3769211.html); centering Black and brown women in feminist activism from early on.
1.1.4.4.1. Con: Historically, many women of colour found feminist talking points reductive, to the point of establishing parallel movements such as [womanism](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2010/apr/10/white-feminism-black-woman-womanism)(Feminism is the form of women's organisation that is prioritised both in the media and academia, but many black women have turned to womanism in an attempt to counter the ways in which the combined oppressions of race and gender affect our lives. Womanism is not just feminism for women from minorities; it is based in our spirituality, honouring our foremothers and a desire to support both men and women. While womanism at its heart is pro-woman, it is also about understanding the communal value of all people of colour.).
1.1.4.4.2. Con: Black women played an [integral leadership role](https://www.forbes.com/sites/marianneschnall/2020/08/05/its-time-the-truth-be-told-about-black-womens-leadership-in-the-fight-for-the-vote/) in the women's suffrage movement; yet, their contributions are rarely mentioned alongside their white feminist counterparts.
1.1.4.4.3. Pro: [Sojourner Truth](https://www.theatlantic.com/magazine/archive/1863/04/sojourner-truth-the-libyan-sibyl/308775/) preceded the Civil Rights movement and was undoubtedly a [feminist activist](https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/soujourner-truth-birth-death-google-doodle-slavery-womens-rights-lincoln-history-a8757366.html), offering one of the first [arguments](https://www.nps.gov/articles/sojourner-truth.htm)(That man over there says that women need to be helped into carriages, and lifted over ditches, and to have the best place everywhere. Nobody ever helps me into carriages, or over mud-puddles, or gives me any best place! And ain't I a woman? Look at me! Look at my arm! I have ploughed and planted, and gathered into barns, and no man could head me! And ain't I a woman? I could work as much and eat as much as a man - when I could get it - and bear the lash as well! And ain't I a woman? I have borne thirteen children, and seen most all sold off to slavery, and when I cried out with my mother's grief, none but Jesus heard me! And ain't I a woman?) that complicated theories of gender and the treatment of Black women.
1.1.5. Con: The voices and opinions of men, even those attempting to be allies, are often excluded from feminist discussions.
1.1.5.1. Con: Men have [thanked](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/jun/18/the-good-men-inside-the-all-male-group-taking-on-modern-masculinity) feminism for its help and joined the movement.
1.1.5.1.1. Con: A previous leader left the feminist movement to become a [men's rights activist](https://www.motherjones.com/politics/2015/01/warren-farrell-mens-rights-movement-feminism-misogyny-trolls/)(Farrell is widely considered to be the father of the men’s rights movement. In a series of books published since the 1980s, he has made the case that the primary victims of gender-based discrimination are men—casualties of a society that relies on their sacrifices while ignoring their suffering. He blames this phenomenon for a litany of woes, from the plight of blue-collar workers to the state of veterans’ health care and rising suicide rates among young men. Many of today’s men’s rights activists view Farrell’s 1993 book, The Myth of Male Power: Why Men Are the Disposable Sex, as their touchstone, and the online forums where they congregate are steeped in Farrell’s ideas.), eventually viewing women as the true controllers of society. This clearly demonstrates the extent to which feminism is alienating to men.
1.1.5.1.2. Pro: Feminist men and women are able to mutually support one another to create great progress; this is [celebrated](https://www.feminist.com/resources/artspeech/genwom/fathersday.html) through events like [International Men's Day](https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/womens-blog/2013/nov/19/feminist-international-mens-day).
1.1.5.2. Con: Men, even allies, can sometimes make the mistake of fighting sexism on behalf of women, instead of alongside women - it is legitimate for feminists to push back against this \([p. 646](https://xyonline.net/sites/xyonline.net/files/Drury%2C%20Allies%20against%20sexism%202014.pdf)(One important caveat in the study of allies is the balance between men working alongside women to confront sexism versus men working on behalf of women, with the later broaching the territory of paternalistic helping and benevolent sexism. Although seemingly positive on the surface, paternalistic helping can be condescending and threatening to its supposed beneficiaries \(Becker et al., 2011\).)\).
1.1.5.2.1. Pro: Some feminist allied men may follow a paternalistic instinct to protect women, paradoxically reinforcing gender stereotypes and sexism \([p. 2](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC6978718/pdf/fpsyg-10-02988.pdf)(However, paternalistic goals can also lead men to confront sexism. Good et al. \(2016\) found that the duty to protect women may be one of the motives that lead men to confront sexism, thus paradoxically reinforcing the status quo. Understanding the motivational processes underlying male confrontation of sexism is essential for determining when such confrontation may help or hinder gender inequality.)\).
1.1.5.2.2. Con: Male feminists are often [maligned](https://www.gq-magazine.co.uk/article/the-problem-with-fake-male-feminists) and depicted as having [ulterior motives](https://www.thecrimson.com/column/femme-fatale/article/2017/3/23/hu-beware-male-feminist/)(Recently, Saturday Night Live produced a skit called “Girl at a Bar” where a woman sitting alone at a bar is repeatedly approached by self-proclaimed feminist men—“not gross guys trying to hit on you or anything”—who make it clear, through their pussyhats and their feminist T-shirts, that they are not one of those “skeazy guys” at a bar. However, after successfully convincing the woman of their feminist credentials, these men use the opportunity make a sexual advance. And when she gently rebuffs their advances, these men become angry, calling her a “bitch” and complaining that “it’s not fair.”\n\nThis is the “woke misogynist” that Nona Willis Aronowitz wrote about. This is the self-proclaimed feminist man who proudly attends the Women’s March and reads Judith Butler and casually throws around terms like “gender performativity,” but who also harasses, talks over, belittles, and sexually assaults women.) for their political engagement; this limits discourse, and may be done disingenuously.
1.1.5.2.3. Pro: Some men could be considered a "[woke misogynist](https://www.independent.co.uk/voices/sexism-men-woke-misogynists-feminism-male-feminists-what-to-do-a7660841.html)," someone that labels themself a feminist without actually changing any behaviors to support the movement.
1.1.5.3. Pro: Some women have accused men of [colonising](https://www.newsweek.com/why-men-must-be-excluded-feminism-stop-it-becoming-all-about-them-504298) feminism for their own ends, and advocate for their exclusion.
1.1.5.3.1. Pro: Instead of advocating for integrated spaces that enable all entrepreneurs to work together, some feminists have started [women-only](https://www.elle.com/uk/life-and-culture/longform/a35646/women-only-spaces/) businesses and [clubs](https://slate.com/human-interest/2021/12/the-wing-coworking-gelman-men-still-pink.html).
1.1.5.3.2. Con: Those who believe men should be excluded from feminism are in the [minority](https://www.huffpost.com/entry/we-need-to-include-men-in-feminism_b_11983946).
1.1.5.3.3. Con: Men who are encouraged to join feminism and treated as important actors for making change are more likely to report intent to act. This may inspire more long term inclusion and improve feminism \([p. 2](https://www.readcube.com/articles/10.3389/fpsyg.2019.02988)(Subašić et al. \(2018\) similarly found that considering men as agents of change toward gender equality increases men’s collective action intentions, as well as feminist solidarity and the perceived illegitimacy of gender inequality. In addition, researchers recently showed a positive relationship between men’s feminist identification and their willingness to take part in feminist actions)\).
1.1.5.4. Pro: Some men believe that politically correct men and feminists have [excluded](https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2015/nov/19/philip-daviestory-mp-politically-correct-males-pander-to-militant-feminists) them from conversations regarding mental health and well-being.
1.1.5.4.1. Pro: There are [concerns](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/av/uk-politics-59414466) from some men that boys now [lack role-models](https://www.newstatesman.com/society/2021/11/a-female-doctor-who-might-not-be-causing-crime-to-rise-but-the-crisis-in-masculinity-is-very-real) in media, which may drive them to despair and crime. Current feminist trends preclude balanced representation, leaving men by the wayside.
1.1.5.4.2. Con: Outreach for men's mental health happens in a wide variety of [forms](https://www.skysports.com/football/news/11095/12122567/footballs-mental-health-epidemic-big-problem-nobody-is-talking-about), [sites](https://giveusashout.org/latest/seeking-mens-mental-health-support/), or [campaigns](https://www.marketingmag.com.au/hubs-c/boys-do-cry-campaign-channels-the-cure-to-help-overcome-stigma-around-mens-mental-health/), supporting them in a number of ways. This may attract less notice as it is not an incendiary talking point that drives attention.
1.2. Pro: Feminism aims to correct the systemic biases against women and other minorities that are born into historical discrimination.
1.2.1. Pro: [Treatment](https://theconversation.com/gender-bias-in-medicine-and-medical-research-is-still-putting-womens-health-at-risk-156495)(Eight out of ten of the drugs removed from the US market between 1997 and 2000 were withdrawn because of side effects that occurred mainly or exclusively in women. Between 2004 and 2013, US women suffered more than 2 million drug-related adverse events, compared with 1.3 million for men.) and [research](https://www.nature.com/articles/d41586-021-02085-6)(More than one-eighth of the world’s population has a condition that can cause pain, heavy bleeding and reduced fertility, all potential consequences of benign tumours called uterine leiomyomas, or fibroids... Unfortunately, fibroids are just one of many understudied aspects of health in people assigned female at birth. \(This includes cisgender women, transgender men and some non-binary and intersex people; the term ‘women’ in the rest of this editorial refers to cis women.\) Clinical and pre-clinical studies alike tend to focus on men: only one-third of people participating in clinical trials relating to cardiovascular disease are women, and an analysis of neuroscience studies published in six journals in 2014 found that 40% of them used only male animals.) for women's health issues are [not prioritized](https://www.theguardian.com/education/2019/dec/18/women-have-been-woefully-neglected-does-medical-science-have-a-gender-problem)(It wasn’t just the topic of pain that was poorly researched. The lack of evidence was a problem she encountered time and time again, which is no surprise when you look at the research gap: less than 2.5% of publicly funded research is dedicated solely to reproductive health, despite the fact that one in three women in the UK will suffer from a reproductive or gynaecological health problem. There is five times more research into erectile dysfunction, which affects 19% of men, than into premenstrual syndrome, which affects 90% of women.) as highly as those that are universal, or affect solely men.
1.2.1.1. Pro: Men's sexual and reproductive health needs are often [prioritised](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/entry/why-cover-viagra-if-contraceptives-arent-covered_us_5963eceee4b0deab7c646b13) over women's.
1.2.1.1.1. Con: Women, who often have wombs, are [impractical](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4800017/)(At the same time, researchers often thought that women would have the same response as men from drugs in clinical trials. They also viewed women as confounding and more expensive test subjects because of their fluctuating hormone levels. Concerns of potential reproductive adverse effects led to policies and guidelines that considered pregnant women as a “vulnerable population” and, subsequently, excluded these women from research and restricted the ability of women of child-bearing potential to enroll in trials, especially in early stages of research.) to include in medical trials due to variations in their hormones throughout the menstrual cycle, though they are similar on average to men. This is why it appears as though there is a prioritisation of men's illness in research.
1.2.1.1.2. Pro: Medical implants for people with wombs, like the [Dalkon shield](https://blogs.bmj.com/bmjsrh/2019/05/27/medical-devices-and-the-legacy-of-the-dalkon-shield-the-struggle-for-evidence-based-contraception/)(The Dalkon Shield was an intrauterine device which its inventor, Dr Hugh J Davis of Johns Hopkins University, claimed was remarkably effective compared with the competition. His claims appealed to the American government which was concerned about an impending post-war overpopulation crisis and conveniently allowed him to make large amounts of money from Dalkon Corporation.\n\nBut his data was bad. His follow up averaged only four and a half months across 640 women. Over time, reports of high levels of pelvic inflammatory disease began to surface but the company was slow to act. It became clear that both the safety and efficacy of the Dalkon Shield had been overstated beyond the supporting evidence.) and [transvaginal meshes](https://www.bmj.com/content/359/bmj.j5515)(Concern is increasing that use of transvaginal mesh devices to treat stress urinary incontinence and pelvic organ prolapse has exposed women to avoidable harms. Part of the problem may lie with the governance of medical devices, which has enabled new devices to be brought to market with inadequate evidence, and over 100 000 litigation cases are now under way.), are often underresearched and can have incredibly poor health outcomes for those outfitted with them.
1.2.1.1.3. Pro: In order to address recurrent medical failures that perpetuated information asymmetries around women's experiences of the pill, women have [started forums](https://www.wired.co.uk/article/contraceptive-pill-the-lowdown)(Contraception, she realised, could be approached like any other data problem – but what she found online was a mess of uncollated information. She couldn’t even locate a place where all the different brands of pill were listed. Conversations were happening on forums such as Mumsnet and Reddit, confirming that she was far from alone in her struggle to find the right contraceptive, but the threads were often disjointed and confusing...\nIn 2019, she launched The Lowdown, a contraception review platform and online community which now has more than 80,000 users.) and crowdsourced data.
1.2.1.1.4. Con: Men's [infertility](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2018/mar/18/obsession-femaleness-fertility-ignore-male-problem-falling-sperm-counts-research-funding)(The Human Fertilisation and Embryology Authority’s 2014-16 report reveals, among other findings, that male infertility is the most common reason \(37%\) for British couples seeking IVF. Meanwhile, elsewhere, it’s revealed that male infertility is considered such an “unsexy” research area that it’s nigh-on impossible to get funding. While pooled 2017 research found that sperm counts in the US, Europe, Australia and New Zealand had halved in 40 years, and one in 20 young men had a low sperm count, the science of male infertility remains stuck at the 1950s level of counting sperm on laboratory slides.) is often ignored as reproduction is seen to be a woman's duty. This causes distress and hinders care.
1.2.1.1.5. Pro: The market for [sexual enhancement supplements](https://www.bloomberg.com/press-releases/2019-10-21/growth-of-sexual-enhancement-supplements-market-to-be-impacted-by-the-increase-in-risk-factors-leading-to-sexual-problems) for men is exploding, and millions are being spent on the research and development of these products. The same investment is not being made in the sexual and reproductive health market for women.
1.2.1.1.5.1. Con: Most of the male genitalia enhancement-style pills are unique to men, there is no equivalent product for women and no need for research to be conducted in this area.
1.2.1.1.5.2. Pro: Vagismum affects 1 in 500 women, but is [drastically underresearched](https://www.refinery29.com/en-gb/uk-doctors-to-be-educated-about-vaginismus)(This statistic said that on the research database PubMed there were a whopping 1,954 clinical trials studying erectile dysfunction, compared to just 393 exploring female sexual pain. Of those 393, a mere 10 were studying vaginismus.\n...\nGiven that there are 200 times fewer trials exploring it than erectile dysfunction, you might think that it’s not that common or serious a condition. But it’s reported that around one in every 500 women and people with vaginas will experience vaginismus and that it can make penetration near impossible and incredibly painful.) compared to sexual dysfunction in men.
1.2.1.2. Pro: Women are [more likely](https://www.euro.who.int/en/health-topics/health-determinants/gender/activities/gender-and-non-communicable-diseases/gender-and-mental-health)(Gender differences occur particularly in the rates of common mental disorders - depression, anxiety and somatic complaints. 1.2.1.2.1. 1.2.1.2.1.1. Pro: Sensual or sexual stereotypes in advertising have [negative effects](https://wunrn.com/2016/10/sexist-advertisement-in-the-nordic-countries-an-evaluation-of-regulations-implementation-report/)(The stereotypical portrayal of women and men in advertising is a problem for both the individual and society. For the individual, sexist advertising can lead to mental health problems. Advertisements containing beauty ideals and objectification can create distorted body image, increased self-objectification, lower self-confidence and even a reduced initiative and desire to lead. To achieve an equal society, it is crucial that discrimination and images of gender stereotypes are counteracted in the media and advertising.\n...\nNine out of ten female respondents answered that advertising makes them want to change something about themselves, and that ads have made them feel bad about their looks and/or their weight. Half of the girls said that they are affected by it every day or every week. 1.2.1.2.1.1.1. 1.2.1.2.1.1.2. Through the normalization of photo editing, [dysmorphic](https://professionalbeauty.co.uk/site/newsdetails/cases-of-body-dysmorphia-rise-due-to-photo-manipulating-apps-such-as--facetune-and-snapchat) body ideals are often [promoted](https://www.hsph.harvard.edu/news/features/advertisings-toxic-effect-on-eating-and-body-image/).
1.2.1.2.1.1.3. 1.2.1.2.2. Pro: Women are often [dismissed](https://inews.co.uk/opinion/chronic-illness-women-me-fibromyalgia-research-treatment-905879)(Sadly, not much has changed for endometriosis patients since Dee was in her teens.
