1.2.1.2.3. Pro: The increased inclination to believe that women were mentally ill led doctors to prescribe them psychopharmaceuticals at high rates, [increasing](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5675036/)(Findings from the literature and our data suggest women are more likely to use prescription opioids compared to men. There is limited information on gender differences in opioid use risk factors and outcomes and more research in this area is warranted.) drug use in later generations \([p. 241](https://www.med.umich.edu/psych/FACULTY/metzl/07_Metzl.pdf)(Health columns such as Henry Safford’s regular ‘Tell me Doctor’ section in Ladies’ Home Journal and Walter Alvarez’s ‘Ask the Doctor’ in Cosmopolitan explained how, thanks to psychopharmacology, ‘emotional’ problems could be cured simply by visiting a doctor, obtaining a prescription and taking a pill. Invariably, these problems ranged from a woman’s frigidity, to a bride’s uncertainty, to a wife’s infidelity. The predominance of such conditions suggests how psychopharmaceuticals came of age in a post-war consumer culture intimately concerned with the role of mothers in maintaining\nindividual and communal peace of mind. As a result, the 1950s set precedents connecting women and psychopharmaceuticals that lay the foundation for Mother’s Little Helpers in the decades to come.)\).
1.2.1.2.4. Con: Men are often considered to suffer from [externalised](https://www.livescience.com/15658-mental-illness-women-men-differences.html)(Women are more likely to develop anxiety and mood disorders such as depression, while men's mental health issues are more likely to involve antisocial personality and substance abuse disorders, a new study says.\n\nThat's because women are more likely to internalize their emotions, which can bring on withdrawal, loneliness and depression, whereas men externalize them, becoming aggressive and impulsive, the researchers showed.) mental health issues; yet, such a perspective may encourage men's mental health issues to be [dismissed](https://www.mayoclinic.org/diseases-conditions/depression/in-depth/male-depression/art-20046216)(Depression can affect men and women differently. When depression occurs in men, it may be masked by unhealthy coping behavior. For a number of reasons, male depression often goes undiagnosed and can have devastating consequences when it goes untreated. But male depression usually gets better with treatment.) until they [manifest](https://www.bmihealthcare.co.uk/health-matters/mens-health/men-and-mental-health-a-damaging-stigma)(Some people suffering from mental health problems, such as anxiety and depression, can turn to alcohol as a coping mechanism. However, alcohol can actually increase stress and anxiety. Getting drunk is often an avoidance strategy used instead of confronting the underlying issues, such as what’s causing you to feel stressed. It’s important to know that alcohol is a depressant. This means that it can contribute to feelings of depression over the long term. There is a strong link between depression and alcohol.) stereotypically.
1.2.1.2.5. Con: Men are left out of conversations on mental health and struggle to identify the warning signs of mental illness. Suicide rates are often [higher](https://www.bbc.com/future/article/20190313-why-more-men-kill-themselves-than-women)(But men may be less likely to admit when they feel vulnerable, whether to themselves, friends, or a GP. They also can be more reticent than women to see a doctor. A UK British Medical Journal study found general primary care consultation rates were 32% lower in men than women. \(Consultation rates for depression, assessed by whether patients received antidepressant prescriptions, were 8% lower in men than women\).\n\n"Men seek help for mental health less often,” Harkavy-Friedman says. “It's not that men don't have the same issues as women – but they're a little less likely to know they have whatever stresses or mental health conditions that are putting them at greater risk for suicide.") in men as a result and poor risk communication may be contributing factor.
1.2.1.3. Pro: Women [often](https://www.bbc.com/future/article/20180518-the-inequality-in-how-women-are-treated-for-pain) [experience](https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2018/jun/28/a-decade-after-the-butcher-of-bega-red-flags-continue-to-be-missed) [mistreatment](https://www.who.int/news/item/09-10-2019-new-evidence-shows-significant-mistreatment-of-women-during-childbirth) at the hands of medical practitioners, including having their [privacy](https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2019/apr/26/doctor-suspended-over-remarks-also-shared-patient-x-rays-online) violated.
1.2.1.3.1. Pro: Though responses to women's pain vary in Western medicine - from the view that Black women [do not feel pain](https://www.theguardian.com/science/2021/sep/21/bias-that-blinds-medical-research-treatment-race-gender-dangerous-disparity)(Women of colour are at particular risk for poor treatment. A 2019 analysis of their childbirth experiences found that they frequently encountered condescending, ineffective communication and disrespect from providers; some women felt bullied into having C-sections. Serena Williams’s childbirth story is by now well known: the tennis star has a history of blood clots, but when she recognised the symptoms and asked for immediate scans and treatment, the nurse and the doctor doubted her. Williams finally got what she needed, but ignoring women’s symptoms and distress contributes to higher maternal mortality rates among Black, Alaska Native and Native American women. Indeed, Black women alone in the US are three to four times more likely to die of complications from childbirth than white women.), to assuming that others are [hysterical](https://aeon.co/essays/womens-pain-it-seems-is-hysterical-until-proven-otherwise)(Alternatively, consider the fact that a woman who finds sex painful \(without an underlying physical pathology that makes sex painful\) currently meets the diagnostic criteria for a mental disorder if the pain causes her distress. The definition considers only her pain and the distress it causes her – even if she’s having sex in a world that prioritises men’s sexual pleasure over women’s discomfort, or having sex with a partner who expects rough and aggressive intercourse. If it hurts and that bothers her, she technically meets the criteria for a mental disorder. Women’s pain, it seems, is hysterical until proven otherwise.) - the end result is often [poor care](https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/2017/nov/20/healthcare-gender-bias-women-pain).
1.2.1.3.2. Pro: Various medical phenomena, like the [husband stitch](https://www.healthline.com/health-news/husband-stitch-is-not-just-myth) or [symphisiotomies](https://nursingclio.org/2016/05/31/the-torture-began-symphysiotomy-and-obstetric-violence-in-modern-ireland/)(This worldview complicated the practice of Cesarean sections, which were thought at the time to be tantamount to contraception \(popular medical opinion asserted that a woman could only undergo 3 or 4 C-sections in a lifetime\). In a culture that vehemently opposed any limitation to childbearing capabilities, the Cesarean section was viewed as an unsatisfactory and even untenable option. While most of their peers in Europe and the US had discounted symphysiotomy, then, Irish physicians, particularly in the 1950s, preferred its use in challenging deliveries.), show the scant disregard some doctors and institutions have for people in labour.
1.2.1.3.3. Con: Abuse from medical practitioners is not exclusive to women \([p. 3](https://bmcmededuc.biomedcentral.com/track/pdf/10.1186/s12909-016-0595-3.pdf)(In qualitative studies, both male and female patients emphasized a loss of their human value. Women\nseemed to turn these emotions inwards and felt powerless, ignored, and that they were treated with\ncarelessness and non-empathy, which could be summarized in the core category “nullified” \[22\]. Men perceived a crisis in confidence in the health care system, and felt ignored and frustrated, and these emotions could be summarized in the core category “mentally pinioned” illustrating the men’s inability to act according to their own interests \[23\].)\). Rather, because the medical system is [regulatory by nature](https://criticallegalthinking.com/2017/05/10/michel-foucault-biopolitics-biopower/)(The second, formed somewhat later, focused on the species body, the body imbued with the mechanics of life and serving as the basis of the biological processes: propagation, births and mortality, the level of health, life expectancy and longevity, with all the conditions that can cause these to vary. Their supervision was effected through an entire series of interventions and regulatory controls: a biopolitics of the population.), it influences everyone and particularly harms the "deviant" by stripping them of autonomy \([pp. 23-24](https://journals.uair.arizona.edu/index.php/arizanthro/article/viewFile/18504/18155)(Medicine, through such means as the creation of disease categories, \nacquired the power to define the "normal" and identify the "deviant". The medical profession thus had the authority to create statistical \nmeasures--norms against which all individuals could be judged. Through the process of normalization, power is both "totalizing", because it controls all aspects of life by creating pressure to conform to norms, and \n"individualizing", because those who fall outside the norm are marked as deviant and targeted with disciplinary strategies designed to neutralize their deviance.)\).
1.2.1.4. Con: Despite their shorter life span, men's health is often [underdiscussed](https://www.mobihealthnews.com/blog/invisible-inequality-men-s-health).
1.2.1.4.1. Con: As men [historically](https://link.springer.com/referenceworkentry/10.1007%2F978-1-4614-5583-7_16) were [viewed](https://news.yale.edu/2018/08/14/why-male-our-default-gender) as the default, and women as deviant, feminists must prioritise campaigning for women's [research](https://www.theguardian.com/bunya-productions-the-leadership/2020/sep/30/what-has-default-male-culture-got-to-do-with-the-lack-of-women-in-leadership) needs if they wish to make change.
1.2.1.4.2. Pro: Men are known to avoid seeking help due to issues in medical training and social norms \([p. 1058](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1121551/pdf/1058.pdf)(Men do care about health issues but often find it difficult to expresses their fears\n\nMen tend to attend their general practitioner later in the course of a condition than women and this phenomenon is exacerbated by social class inequalities\n\nUptake of health information and health services can be improved by making them male friendly, anonymous, and more convenient\n\nBetter use should be made of services such as NHS Direct, pharmacists, occupational health, and online advice\n\nThe nature of medical school education and medical training may contribute to potential problems in consultations between male doctors and patients.)\), yet service delivery remains mostly unchanged \([p. 146](https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/pdf/10.1080/10833196.2018.1452562?needAccess=true)(Why men’s health has, as yet, not been addressed by most national governments and international health organisations has not been studied and there are no known published statements from policy-makers which provide any insight. 1.2.1.4.4.3. Pro: Men often engage in [self-surveillance](https://bmchealthservres.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/1472-6963-8-56#Sec5)(The nexus between knowing one's body, recognising that a health problem exists and being able to 'fix' a health problem is complex. 1.2.1.4.5. 1.2.2. Those opinions are listened to and decisions are then made based on those that are deemed the best. It’s important to understand that a meritocracy is not a democracy. There is no “decision by consensus”; not everyone has a vote. This is the key distinction of the meritocracy. While everyone does have a voice, some are listened to more than others.), which is an important aspect of equality that is universally accessible. 1.2.2.1. Pro: [Some](https://ecpr.eu/Events/Event/PaperDetails/33157)(On the surface, quotas are an explicitly feminist policy; they seek to correct the overrepresentation of men in politics and advance the political and symbolic representation of women. For example, the first post-quota national elections in France in 2002 caused a lot of disappointment as women only received 12% of the seats of the French National Assembly, even though the French policy required the nomination of equal proportion of men and women. This was due to the lack of enforcement of the policy: on the national level, only financial penalties applied to non-compliant parties, and many of them chose to pay the fine rather than comply with the quota \(Kittilson, 2005\).) and defeat the point of having a movement for equality.

1.2.2.1.1.1. Pro: [Research](https://womendeliver.org/2018/why-women-in-politics/) indicates that female politicians increase policy-making that emphasises quality of life and reflects the priorities of families, women, and ethnic, and racial minorities.
1.2.2.1.1.1.1. Pro: Nations led by women handled the COVID-19 pandemic [more effectively](https://www.forbes.com/sites/tomaspremuzic/2021/03/07/if-women-are-better-leaders-then-why-are-they-not-in-charge/) than the ones led by men.
1.2.2.1.1.2. Con: All-women shortlists are [undemocratic](https://www.democraticaudit.com/2014/07/14/all-women-shortlists-are-anti-meritocratic-tokenism-at-its-worst/) and do more harm than good.
1.2.2.1.1.2.1. Con: Rwanda has made huge strides toward [gender parity](https://www.theguardian.com/society/2014/jul/01/lessons-rwanda-female-run-institutions-mps) in governance, potentially creating space for long term improvements to their democratic participation \([p. 362](https://academic.oup.com/afraf/article-pdf/107/428/361/33386/adn024.pdf)(Many observers, including journalists, the Rwandan President Paul Kagame, the Minister of Gender and Women in Development, representatives of international NGOs and the United Nations, heralded the representation of women in the Rwandan Parliament as the dawn of a new, more ‘peaceful’, and ‘equitable’ age in Rwandan politics.)\).
1.2.2.1.1.2.2. Pro: In some areas, left-wing voters are more likely to vote for women. By creating all-women short lists, right wing candidates may find that their politicians do not accurately reflect their values \([p. 16](https://www.ippr.org/files/publications/pdf/gender-balance-of-power_May2017.pdf)(Indeed, high local female representation in Germany has been linked to being in an urban area, high female participation in the labour market and support for the left \(Sundström and Stockemer 2015\).)\).
1.2.2.1.1.2.3. Pro: All-women shortlists may [separate](https://www.europarl.europa.eu/workingpapers/femm/w10/4_en.htm)(Criticisms of quotas include:\n\nthe fairness of such mechanisms\n\nwhether it is merely tokenism\n\nthe establishment of a hierarchy between those M.P.s that were elected "on merit" through all stages of the election process, and those female M.P.s that were elected using a reserved seat\n\nif it is sufficient alone to affect female representation or if other specific measures are needed to strengthen it.) politicians elected from the lists and those who are not. This may be used to attack women's merit and legitimacy as policy makers.
1.2.2.1.1.2.4. Con: Party candidate selection processes are typically undemocratic, as parties are free to choose the candidates they want, like any organisation.
1.2.2.1.1.2.5. Con: Democracy is preserved, even with all-women shortlists, as every individual is free to vote for the candidates of their choice at the ballot box.
1.2.2.1.2. Pro: Gender quotas that aim to achieve equality may yield [counterproductive](https://www.economist.com/leaders/2018/02/15/why-board-quotas-are-no-friend-to-women-workers) results.
1.2.2.1.2.1. Pro: Quotas reduce people to numbers, restricting their opportunities and [disregarding their skillsets](https://www.in-mind.org/article/what-are-the-positive-and-negative-side-effects-of-gender-quotas)(One group of participants was informed that the company had implemented a gender quota, while another group was told that candidates were selected based on merit. Although the female candidate had the same qualifications in both conditions, participants thought of her as less competent and effective on the job if the company’s rules for promotion featured a quota. What’s more, her chances to further climb up the career ladder was perceived to be smaller as well. This study exposes a negative side effect of gender quotas, namely that there can be a “stigma of incompetence” attached to women because gender quotas may suggest that merit played a negligible role in the selection process.) and aspirations when it comes to work.
1.2.2.1.2.2. Con: Habitual discrimination against women often goes unremarked upon, and [requires](https://www.gendereconomy.org/the-debate-about-quotas/)(As a whole, these unconscious processes are deeply embedded in individuals and organizational systems, and it is unrealistic to expect that these will disappear without an abrupt external shock. Under the Canadian “comply or explain” approach to board diversity, the primary explanation offered by companies who do not adopt gender targets is that they recruit “based on merit.”14 However, research shows that supposedly meritocratic systems are as susceptible to these biases as other systems \(and perhaps even more\).15 Thus, quotas provide a stringent and structured framework to overcome these unconscious biases such that there is less room for unintended discrimination to emerge.) quotas to call attention to. This is worth any pushback that the policy receives, as more women may join politics in the long term.
1.2.2.1.2.3. Pro: People often perceive quotas for women to be [particularly unfair](https://www.frontiersin.org/articles/10.3389/fpsyg.2020.00700/full)(Students perceived women quotas as counterproductive, derogatory, and unfair, whereas they perceived men quotas as beneficial and fair. Concerns over the negative perceptions of quota beneficiaries were associated more frequently with women quotas than men quotas.) compared to those for men. Therefore, shocks to unconscious biases may not accrue, and negative perceptions of women may persist.
1.2.2.1.2.4. Con: Political quotas can increase the quality of the candidate pool \([p. 23](https://www2.novasbe.unl.pt/Portals/0/KnowledgeCenters/Economics%20for%20Policy/documents/The-Good-the-Bad-and-the-Dierent-Can-Gender-Quotas-Raise-the-Quality-of-Politicians.pdf)(It is immediate that a quota results in an increase in quality for levels slightly above the status\nquo, and remain constant when high-ability, high-signal females entering politics replace high-\nability, high-signal males who are exiting to the private labour market. An increase in hF raises the\nquality of those elected.)\).
1.2.2.1.3. Pro: People may prefer to be acknowledged as individuals instead of being defined by their gender identity.
1.2.2.1.3.1. Pro: Quotas may be essentializing to those wishing to identify themselves simply as an individual \([p. 22](https://www.legislationline.org/download/id/2891/file/Not%20All%20Quotas%20are%20Equal%20-%20study%20on%20use%20of%20quotas.pdf)(Some conservatives oppose quotas because they support strict equality of opportunities, while others defend quotas because they believe that women and men are essentially different. Similarly, some progressives oppose quotas because they fear these essentialize gender differences, while other defend quotas because they favor equality of results.)\).
1.2.2.1.4. Con: There is no feminist consensus on the implementation of quotas, as some fear that they are used to create a more palatable political apparatus without structural change \([p. 348](https://mlkrook.org/pdf/social_politics_2008.pdf)(Many feminists oppose these provisions, however, because they interpret them as an attempt to make electoral gains among female voters, while promoting the selection of “malleable” women who will not challenge the patriar-\nchal status quo \(Goetz and Hassim 2003; Huang 2002; Rai 1999\).)\).
1.2.2.1.5. Pro: Discrimination is never justified.
1.2.2.1.5.1. Pro: People [do not choose](https://cherwell.org/2021/10/09/gender-abolition-why-it-matters/)(Gender is not innate, nor inevitable. Gender is a socially constructed class system in which the class of man benefits from the systematic oppression of the class of woman \(as anti-trans ‘feminists’ have appropriated some of the language of gender abolition, it is important to make clear that this category of women absolutely includes trans women\). While sex refers to physical and biological characteristics, gender is a term to describe behaviours and attitudes assigned to these features. We gender biological sex characteristics just as we gender toys, clothing and colours. There is nothing inherently masculine about the colour blue – yet since we have a concept of gender, we assign cultural significance to that colour.) their identities, and as such should not be held accountable for making social change.
1.2.2.1.5.2. Con: Corrective discrimination is justified, insofar as it rectifies historic harms that arise from an initial act of injustice.
1.2.2.1.5.2.1. Pro: Quotas have helped tens of thousands of Afro-Brazilians attend university in Brazil \([pp. 172-173](https://www.ses.unam.mx/integrantes/uploadfile/mlloyd/Lloyd_ADecadeOffAffirmativeActionInBrazil.pdf)\).
1.2.2.2. Con: Meritocracy is only valuable when everyone competes from an equal starting point; as society finds women less persuasive based on arbitrary characteristics, feminism is necessary \([p. 2698](https://royalsocietypublishing.org/doi/pdf/10.1098/rspb.2012.0311)(Our results show that both men and women select male and female leaders with lower voices. These findings suggest that men and women with lower-pitched voices may be more successful in obtaining positions of leadership. This might also suggest that because women, on average, have higher-pitched voices than men, voice pitch could be a factor that contributes to fewer women holding leadership roles than men. Additionally, while people are free to choose their leaders, these results clearly demonstrate that these choices cannot be understood in isolation from biological influences.)\).
1.2.2.2.1. Pro: Feminists tackle [perception gaps](https://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/women/google-translate-sexist-masculine-feminine-he-said-she-said-english-spanish-languages-a8672586.html)(“Flawed algorithms can amplify biases through feedback loops,” professors James Zou and Londa Schiebinger wrote in a paper titled “AI can be sexist and racist - it’s time to make it fair.” “Each time a translation program defaults to ‘he said,’ it increases the relative frequency of the masculine pronoun on the web - potentially reversing hard-won advances toward equality.”\n\nThe issue occurred when translating to languages where words are gendered as well - with words such as “doctor” changing to masculine and “nurse” changing to feminine.) in AI by noting the ways in which translation apps perpetuate stratification of roles, and [hiring discrimination](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/technology-45809919). This activism facilitates true meritocracy.
1.2.2.2.2. Pro: Women are systemically [excluded](https://hbr.org/2013/09/women-rising-the-unseen-barriers) from positions of power by [norms](https://www.whysocialscience.com/blog/2020/10/20/because-misogyny-is-still-alive-and-well-and-women-still-dont-rule-equally-to-men) which demean ambitious women, create [inhospitable](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-wales-58408550) workplaces, and worsen socio-economic [inequalities](https://www.unwomen.org/en/what-we-do/economic-empowerment/facts-and-figures).
1.2.2.2.3. Con: Not all biases are bad, as men and women are different. This means that differences in perception are legitimate, and feminists are wrong to seek equality.
1.2.2.2.3.1. Con: [Biases](https://fs.blog/confirmation-bias/) are often justified using incorrect or limited recollections of the past, in order to perpetuate ideas of difference. These are illegitimate and must be corrected.
1.2.2.2.3.1.1. Pro: Feminists rectify a perspective gap when they note that a woman is the first to do something, as women are often [written out](https://www.smithsonianmag.com/science-nature/unheralded-women-scientists-finally-getting-their-due-180973082/) of history, or actively discriminated against.
1.2.2.2.3.2. Con: Patriarchal bias may lead people to [rely on history](https://theconversation.com/the-evolutionary-history-of-men-and-women-should-not-prevent-us-from-seeking-gender-equality-88703) to justify sexism. Yet the past needn't define the future of society, particularly if it allows the world to remain unjust.
1.2.2.2.3.3. Pro: There are [physiological and psychological](http://www.acrwebsite.org/search/view-conference-proceedings.aspx?Id=6390) differences between men and women which justify their different positions in society. These biases are not bad, and are illegitimate for feminists to disregard.
1.2.2.2.3.3.1. Con: The alleged differences between men and women are often examined without holistic evaluation of their context \([p. 1](https://www.apa.org/pubs/journals/releases/amp-606581.pdf)(The differences model, which argues that males and fe-\nmales are vastly different psychologically, dominates the\npopular media. Here, the author advances a very different\nview, the gender similarities hypothesis, which holds that\nmales and females are similar on most, but not all, psy-\nchological variables. Results from a review of 46 meta-\nanalyses support the gender similarities hypothesis. Gen-\nder differences can vary substantially in magnitude at\ndifferent ages and depend on the context in which mea-\nsurement occurs. Overinflated claims of gender differences\ncarry substantial costs in areas such as the workplace and\nrelationships.)\). This is reductive and ignores the ways in which society creates differences.
1.2.2.2.3.3.2. Pro: Men and women often have differences in their brain size and structures; by ignoring these [physiological](https://stanmed.stanford.edu/2017spring/how-mens-and-womens-brains-are-different.html)(“These findings have all been replicated,” she says. Women excel in several measures of verbal ability — pretty much all of them, except for verbal analogies. Women’s reading comprehension and writing ability consistently exceed that of men, on average. They out­perform men in tests of fine-motor coordination and perceptual speed. They’re more adept at retrieving information from long-term memory.\n\nMen, on average, can more easily juggle items in working memory. They have superior visuospatial skills: They’re better at visualizing what happens when a complicated two- or three-dimensional shape is rotated in space, at correctly determining angles from the horizontal, at tracking moving objects and at aiming projectiles.) disparities, people may not be usefully nudged to areas where they are more skilled.
1.2.2.2.3.3.3. Pro: Women [are closer](http://www.theregister.co.uk/2010/01/14/chimp_genome_y_chromosome_gumble)(What this means, of course, is that women are in fact much closer genetically to being chimps than men are. Some have even interpreted the research to mean that men are "more evolved" than women, having left their heritage as apes further behind than the ladies.\n\nTechnically speaking this is correct, but Page and his colleagues caution that most of the rapid changes taking place in men haven't involved anything that modern civilisation would necessarily regard as evidence of superiority: the shift from poo-flinging to speech and writing as means of expressing oneself, for instance, is unrelated to the Y chromosome.) in terms of their DNA to chimpanzees than to human men.
1.2.2.2.3.3.3.1. Con: The suggested genetic similarity between women and chimps is discounted by many scientists as only [one gene](https://theconversation.com/differences-between-men-and-women-are-more-than-the-sum-of-their-genes-39490) is involved.
1.2.2.2.3.3.3.2. Con: [Different evaluations](https://geneticliteracyproject.org/2015/07/31/who-has-more-similar-genome-men-and-women-or-males-and-male-chimps/) of the genetic difference between men and women narrow the gap to a 1% divergence.
1.2.2.2.3.3.4. Con: Viewing gender or [sex](https://childrensnational.org/visit/conditions-and-treatments/diabetes-hormonal-disorders/differences-in-sex-development) as a binary [is outdated](https://scopeblog.stanford.edu/2015/02/24/sex-biology-redefined-genes-dont-indicate-binary-sexes/), rendering debates on the dichotomy of men and women unnuanced.
1.2.2.3. Pro: People often [prefer just societies](https://www.theguardian.com/inequality/2017/may/04/science-inequality-why-people-prefer-unequal-societies) to equal ones; when feminists fail to recognise that people work hard and should be rewarded for it, they damage their movement.
1.2.2.3.1. Pro: Equality, [unlike equity](https://www.mentalfloss.com/article/625404/equity-vs-equality-what-is-the-difference)(Equality has to do with giving everyone the exact same resources, whereas equity involves distributing resources based on the needs of the recipients.), implies a lack of recognition of natural or developed differences between individuals. Since this lack of recognition could have negative results, feminists should not seek equality.
1.2.2.3.2. Pro: Feminism may encourage a focus on identity over other efforts - this [undermines](https://femmagazine.com/how-elites-weaponize-identity-politics/)(And yet, that is not how identity politics is being played out in contemporary American politics. Elites of our political sphere weaponize identity politics to, at best, create the veneer of diversity and progressivism with mere promises of incremental change and, at worst, co-opt this political approach to advance even more harmful policies. In doing so, elites strive to minimize the centuries of efforts from Black and Indigenous people to dismantle oppressive structures by offering hollow representations of change, in attempts to appease demands for something more meaningful.) the importance of hard work and positive actions.
1.2.2.3.3. Con: Though feminism may suffer from undermining [meritocracy myths](https://www.theguardian.com/women-in-leadership/2013/jun/24/false-theory-meritocracy-women-lose) in the short term, they make considerably more change in the long term than they would through [acquiescence](https://jezebel.com/the-lie-of-feminist-meritocracy-1835621298)(The feminist meritocracy demands hustle: there are conference calls at 5:30 in the morning, there are working lunches, there are power poses, there are life hacks about making your voice heard in meetings. The framing here is often telling. The cottage industry of self-help for successful working women often points back to other women—there are mentors and girl squads by your side through all of it—but the task itself—the negotiation, the presentation you need to ace, the boss you need to impress—always happens alone. There are millions of dollars in venture capital heavily invested in precisely this model of together-alone women’s “empowerment.”\n\nYou see this acutely in the girl boss imperative to talk about money. Pay transparency is an important part of more equitable workplaces, but can lose its actual power when viewed through the lens of feminist meritocracy.).
1.2.2.3.4. Con: Preferences are malleable and affected by a number of factors. It is reductive to limit just action to preserve current ideals \([p. 20](https://core.ac.uk/download/pdf/161947553.pdf)(It is because her inherent capacity for rational thinking has been molded in long-lasting ways by the policies enacted at time A. To use the language of bounded rationality, a policy choice at time A might have instilled in our citizen particular long-lasting biases that simply would not have existed had that choice not been made. Or she might express certain biases—again, in a “sticky” and long-lasting way—to a greater or lesser degree than she would have otherwise. In some cases, our policy inputs at time A will enhance people’s abilities to act in desired ways at time B. In other cases, they might undermine people’s later ability to respond to laws in the way we expect or want them to.)\).
1.2.3. Con: Feminism has helped minority women [less often](https://www.pewresearch.org/social-trends/2020/07/07/a-century-after-women-gained-the-right-to-vote-majority-of-americans-see-work-to-do-on-gender-equality/)(A majority of Americans say feminism has had a positive impact on the lives of white, Black and Hispanic women. About six-in-ten or more U.S. adults say feminism has helped the lives of white \(64%\), Black \(61%\) and Hispanic \(58%\) women at least a little. But more say feminism helped white women a lot \(32%\) than say it’s done the same for Black \(21%\) or Hispanic \(15%\) women. About a quarter \(24%\) say feminism has helped wealthy women a lot; just 10% say it’s been equally helpful to poor women.) than white women.
1.2.3.1. Pro: White feminists often [leverage](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/full/10.1177/1367549420985852)(The cultural power of mainstream white feminism partly derives from the cultural power of white tears. This in turn depends on the dehumanisation of people of colour, who were constructed in colonial ‘race science’ as incapable of complex feeling \(Schuller, 2018\). Colonialism also created a circuit between bourgeois white women’s tears and white men’s rage, often activated by allegations of rape, which operated in the service of economic extraction and exploitation... Such feminisms exemplify what I call ‘political whiteness’, which centres assertions of victimhood: through these, womanhood \(and personhood\) is claimed to the exclusion of the enemy.) their race to emphasise the importance of their victimhood; this can lead to myopic lobbying with negative effects for others.
1.2.3.1.1. Pro: White women, in places like the US and the UK, [simultaneously](https://blogs.lse.ac.uk/medialse/2020/10/01/how-white-feminists-and-elites-appropriated-slavery-and-still-do/)(In her book Subject to Others, Moira Ferguson analyses texts by British women writers on slavery between 1670 and 1834 and finds that African slaves were represented as an essentialised and homogenised mass where women followed the ‘patriarchally prescribed female roles and idealised self-images: these ranged from abused victim, orphan, and grieving mother, to altruist and loyal “servant”’. Thus, the colonial ‘other’ became even further dehumanised, objectified and fetishised as a weak and marginalised entity always in need of protection and pity from western colonisers.\n\nFerguson argues that these elite western women writers also hesitantly and ambiguously began writing their ‘own assumed powerlessness and inferiority onto their representations of slaves’/ This historical intersection of the anti-slavery movement with the desire to secure self-empowerment was instrumental in white western bourgeois women’s demand for political rights and freedom.) denigrated and homogenised the enslaved whilst co-opting their suffering. When feminists do not confront this practice they may allow it to continue.
1.2.3.1.2. Con: Aligning ineffective forms of feminism with a particular race or social group can [hamper](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2021/sep/26/white-feminists-are-under-attack-from-other-women-here-can-only-be-one-winner--men)(Yet that is exactly what lazy polemics about terrible white feminism do: they empower men to use the fact that all white women are supposedly high up in the privilege pecking order to tell middle-aged women to shut up or, even worse, accuse them of weaponising their abuse and trauma. It doesn’t help women of colour, either: it implicitly posits Asian male crime against women as somehow lesser than white male crime, because Asian men are victims too.) activists looking to expand conversations of harm - playing into the patriarchy's hands.
1.2.3.1.3. Con: [Significant](https://annehelen.substack.com/p/the-trouble-with-white-women)(But The Trouble with White Women is also, as Brittney Cooper explains it in the foreword, illuminating the very real damages, past and present, of white feminism. “For Black women who need white women to admit it, this book will do that,” Cooper writes. “For white women who continually ask me how to get better, I say, begin here.”) [work](https://www.teenvogue.com/story/michaela-coel-book-misfits) is done by [modern activists](https://www.jacobinmag.com/2020/09/feminism-interrupted-review-lola-olufemi)(In this context, Lola Olufemi’s new book is both a timely and stirring intervention. Feminism, Interrupted expresses the radical voices which are coming into feminism from the solidarity work taking place on the ground. It both unravels a silenced history of radicalism — and points toward a truly just future.\n\nThe relationship between feminism and political radicalism is both necessary and complex. Feminism, Olufemi persuasively shows, does not have necessarily radical tendencies — rather, there is a long history of women giving their support to oppressive systems under the guise of “feminism.” Take the white suffragettes who did not see colonial subjects as part of their struggle for a vote \(and even cheered on British imperialist forces\).) to undermine reductive or lazy approaches to feminism; as such, it is erroneous to consider white feminism to be the sole narrative force of the movement.
1.2.3.2. Pro: The [intersectional invisibility](https://www.apa.org/news/press/releases/2020/07/black-women-social-justice)(“Black women are often overlooked in people’s conversations about racism and sexism even though they face a unique combination of both of these forms of discrimination simultaneously,” said lead researcher Stewart Coles, a PhD candidate at the University of Michigan’s Department of Communication and Media. “This ‘intersectional invisibility’ means that movements that are supposed to help Black women may be contributing to their marginalization.”) of Black women has marginalized their existence and excluded them from feminist movements.
1.2.3.2.1. Pro: -> See 1.1.4.4.2.
1.2.3.2.2. Pro: Black women are systematically excluded from [leadership roles](https://www.newyorker.com/news/our-columnists/until-black-women-are-free-none-of-us-will-be-free)(The Combahee River Collective was a small organization, but it involved some of the luminaries of Black feminism: Barbara Smith and her twin sister, Beverly Smith, as well as Demita Frazier, Cheryl Clarke, Akasha Hull, Margo Okazawa-Rey, Chirlane McCray, and Audre Lorde. Equally dismayed by the direction of the feminist movement, which they believed to be dominated by middle-class white women, and the suffocating masculinity in Black-nationalist organizations, they set out to formulate their own politics and strategies in response to their distinct experiences as Black women.) in modern feminist organizations.
1.2.3.2.2.1. Pro: Black women, excluded from leadership roles, are often called on en masse to "[save the day](https://www.forbes.com/sites/marianneschnall/2020/08/17/when-black-women-lead-we-all-win/)(Don't just call on Black women when things are burning and people are like, “Oh my God, we need Black women to save the day.” Well, Black women might not have to be Batman if everybody else handled their own situation and approached the world with more empathy. But Black women happen to be strong and tender at the same time. We are loud and we're still quiet in the moments we need to be. We occupy so many spaces and are expected to move through the world so seamlessly, and we do it with so much grace. So when people were saying, “We need Black women to save us,” it's like, maybe we won’t have to be the saviors if you actually just saw us in our full humanity to begin with.)." Viewing them as an afterthought could have been avoided had they been invited to positions of power from the start.
1.2.3.2.2.2. Con: Black women took the initiative to create their own organizations, creating opportunities to [better advocate](https://www.newyorker.com/news/our-columnists/until-black-women-are-free-none-of-us-will-be-free)(many Black women felt shut out of directing those organizations, just as they felt that their experiences as Black women were ignored.\n\nThey fared no better in organizations led by white women, who, for the most part, could not understand how racism compounded the experiences of Black women, creating a new dimension of oppression. The overwhelming majority of Black women were working-class and were forced to labor both outside and inside their homes. But Black women who tried to utilize public welfare so that they could spend more time caring for their children were demonized as freeloaders, even as white women who chose to work at home were celebrated for prioritizing their families over personal ambition. In the reality of organizing, these tensions manifested themselves in white women’s desire to focus their organizing on abortion rights, while Black feminists argued for the broader framework of reproductive justice) for their rights.
1.2.3.2.2.2.1. Con: Black women were forced to create their own organizations due to a [lack of opportunities](https://qz.com/quartzy/1265902/why-im-giving-up-on-intersectional-feminism/) in the traditional, white-focused ones.
1.2.3.2.2.3. Pro: [BIWOC](https://www.healthline.com/health/bipoc-meaning) \(Black, Indigenous, and Women of Color\) are often excluded from critical comemorative events \([p. 11](https://www.nature.com/articles/s41599-020-00554-3.pdf)(In a “browner” and “flatter” America in 2020, a compartmentalized view on the suffrage centennial and a one-sided approach to its iconic heroes and protagonists further dislink gender and race. As of now, the celebration of the Centennial of Women’s Suffrage bears relevance still largely to a specific group—the WASP and proud women. Then, should women of color, men of color, and all historically underrepresented groups be celebrating the Centennial with the same pride and the same sense of achievement? The split between gender and race remains an open-ended topic for dialog if 2020 promises to be a more integrated society and a more inclusive culture.)\).
1.2.3.2.2.4. Con: [Black women](https://www.aljazeera.com/opinions/2021/3/8/what-is-international-womens-day-for-black-women)(Black women and Black transgender women are now at the forefront of various working-class, feminist, and anti-racist initiatives and movements. Black Lives Matter, a formidable movement founded by three Black women – Patrisse Khan-Cullors, Alicia Garza, and Opal Tometi – has reshaped the conversation about racial justice and equity in the US. Along with Latinx activists, Black women are also leading the effort in the fight for a $15 minimum wage.) in the US currently lead vital progressive movements that, if successful, will help many people.
1.2.3.2.3. Pro: Black feminist organizations are [critically underfunded](https://www.hrfn.org/community-voices/the-dire-state-of-funding-for-black-feminist-movements-and-what-donors-can-do-about-it/)(Funding for Black women, girls, and trans people constitutes roughly 5% of human rights funding, both in dollars and number of grants. \n\nPutting this into context, human rights grants make up 2% to 7% of foundation funding globally. Even at the most broadly defined, this means that Black feminist movements receive somewhere between 0.1% and 0.35% of annual grant dollars from foundations.).
1.2.3.2.4. Con: The amount of help provided by feminist movements can only be subjectively evaluated; [some would argue](https://www.thelily.com/black-women-share-what-bell-hooks-taught-them-about-feminism/?) that Black women have been helped by feminism, and not actively harmed.
1.2.3.2.5. Pro: Very little research about Black views on feminism has been [conducted](https://www.tandfonline.com/doi/abs/10.1300/J014v10n03_03?journalCode=wzwp20), actively demonstrating feminist academics' ignorance to the nuanced views of Black women on the subject. This may have hampered their activism.
1.2.3.2.6. Con: No one has been actively excluded from these movements; some women may feel like their contributions and opinions are not being appreciated enough and decide to leave and create their own organizations instead.
1.2.3.3. Pro: [Western feminists](https://blogs.lse.ac.uk/medialse/2021/09/02/afghanistan-and-the-colonial-project-of-feminism-dismantling-the-binary-lens/)(The struggles of the white, heterosexual, elite, western woman have gained currency as the only history of feminism setting itself up as a role model for the rest of the world. Any woman who does not fit this image is deemed oppressed and in need of saving, making her a white man’s burden and the white feminists’ cause célèbre. Hence it is important to deconstruct the normative western feminist notions of gender and bring into focus indigenous understandings of gender from the global south and include it into the larger geo-political feminist epistemology.) often engage in [colonial statecraft](https://www.journals.uchicago.edu/doi/abs/10.1086/655914)(After the events of September 11, 2001, George W. Bush’s administration launched a military and public relations campaign to promote U.S. national interests using the language of feminism and human rights. While these discourses in the United States helped to reinvigorate a declining economy, and specifically a flagging fashion industry \(as Pham addresses in her companion essay\), feminism abroad was deployed to very different ends. This article considers the establishment of the Kabul Beauty School by the nongovernmental organization Beauty without Borders, sponsored in large part by the U.S. fashion and beauty industries. Examining troubling histories of beauty’s relation to morality, humanity, and security, as well as to neoliberal discourses of self‐governance, the author teases out the biopower and biopolitics of beauty, enacted here through programs of empowerment that are inseparable from the geopolitical aims of the U.S. deployment in Afghanistan.) to the active detriment of women in other nations.
1.2.3.3.1. Pro: In France, [Burqa bans](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-13038095)(On 11 April 2011, France became the first European country to ban the full-face Islamic veil in public places.\n\nUnder the ban, no woman, French or foreign, is able to leave their home with their face hidden behind a veil without running the risk of a fine.\n\nAs President, Nicolas Sarkozy, whose administration brought in the ban, said that veils oppress women and were "not welcome" in France.) are often legitimised through appeals to [feminism](https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/womens-blog/2015/jul/20/france-feminism-hijab-ban-muslim-women)(Even before the 2004 law meant scarf-wearing teenagers would be excluded from schools – thus violating their fundamental right to education – France’s established feminist groups did not accept scarf-wearing women in their meetings.\n\nThey decided early on these women could not be feminist, indeed must be against everything that feminism stands for, that the hijab was a symbol of oppression.), despite the fact that they restrict women's choices and perpetuate racism.
1.2.3.3.2. Con: While mainstream forms of feminism may be reductive, there has always been [pushback](https://www.afterall.org/article/why-we-need-decolonial-feminism-differentiation-and-co-constitutional-domination-of-western-modernit) against these approaches in the form of [decolonial feminism](https://pentransmissions.com/2021/04/30/decolonial-feminisms-an-interview-with-francoise-verges/)(Decolonial feminism is about making visible the colonial genealogy of entanglements of oppression. It stands alongside revolutionary feminism, decolonial, queer, black, indigenous and Islamic feminisms, but if I write about decolonial feminism it is because I see the process of decolonisation as being vital and necessary. The feminism I defend is not exclusive of other feminisms that are radically anti-racist, anti-capitalist and anti-imperialist, and thus anti-heteropatriarchy.). This approach is now being adopted more widely, giving a broader perspective on [many](https://truthout.org/articles/to-abolish-prisons-and-militarism-we-need-anti-imperialist-abolition-feminism/) [issues](https://theecologist.org/2021/sep/14/climate-migration-feminist-issue).
1.2.3.3.3. Con: While feminism in the West has a racist history, great strides are being made to decolonise, radicalise, and [nuance](https://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/2021/mar/17/my-feminism-will-be-intersectional-or-it-will-be-bullshit-whats-next-for-the-march-4-justice) modern day forms of feminism.
1.2.3.3.3.1. Pro: Increasingly, [anti-racist](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2021/sep/19/no-more-white-saviours-thanks-how-to-be-a-true-anti-racist-ally) views are being platformed. This may erode the [liberal assumptions](https://www.thecut.com/2021/08/rafia-zakaria-against-white-feminism-book.html)(White feminism as a worldview speaks to a set of entrenched assumptions and behaviors that center whiteness and see western values as superior. This universalization of white feminists’ concerns as being those of all feminists has been successfully exported globally, and the consequences have been particularly devastating for women of color around the world — from the daily humiliations that come from tokenistic corporate initiatives in the U.S. to white-savior programs in the Global South that go nowhere.) of mainstream forms of feminisms to create a better and more sensitive movement.
1.2.3.3.3.2. Pro: Previously regressive teen girl magazines have become [radically feminist](https://www.journals.uchicago.edu/doi/abs/10.1086/707797) and adopted many [intersectional](https://www.berghahnjournals.com/view/journals/girlhood-studies/14/3/ghs140304.xml) stances. This educates younger generations and is likely to ensure that feminist movements continue to improve.
1.2.3.3.3.3. Con: Rising [transphobia](https://thewire.in/lgbtqia/chimamanda-adichies-essay-and-the-rise-of-trans-exclusionary-feminism) from some feminists can fuel [anti-Black](https://www.them.us/story/anti-trans-sports-bills-transphobic-racist) policy making, particularly in [sports](https://gal-dem.com/athletics-war-of-transphobia-and-misogynoir-black-african-women-losing/)(At their core, the rules are a bio-essentialist dictation of what ‘womanhood’ is. And black African women are disproportionately falling afoul of the regulations. \n\nSince the ruling, seven black African women have been forced out of their events thanks to their natural hormone levels...\n\nThe narrow definition of what World Athletics views as a ‘woman’, draws on colonial and racist histories to police the bodies of black – and especially black African – women. \n\nThese regulations imply that womanhood is something that can be measured and plotted, but this view of gender always results in an ‘ideal’ and an excluded ‘Other’. In this case, black women who have historically been viewed as ‘masculine’, are the targets of these exclusionary policies, particularly those who have higher testosterone levels, despite the fact they naturally occur.).
1.2.3.3.4. Pro: Western feminists often hold reductive and dangerously binaristic ideals that associate the West with development and liberation, obfuscating histories of gender equality in other nations \([p. 2](https://www.e-ir.info/pdf/58703)(A view shared among the WMW feminists is that gender equality is solely a Western idea\(l\), despite egalitarian relations between men and women being ‘a living reality in much of the world in precolonial times, which was far from the case in Western culture’ \(Etienne and Leacock 1980a:vi\).)\).
1.2.3.3.5. Pro: The birth of the modern feminist movement was rooted in white women voicing their opinions and making demands to shape policies to help other white women; the achievements, needs, and desires of minorities were often [ignored](https://time.com/6108414/white-feminism-world-fair-chicago-history/).
1.2.3.4. Con: Feminist movements in [Asia](https://www.ips-journal.eu/regions/asia/a-new-feminism-is-emerging-in-asia-4225/)(With representation from feminists and political activists of all ages, classes and genders, the Girls at ‘Dhabas’ movement in Pakistan and India’s ‘Pinjra Tod’ \(Break the Cage\) and ‘I Will go Out’ movements are additional examples of more inclusive alliances.\n\nIn these examples, women formed small informal initiatives and addressed very specific issues at first such as restrictive house rules for female students. They dared to go out alone or in groups at night and made smart use of social media, making their individual acts visible to wider audiences. They were also open and adapted to criticism about inclusiveness and pushed intersectionality by reflecting about class and caste. Very soon they picked up wider social justice issues such as domestic violence or climate change.) are highly inclusive and growing in strength; such advances are likely to help women of many races.
1.2.3.4.1. Pro: Asian feminists have pushed for [expansions](https://asiafoundation.org/2021/10/13/is-asia-ready-for-a-feminist-foreign-policy/) of their role into foreign policy, which is likely to have great dividends in the future as [diplomacy](https://oxfordre.com/internationalstudies/internationalstudies/view/10.1093/acrefore/9780190846626.001.0001/acrefore-9780190846626-e-130)(Feminists argued that these expectations valorize behaviors that are associated with men and therefore perpetuate their dominance in the field. Instead, they introduced alternative perspectives on conflict, mediation, and negotiation, focusing primarily on power dynamics and social aspects of relationships \(Kolb and Coolidge 1991; Kolb 1992; Taylor and Miller 1994; Kolb and Putnam 1995; Ely and Meyerson 2000; Putnam and Kolb 2000\).) is bolstered.
1.2.3.4.2. Con: In places like [South Korea](https://observers.france24.com/en/asia-pacific/20210914-the-south-korean-men-waging-a-vulgar-and-violent-war-against-feminists), traditional values are seen as diametrically opposed to women's liberation; the movement may be unable to circumvent this.
1.2.3.4.3. Con: Chinese feminists may find themselves [censored](https://www.reuters.com/world/china/closure-online-feminist-groups-china-sparks-call-women-stick-together-2021-04-14/); this stifles activism and may have negative [outcomes](https://www.businessinsider.com/china-social-credit-system-punishments-and-rewards-explained-2018-4?r=US&IR=T) for the women themselves.
1.2.3.4.4. Pro: Women in [Myanmar](https://www.opendemocracy.net/en/5050/were-unstoppable-meet-the-women-leading-myanmars-protests/) stand as role models in their fight to preserve democracy and achieve gender equality.
1.2.4. Con: Women have become less happy as they have experienced an increase in rights and access to the workforce - in part tied to the rise of feminist action \([p. 3](https://www.frbsf.org/economic-research/files/wp09-11bk.pdf)(We will show in this paper that women’s happiness has fallen both absolutely and relative to men’s in a \npervasive way among groups, such that women no longer report being happier than men and, in many \ninstances, now report happiness that is below that of men. Moreover, we show that this shift has occurred through much of the industrialized world.)\). As such, the policies feminists support are not conducive to a better society.
1.2.4.1. Pro: Feminism may struggle to make change as it promotes [anti-family](https://medium.com/\@NikitaCcoulombe/why-feminism-wants-to-dismantle-the-family-long-4695d45bcf88) policies and perspectives. These are legitimised by claiming that marriage and child-rearing are patriarchal.
1.2.4.1.1. Pro: Some feminists believe women should work and take up the fight for equality - instead of getting married, and [raising kids](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2015/mar/02/housewife-feminist-baby)(My take used to be the one espoused by Ann Oakley, the British feminist and author of 70s text Housewife: “Housework is work directly opposed to the possibility of human self-actualisation.) - as they do not believe it is possible or desirable to do both.
1.2.4.1.1.1. Con: Feminists are not anti-family as that would defy their ethos of gender equality; rather their policies expand freedoms to benefit many, including [families](https://msmagazine.com/2021/11/08/paid-leave-families-build-back-better/).
1.2.4.1.1.2. Pro: Some feminists have suggested that stay-at-home mothering should be [illegal](https://www.nationalreview.com/2017/03/feminist-columnist-stay-home-moms-illegal-australia/), directly countering the principles of free choice that feminism espouses.
1.2.4.1.1.3. Con: Popular media outlet, [Everyday Feminism](https://everydayfeminism.com/2016/03/myths-stay-at-home-moms/), promotes that stay at home moms should be supported by feminism.
1.2.4.1.2. Pro: [Political lesbianism](https://theconversation.com/the-gay-community-should-stop-attacking-anyone-who-dares-suggest-sexuality-is-a-choice-29297)(The notion of political lesbianism based on a feminist rejection of heteropatriarchy has been around since the 1970s, and there is also research suggesting that women’s sexuality is more fluid than men’s.) encouraged women to actively disavow people they loved in order to subvert the patriarchy. This approach [denigrated](https://jezebel.com/lesbianism-sexual-orientation-political-choice-or-b-5144133)(It's good to think of homosexuality as something that can be joyful and empowering, rather than some sort of congenital disease. But Bindel's view does a disservice to people who don't feel they chose their sexual orientations, and especially to people who have been fighting for equal rights partially on that basis. It also assumes that men are the enemy, and that women can achieve happiness and political self-actualization only by living apart from them.) women's choices and was likely alienating.
1.2.4.1.3. Con: Feminists do not disavow family, marriage, or traditional house-keeping as a rule; rather they disavow the systems involved in each of these that denigrate women's work and restrict their choices \([pp. 76-77](https://warwick.ac.uk/fac/arts/english/currentstudents/postgraduate/masters/modules/femlit/04-federici.pdf)(The difference lies in the fact that not only has housework been imposed on women, but it has been transformed into a natural attribute of our female physique and personality, an internal need, an aspiration, supposedly coming from the depth of our female character.\nHousework had to be transformed into a natural attribute rather than be recognized as a social contract because from the beginning of capital’s scheme for women this\nwork was destined to be unwaged. Capital had to convince us that it is a natural, unavoidable and even fulfilling activity to make us accept our unwaged work.)\).
1.2.4.1.4. Con: Women often feel [pressure](http://newsroom.unl.edu/releases/2012/10/11/Study%3A+Childfree+women+feel+most+pressure+to+have+kids,+but+stress+least+about+it)(Women who choose to be permanently childfree feel less distress about not having kids than women who are childless from infertility and other reasons, a new national study shows. At the same time, voluntarily childfree women perceive more social pressures to become mothers than women who cannot have children.\n\n The study, from a national survey of nearly 1,200 American women of reproductive age with no children, identified various reasons why women have no children -- from medical and situational barriers to delaying pregnancy to choosing to be childfree. It sought to determine if those reasons contributed to different types of concerns about being childless) to have children, despite having other priorities. When feminism celebrates alternative forms of the good life - career based or otherwise - these women may feel as if they have more support.
1.2.4.2. Pro: Part of the decrease in women's happiness may stem from feminists [shaming](https://www.theguardian.com/fashion/2020/jan/27/tradwives-new-trend-submissive-women-dark-heart-history) traditional women. These women are often seen as counter to the movement and are pressured to adopt different ideals and behaviors.
1.2.4.2.1. Pro: Feminism can put [unrealistic pressure](https://time.com/5789438/feminism-poverty-gun-violence/)(I am talking about feminist issues, though you may not recognize them as such. We hear about career advancement and dating while feminist and body hair and last names, but rarely does mainstream feminism center the conversation on issues that concern most women in this country. Can they afford food? Do they have access to health care? Are they safe in their homes? Do they have homes at all? Can they meet all of their basic needs?\n\nOverwhelmingly, the answer to that last question is “no.” For a movement that is meant to represent all women, feminism frequently focuses on those who already have most of their needs met. All too often it’s not about survival but about increasing privilege.) on women to succeed. Some may feel that their life does not measure up to the movement's ethos and feel dejected.
1.2.4.2.2. Con: Some of the unhappiness women experience may stem from anti-feminist backlash. This indicates the continued necessity to push for social progress \([p.703](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/pdf/10.1177/1369148120948733)(Such attempts first started in the early 1990s when a loose antifeminist group formed opposing women’s rights advocates who were\nbecoming increasingly successful globally... A joint opposition to ‘gender ideology’ and the aim of restoring the ‘natural family’ unite the alliance. In recent years, its members have intensified their activities in the UN Human Rights Council, the Commission on the Status of Women \(CSW\), and the Security Council. It is in these fora that they have had the most success in halting and reversing the\ncourse of women’s rights.)\).
1.2.4.2.3. Con: Whilst some feminists may be dogmatic, others are open to [supportive discussions](https://theconversation.com/tradwives-the-women-looking-for-a-simpler-past-but-grounded-in-the-neoliberal-present-130968)(So although at first blush the Tradwife movement may seem profoundly at odds with our times – particularly in the wake of movements likes MeToo and TimesUp – it is very much a product of the contemporary moment. The choices made by women who identify as tradwives may be presented as entirely personal. However, they are inseparable from the profound crisis of both work and care under neoliberal capitalism.\n\nWe live in a time when normative gender roles and dominant notions of sexuality have not only been challenged but are in flux. As such, reasserting a narrowly defined version of femininity may be a way for some women to gain a sense of control over their lives.) of traditional values and the influences of choice in modernity.
1.2.4.3. Con: Correlation is not causation; there is no reason to believe that the rise in feminist activity caused a decrease in women's happiness.
1.2.4.3.1. Pro: Women are often stressed about balancing family and career, as men do not share equally in [household responsibilities](https://www.huffingtonpost.ca/2017/09/27/women-chores-home_a_23224733/). It is not choice that causes women stress, but patriarchy.
1.2.4.3.2. Pro: Women may no longer feel pressure to feign happiness, due to feminism \([p. 28](https://www.frbsf.org/economic-research/files/wp09-11bk.pdf)(In the context of the findings presented in this paper, women may now feel more comfortable being honest about their true happiness and have thus deflated their previously inflated responses.)\). This increase in honesty makes it more possible to craft useful social policy, as there is more information on women's true preferences and needs.
1.2.4.3.3. Con: Women now have to choose between having a family, their career, or balancing both - which can be [challenging](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2016/oct/14/perfect-girls-five-women-stories-mental-health) to manage. Feminism did not improve their quality of life by encouraging this dilemma.
1.2.5. Pro: Feminists fight to [protect](https://www.unwomen.org/en/news/in-focus/end-violence-against-women) women from gendered violence, sexual assault, and [harassment](http://www.stopstreetharassment.org/resources/statistics/).
1.2.5.1. Pro: [Thirty-five percent of women](http://www.unwomen.org/en/what-we-do/ending-violence-against-women/facts-and-figures) worldwide have experienced either physical and/or sexual intimate partner violence or sexual violence by a non-partner at some point in their lives. Feminism can help combat this by changing social norms.
1.2.5.1.1. Pro: [Seventy percent](http://big.assets.huffingtonpost.com/toplines_harassment_0819202013.pdf) of women who claim to have been sexually assaulted in the workplace did not report it.
1.2.5.1.2. Con: Feminist activism, in particular the [#MeToo](https://www.vox.com/identities/2018/10/9/17933746/me-too-movement-metoo-brett-kavanaugh-weinstein) movement, has been criticized for creating an [anti-men bias](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/nov/30/metoo-has-been-misrepresented-as-plot-against-men-says-founder) in legal systems. Critics say this [may](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-us-canada-42200092)(The question of who stands as judge and jury is also a cause for concern. There's often no corroborating evidence in cases of historic abuse, no witnesses or photographs. We are all still learning how to distinguish what seems credible and what doesn't. Women's stories of harassment should be believed, and they often haven't been in the past, but they should also be able to withstand scrutiny.\n\nAs in all reporting, due diligence is as necessary here as ever. As we get more accounts of fake accusers, trying to discredit real accusers, this need for scrutiny will grow. Women are tough enough to withstand fair questions.) harm due process, and encourage people to [assume](https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/business/digital/attorneys-combat-me-too-era-armie-hammer-1234958769/) the guilt of the accused.
1.2.5.1.2.1. Con: Anti-men bias does not exist if the claims are true. Men are [statistically](https://www.usnews.com/news/best-countries/articles/2017-10-25/how-metoo-has-awoken-women-around-the-world) more likely to be sexual predators, and women are [statistically](https://fortune.com/2017/10/17/me-too-hashtag-sexual-harassment-at-work-stats/) more likely to be the victims.
1.2.5.1.2.1.1. Con: [Statistics](https://towardsdatascience.com/what-is-statistical-bias-and-why-is-it-so-important-in-data-science-80e02bf7a88d) may neither prove nor disprove a bias, as they can be heavily influenced by existing [biases](https://www.theguardian.com/science/2019/jan/12/psychology-of-group-reasoning-versus-individual).
1.2.5.1.2.1.2. Con: Social expectations and understanding of coercion may [contribute](https://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/female-sex-offenders-more-common-gender-bias-statistics-rape-abuse-a7839361.html) to a significant undercounting of female sexual predators.
1.2.5.1.2.1.3. Pro: Image based sexual abuse is more likely to harm women than men, due to deeply gendered moral ideas of sex \([p. 2](https://www.birmingham.ac.uk/Documents/college-artslaw/law/research/bham-law-spotlight-IBSA.pdf)(The harms of image-based sexual abuse are deeply gendered. Not only are victims mostly women and girls, but the abuse and harassment to which they are subjected is sexualised and misogynistic. The persistence of sexual double standards enables offenders to shame and humiliate victims - with families, friends, employers and strangers commonly blaming victims.)\).
1.2.5.1.2.1.4. Pro: Women often [fear](http://www.gq-magazine.co.uk/article/incel-meaning-explained) for their safety when rejecting romantic interest from male strangers, given the [risk](https://www.theguardian.com/world/shortcuts/2019/mar/25/being-a-woman-is-scary-the-unspoken-danger-of-declining-a-mans-advances) that they could be [harmed](https://www.latimes.com/archives/la-xpm-2010-jan-11-la-na-rape-craigslist11-2010jan11-story.html).
1.2.5.1.2.2. Pro: Many celebrities, business leaders and media personalities have [lost jobs](https://fortune.com/2018/10/23/metoo-movement-female-replacements/)(According to a New York Times analysis, at least 200 men have been dismissed or demoted following allegations of sexual misconduct. The actions of these 200 men have affected as many as 920 individuals; some of the men in question now face criminal charges.\n\nThe allegations have also had an effect on the way industries do business: in May, the Senate passed a new bill addressing Congress’s sexual harassment policy, and Wall Street has implemented a ‘Weinstein clause.’ Even this year’s Nobel Peace Prize winners, Congolese doctor Denis Mukwege and Yazidi activist Nadia Murad, were awarded the prestigious prize for their work fighting sexual violence.) over accusations that could be not [substantiated](https://www.axios.com/global-metoo-movement-convictions-charges-382ff226-7ad3-4b26-ac89-451788192578.html)(Why it matters: The #MeToo movement focused global attention on previously unchecked sexual misconduct, leading at least 201 powerful men to lose jobs or major positions. But the movement, dubbed a global reckoning, has had few legal consequences for the accused. Here are some of the most notable cases.) and brought to civil or criminal court.
1.2.5.1.2.3. Pro: A bias is formed when you become influenced by statistics or narratives rather than the facts of a case; feminism encourages this with the shift to [believing all victims](https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2020/05/believe-women-bad-slogan-joe-biden-tara-reade/611617/).
1.2.5.1.2.4. Con: Due process is not controlled by citizens, but rather is influenced by [policing culture](https://www.thecut.com/2021/09/book-excerpt-the-right-to-sex-by-amia-srinivasan.html)(In the U.S., which has the world’s highest incarceration rate, 147 men were exonerated for sexual assault on the basis of false accusations or perjury between 1989 and 2020. \(In that same period, 755 people — five times as many — were found to have been falsely accused, and wrongly convicted, of murder.\) Fewer than half of these men were deliberately framed by their alleged victims. Meanwhile, over half of their cases involved “official misconduct”: a category that applies when the police coach false victim or witness identifications, charge a suspect despite the victim’s failure to identify him as her attacker, suppress evidence or induce false confessions.) and other incentives, which feminists may struggle to influence.
1.2.5.1.2.4.1. Pro: There are few examples, if any, of men who are not provided legal due process. Most reported claims of sexual crimes do not [receive convictions](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/oct/15/metoo-justice-system-complaints-up-convictions-down), suggesting that the legal system has a bias that favors men.
1.2.5.1.2.4.2. Pro: Abuse of due process due to policing culture can be seen in the Duke false allegation case. The DA abused his position of power and [pursued](https://www.vanityfair.com/news/2016/03/duke-lacrosse-case-fantastic-lies-documentary)(Nifong overzealously championed his case in the media. The DNA evidence did not match any of the three players, but it showed that other men had been with Mangum in the week before the incident.\n\nIn a clever tactic, the defense attorneys turned to the North Carolina State Bar to intervene, and for the first time in its history, the state bar brought charges against a sitting district attorney—Nifong—for being too outspoken and concealing the crucial DNA evidence. Nine months into the case, Nifong dropped the rape charge and offered Mangum the chance to abandon the entire case. But she refused his offer. She said she wanted justice. Eventually, to defend himself in front of the state bar, Nifong had to recuse himself from the case, and he handed it over to Roy Cooper, the North Carolina attorney general who four months later dropped the remaining charges against the players, declared them “innocent,” and called Nifong a “rogue prosecutor.”) the case, likely because he was [up for re-election](https://www.huffingtonpost.co.uk/entry/duke-lacrosse-rape-espn-30-for-30_n_56e07e33e4b065e2e3d486f7)(Nifong was running for election as the DA when the case landed on his desk. He had been appointed to the position on an interim basis in 2005. Critics subsequently said Nifong pushed the Mangum case so strongly because of the upcoming election -- and indeed, the investigation helped him garner endorsements from Durham's prominent black leaders. Voters responded at the ballot box by carrying Nifong to a 3 percent win over challenger Freda Black.). Feminists could not influence this.
1.2.5.1.3. Pro: Refuge shelters have [feminist](https://theconversation.com/you-couldnt-leave-your-husband-it-wasnt-done-the-story-of-the-women-behind-the-first-domestic-violence-refuges-160895) origins. Feminists worked to make a space for women as they were, and still are, [overwhelmingly](https://www.ourwatch.org.au/quick-facts/) more likely to be victimised by their partners than vice versa.
1.2.5.1.3.1. Con: Women report higher rates of perpetuating intimate partner violence than men, and men report higher rates of experiencing this violence. Feminism leaves out some victims by emphasising women \([p. 2](https://www.ojp.gov/pdffiles1/170018.pdf)(About 27 percent of women and\n34 percent of men among the\nDunedin study members reported\nthey had been physically abused by\ntheir partner. About 37 percent of\nwomen and 22 percent of men said\nthey had perpetrated the violence.)\).
1.2.5.1.3.2. Pro: Feminist theorists, like MacKinnon, have problematised the idea of a private/public life distinction to call attention to the harms women can experience in the home, opening new space for policy making and discussion \([p. 4](https://gbvaor.net/sites/default/files/2019-07/Feminist%20Strategies%20to%20End%20VAW%20OXFORD%20Handbook%202015.pdf)(Catharine MacKinnon wrote that “\[t\]o complain in public of inequality within the private contradicts the liberal definition of the private. ... In this scheme, intimacy is implicitly thought to guarantee symmetry of power. Injuries arise through violation of the private sphere, not within, by and because of it” \(1989, 190\). According to MacKinnon, the liberal public/private paradigm offers no recourse to women for whom the private sphere is not a haven of freedom, but is instead a space wherein they are beaten, raped, and oppressed. Thus, the feminist response must be to explode this erroneous binary and demand public \(state\) responses to what was previously deemed private \(and therefore unpunishable\) violence.)\).
1.2.5.2. Con: Some forms of feminism fail to reconcile progressive activism with misogynistic practices in some religions and cultures.
1.2.5.2.1. Pro: Some feminists [claim](https://www.eurozine.com/islamic-feminism-contradiction-terms/) that Islam is compatible with liberatory thinking, yet the two [contradict](http://www.dw.com/en/womens-rights-in-the-islamic-world/a-40714427) each other. Ignorance of this repression is illegitimate and causes harm.
1.2.5.2.1.1. Pro: Some feminists [fail](https://www.irishtimes.com/life-and-style/people/why-is-feminism-so-quiet-about-muslim-women-who-refuse-to-wear-the-hijab-1.3189620) to support Muslim women who refuse to wear the veil, for fear of being branded Islamophobic.
1.2.5.2.1.2. Con: Denigrations of Islam as anti-feminist are often based in [reductive](https://penntoday.upenn.edu/news/how-islamic-feminism-could-shape-gender-equity)(Hoodfar does this by making us aware of the colonial history between Islam and the ‘Western world’ that has resulted in an obsession with veiling as something that could only be a symptom of oppression. While the veil could be a sign of oppression, certainly, in other contexts, the veil had more complicated meaning. For instance, the veil in Algeria became a sign of anti-colonial resistance.) perceptions of hijabi autonomy.
1.2.5.2.1.3. Con: Islamic feminists find that their faith [empowers](https://theconversation.com/islam-and-feminism-are-not-mutually-exclusive-and-faith-can-be-an-important-liberator-77086) their politics. By claiming that feminism and Islam are incompatible, these women are harmed.
1.2.5.2.1.4. Pro: In Pakistan, the Council of Islamic Ideology [opposes advancements](https://www.dw.com/en/is-it-time-to-reform-pakistans-council-of-islamic-ideology/a-19262444)(In February, the provincial Punjab assembly passed a landmark women's protection bill, establishing hotlines and shelters for women to protect them from domestic, psychological and sexual violence. While the bill was praised by the Islamic country's rights groups and liberal sections, religious parties and organizations denounced it by saying it conflicted with the Koran and the teachings of Muhammad, Islam's prophet.\n\nBut the most vociferous criticism against the legislation came from the country's Council of Islamic Ideology \(CII\), a powerful religious body that advises lawmakers on the compatibility of legislations with Islam.\n\n"The law is wrong," Muhammad Khan Sherani, the head of the council, told reporters in Islamabad.\n\nSherani said the CII studied the law closely and came to the conclusion that the lawmakers had not taken the Islamic teachings about "family protection" into consideration.) in women's liberation claiming that progressive legislature undermines the family and core tenets of their faith.
1.2.5.2.2. Con: Feminists have [campaigned](https://www.churchmilitant.com/news/article/feminists-demand-women-clergy-as-prelude-to-abolishing-priesthood)(Catholic feminists in Western Europe are mounting an open "revolt" on March 1 demanding the ordination of women, while asserting that the creation of female priests is "only an interim solution" to their ultimate goal of abolishing the hierarchical priesthood.\n\nJesus broke with all hierarchies and would not "even want to build a priesthood," says Lisa Kötter, co-founder of German über-feminist movement Maria 2.0. Likewise, in an unprecedented backlash to Pope Francis' slamming the door on women's ordination in Querida Amazonia, feminist theologians in Spain are saying their "frustrations with the Church have reached a boiling point.") for the [inclusion](https://ordainwomen.org/mission/)(Based on the principle of thoughtful, faith-affirming strategic action, Ordain Women aspires to create a space for Mormon women to articulate issues of gender inequality they may be hesitant to raise alone. As a group we intend to put ourselves in the public eye and call attention to the need for the ordination of Mormon women to the priesthood. We sincerely ask our leaders to take this matter to the Lord in prayer.) of female priests. Women are currently excluded from this crucial ecumenical role in many branches of Christianity, serving only in lower status positions.
1.2.5.2.3.
