1.4.3.2.2.1.3. Pro: [Girls](https://www.npr.org/sections/health-shots/2017/01/26/511801423/young-girls-are-less-apt-to-think-women-are-really-really-smart) often believe that women are not as smart as men and grow up [doubting](https://www.independent.co.uk/student/career-planning/british-girls-don-t-think-they-re-smart-enough-for-science-careers-says-study-a6673466.html) their intelligence. This system likely curtails educational progress, especially in competitive fields.
1.4.3.2.2.1.3.1. Pro: Girls [trust](https://www.ncgs.org/advocacy/blog/2019/02/08/why-girls-schools-students-are-successful-in-stem/) their maths and science skills more if they go to a single sex school. This indicates that socialisation is impacting their ability to learn confidently in co-ed schools.
1.4.3.2.2.2. Pro: Though women receive more STEM degrees than men, women often [prefer](https://www.pewresearch.org/science/2021/04/01/stem-jobs-see-uneven-progress-in-increasing-gender-racial-and-ethnic-diversity/)(The representation of women varies widely across STEM occupations. Women make up a large majority of all workers in health-related jobs, but remain underrepresented in other job clusters, such as the physical sciences, computing and engineering.) to work in health-related industries. These are legitimate choices and indicate opportunity and autonomy.
1.4.3.2.3. Con: Women are more likely to experience [disruption](https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/education-51769845) in their education - quotas ensure that places are preserved for them in spite of this.
1.4.3.2.3.1. Con: When women are allowed equal access to education, they are more likely to achieve the [highest levels](https://www.aei.org/carpe-diem/women-earned-majority-of-doctoral-degrees-in-2019-for-11th-straight-year-and-outnumber-men-in-grad-school-141-to-100/) of qualification.
1.4.3.2.3.2. Pro: Often sexism makes life so difficult for girls going to school that, even though they are allowed to attend, they will drop out \([p. 1](https://www.usaid.gov/sites/default/files/documents/1869/USAID_LGL_FactSheet.pdf)(Around the world 62 million girls are not in school. Millions more are \nfighting to stay there. As a girl grows older the fight to get an education becomes even harder. Her family must be able to afford and be willing to pay school fees. She risks long, dangerous walks to school. She may become pregnant or be forced to marry. And she often lacks access to healthcare and the support she needs to learn.)\).
1.4.3.2.4. Pro: [Women](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0272775717303278) are [more likely](https://www.theatlantic.com/education/archive/2019/02/the-explosion-of-women-teachers/582622/) to become teachers than [men](https://news.sky.com/story/men-make-up-just-three-out-of-every-10-teacher-trainees-this-year-12418386), offering them a crucial space to influence the minds of the next generation; any vestigial sexism is likely to be removed at this stage.
1.4.3.2.5. Con: Despite outperforming men at school, 63% of the time in the US, men receive [higher salary offers](https://hired.com/gender-wage-gap)(Looking back to our first report in 2017, and then again in 2018, men were offered higher salaries than women 63% of the time. Last year, we saw our first glimmer of hope that this gap had narrowed to 60% but this year’s data showed a disappointing return to the status quo: 63%.\n\nThis means that 6 times out of 10, women are offered less money than men to do the exact same job at the exact same company. On average, that salary figure is 3% less.) than women for the same job.
1.4.3.3. Pro: Feminism in legislation is harmfully biased against men.
1.4.3.3.1. Pro: Feminist activists and lawmakers [prioritise women](https://www.bl.uk/spare-rib/articles/violence-against-women) in their campaigns and the crafting of anti-violence legislature.
1.4.3.3.1.1. Pro: Spanish gender equality and violence laws [frame](http://justiciadegenero.com/en/analysis-of-8-years-of-gender-violence-law-in-spain/) women as the beneficiaries of legislature, and men as the perpetrators of harm.
1.4.3.3.1.2. Con: Men are [increasingly](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2021/sep/12/men-are-inventing-new-excuses-for-killing-women-and-judges-are-falling-for-them)(Nothing, anyway, from the Pybus judge, seems likely to diminish the popularity of “rough sex” as just the latest euphemism whereby a case of male violence can be portrayed as something other than part of a relentless, gendered pattern.) able to mount legal defences to justify the killing of their female sexual partners. Feminists need to prioritise women because of this.
1.4.3.3.1.3. Pro: Some feminists, such as Mary Koss, have discriminated against men victims of domestic and sexual violence \([pp. 206-207](http://boysmeneducation.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/01/Koss-1993-Detecting-the-Scope-of-Rape-a-review-of-prevalence-research-methods-see-p.-206-last-paragraph.pdf)\).
1.4.3.3.1.4. Con: Though some feminists may take reductive views on violence in relationships, not all do \([p. 41](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0277953617302721/pdfft?md5=a2306aff0cc0f805a77b8cf4a27facd8&pid=1-s2.0-S0277953617302721-main.pdf)(We ground our study within a feminist analysis, emphasizing the ways in which patriarchal power is constructed \(and sustained\) in the family: \(1\) patriarchy promotes a clear hierarchy, with men in a superior position to women and children; \(2\) childhood and gender norms reflect this structure, de-valuing women and children \(as well as their expected roles and behav-\niors\) while prioritizing men \(and hegemonic masculinities\); \(3\)\nwithin the patriarchal family, men's power/dominance must be demonstrated and reinforced, legitimizing violence as a form of\nsocial control over “subordinate” family members. Similarly, maternal violence must be situated within the broader context of the patriarchal family \(rather than understood as a specific incident or individual pathology\), which systemically disempowers women in many domains of their lives while granting them relative power vis-a-vis their children.)\).
1.4.3.3.1.5. Pro: The National Organization for Women [blasted efforts](http://ncfm.org/2012/06/news/domestic-abuse-violence/the-national-coalition-for-women-blasts-efforts-to-include-sensible-and-gender-inclusive-provisions-in-legislation-to-reauthorize-the-violence-against-women-act/) to [include](https://www.congress.gov/bill/112th-congress/house-bill/4970/text) [gender-inclusive language](https://www.congress.gov/bill/109th-congress/house-bill/2876/text?q=%7B%22search%22%3A%5B%22violence+against+women%22%5D%7D&r=84) in the Violence Against Women Act.
1.4.3.3.2. Con: Feminism [helps](https://mic.com/articles/88277/23-ways-feminism-has-made-the-world-a-better-place-for-men#.VootIviQA)(In 1976, the U.S. Supreme Court ruled it was unconstitutional to treat women and men differently under the law. The case, Craig v. Boren, was filled by a plaintiff in Oklahoma over its gender-specific drinking age policy, which prohibited men from drinking before age 21, but allowed women to drink when as young as 18. This implied that men are inherently more reckless and women are more responsible. After the law was struck down, the drinking age became 21 for all. \n\nAccording to Justice Ruth Bader Ginsburg, the ruling determined much more than just Oklahoma's drinking age. It determined that the "familiar stereotype: the active boy, aggressive and assertive; the passive girl, docile and submissive" was "not fit to be written into law." So the next time you're drinking, raise a glass in honor of RBG.) men by overturning laws unfavourable to them through campaign and activism.
1.4.3.3.2.1. Pro: Women in Illinois unfairly used to be able to drink alcohol at a younger age than men. [Feminists](https://www.theatlantic.com/health/archive/2015/10/when-women-could-drink-at-18-and-men-at-21/409066/) campaigned to raise the legal drinking to be equal for both.
1.4.3.3.2.2. Pro: Feminist politicians have fought for [paternal leave](https://apolitical.co/solution-articles/en/parental-leave-policy-changed-way-sweden-sees-fatherhood), particularly in Scandinavian countries.
1.4.3.3.2.3. Con: As men are often considered the [default](https://www.campaignlive.co.uk/article/unconscious-bias-default-male/1462277) gender in society, there are seldom laws that discriminate against them for their gender. For feminism to prioritise them would be futile.
1.4.3.3.3. Con: Laws are more likely to be unjustly biased against women than men, such that any imbalance that feminists may introduce would be limited in its effect.
1.4.3.3.3.1. Pro: [Many](https://www.unicef.org/protection/child-marriage) women are married or in union before age 18 and can experience a host of negative consequences because of this. They need feminists to fight for them as they are unable to do so themselves.
1.4.3.3.3.1.1. Pro: Feminism in the Philippines likely had some influence over the decision to [raise the age of consent](https://www.reuters.com/world/asia-pacific/philippines-senate-backs-bill-raise-sexual-consent-age-12-16-2021-09-28/) from 12 to 16 \([pp. 11-13](https://library.fes.de/pdf-files/bueros/philippinen/14072.pdf)\).
1.4.3.3.3.2. Con: Given the [power](https://www.usip.org/guiding-principles-stabilization-and-reconstruction-the-web-version/safe-and-secure-environment/nec-0) the state has [over](https://www.bbc.com/future/article/20210427-the-stomp-reflex-when-governments-abuse-emergency-powers) its people, liberatory groups should campaign for all to be treated equally. This is the only way to achieve a just world, so if feminism undermines this it should be called out.
1.4.3.3.3.3. Pro: The [legal system](http://www.jurist.org/paperchase/2009/08/federal-court-demographics-changing-to.php) and [politics](https://www.usnews.com/news/politics/articles/2017-10-24/despite-diverse-demographics-most-politicians-are-still-white-men) in the United States are overwhelmingly dominated by \(white\) men. These systems are and have been biased against women. If feminism counteracts such biases by demanding equality of rights, then this should be welcomed.
1.4.3.3.3.3.1. Pro: One way to advocate for any group, minority or otherwise, is to push for new legislation protecting its constituents' rights, as [feminists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Organization_for_Women) have done in the US.
1.4.3.3.3.3.2. Con: The fact that a homogeneous group is in a position of power does not necessarily translate in biased lawmaking for the minority.
1.4.3.3.3.3.3. Pro: In the US State of Georgia, [it is legal](https://www.bbc.co.uk/bbcthree/article/20fefc32-a03f-493d-9695-2f9454bb2187) to take "upskirt" photos of women without their consent.
1.4.3.3.4. Pro: Women are more likely to receive [child custody following divorce](https://www.divorcenet.com/resources/divorce/for-men/divorce-for-men-why-women-get-child-custody-over-80-time), yet feminists do not campaign to remediate this.
1.4.3.3.4.1. Pro: Courts tend to [favour](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/robert-hughes/are-custody-decisions-bia_b_870709.html) mothers in custody battles in most Western countries.
1.4.3.3.4.2. Pro: In the US, paternity laws commonly [discriminate](https://dadsdivorce.com/articles/harsh-laws-that-discriminate-against-men-and-fathers/) against men; many such laws are supported by feminist groups such as the [National Organization of Women](https://canadiancrc.com/Newspaper_Articles/Wendy_McElroy_Paternity_Innocence_is_defence_14JUL04.aspx)("in 2002 Davis vetoed the California Paternity Justice Act, \(AB 2240\), which would have extended the challenge period and vacated judgments against falsely named "fathers." Women who knowingly signed false declarations of paternity would have been liable for criminal prosecution.\n\n\(Another factor in Davis' veto was the political pressure of groups like the National Organization of Women, who successfully argued that passing the act would harm children who might lose support payments.\)"), among [others](https://www.thecrimson.com/article/2003/5/19/preventing-paternity-fraud-by-luke-smithpthe/)(Feminists sometimes allow this disrespect for men to spill over into their rhetoric. Activist Helen Caldicott argues that men are psychopaths...and she also points out that men are “clinically and psychologically dead.” Columnist Anna Quindlen sums up her philosophy on gender issues: “It’s simply that I think women are superior to men.”\n\nSome might claim these women are joking...But is their man-hating humor really that funny? After all, who cares that the clinically and psychologically dead psychopaths are forced to support other people’s children? Men are guilty and should pay, simply because they are men. As California attorney Fatima Araiza says, “This is no longer the oppression of women. This is now the oppression of men.”).
1.4.3.3.4.3. Pro: Women's rights groups have fought [against](https://www.avoiceformen.com/mens-rights/opposing-shared-parenting-the-feminist-track-record/) shared parenting legislation.
1.4.3.3.4.4. Con: The discrimination in custody battles is [not brought on](https://queerguesscode.wordpress.com/2013/02/06/the-truth-about-feminism-and-child-custody-discrimination/) by feminism, nor is it necessarily [legally enshrined](https://www.blbsolicitors.co.uk/blog/are-the-family-courts-really-biased-towards-women/)(A 2015 study by the University of Warwick concluded that family courts do not discriminate against the father...\n\n“But there was actually no indication of any bias towards mothers over fathers by the courts; in fact we established there was a similar success rate for mothers and fathers applying for orders to have their children live with them...\n\nIndeed, in 2014 the Government pressed through The Children and Families Act 2014, Section 11 which enshrined in law the desire for “parental involvement”, which ordered courts “to presume, unless the contrary is shown, that involvement of that parent in the life of the child concerned will further the child’s welfare”.), so remediation of this issue is unlikely to occur through direct action.
1.4.3.3.4.4.1. Pro: Many custody settlements occur out of court and result in [mutual agreement](https://everydayfeminism.com/2013/08/bias-against-fathers/)(In fact, the majority of custody settlements – even those that favor the mother – are reached by mutual agreements outside of the courtroom.\n\nThat means that both parties agree in these situations that the mother should have custody.\n\nThis is also an unfair manifestation of patriarchal gender expectations in marriage – and those expectations are self-imposed.) that women should care for the children; this cannot be assailed through legal change.
1.4.3.3.4.5. Con: Feminists argue that women shouldn't be the default carer, as they often are \([p. 4](https://read.oecd-ilibrary.org/view/?ref=127_127000-awfnqj80me&title=Women-at-the-core-of-the-fight-against-COVID-19-crisis)(Not only do women dominate employment in the care sector, they also provide most unpaid work at home. Across the OECD on average, at just over four hours per day, women systematically spend around 2 hours per day more on unpaid work than men \(OECD Gender Data Portal\). Gender gaps in unpaid work are largest in Japan and Korea \(2.5 hours\) and Turkey \(4 hours per day\), where traditional norms on gender roles prevail. However, even in Denmark, Norway and Sweden – countries that express strong and progressive attitudes towards gender equality – gender gaps in unpaid work still amount to about one hour per day. Gender gaps in unpaid work are often larger in developing and emerging economies \(Section 3.4\).)\). In an equal society, judgements made regarding child custody would be decided by who is best suited for the task, something made easier through feminist action.
1.4.3.4. Con: In comparison to men, women do not experience meaningful social advantages, as even [benevolent sexism](https://www.sciencedirect.com/topics/psychology/benevolent-sexism) is still sexism. Pushing for feminists to dismantle spaces of only surface level advantage is a waste of their resources.
1.4.3.4.1. Pro: For women who take on the role of primary caregiver in a heterosexual relationship, the supposed advantages of not having to work and being able to spend more time with children can actually result in [social isolation and depression](https://www.glamour.com/story/stay-at-home-mom-depression-is-realand-women-are-finally-talking-about-it)(Complicating matters is the fact that depression is often overlooked among SAHMs because not going to work every day is viewed as a privileged choice. It’s lucky. That often means moms who struggle may feel they don’t have the right to speak out. “I told myself that so many other women would kill to be home with their kids all day, so I bottled up my feelings for fear of seeming ungrateful,” says Pamela Gillett, 32, a former stay-at-home mom of two from Michigan who went back to part-time work \(before the pandemic\) in order to cope.\n\nCompounding the pressure that many at-home moms put on themselves to not feel ungrateful is the message that if you’re at home and unhappy, you have only yourself to blame. Common advice given to at-home moms—get up early so you can have me time or exercise at home—send the message that if you only worked a little harder, you wouldn’t be so miserable.).
1.4.3.4.1.1. Pro: Women are often expected to [feel lucky](https://community.today.com/parentingteam/post/stop-telling-me-i-am-lucky-to-be-a-stay-at-home-mom) to have the choice to be a stay at home parent.
1.4.3.4.1.2. Pro: Women who are stay at home caregivers are [statistically more likely](https://news.gallup.com/poll/154685/stay-home-moms-report-depression-sadness-anger.aspx) to suffer mental health struggles than both their working parent and child-free women counterparts.
1.4.3.4.1.3. Con: Women may struggle initially to adapt to motherhood, though often find support in mother and baby groups that allow socialisation space and reduce stress \([p. 13](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2730910/pdf/jpe-18-012.pdf)(The literature indicates that New Parent groups that are attended predominantly by mothers are beneficial in terms of social support resulting from the opportunity to meet other mothers and to share experiences \(Carolan, 2004/2005; Gillieatt et al., 1999; Hanna et al., 2002; Lawson & Callaghan, 1991; Scott et al., 2001\). Social support also appears to exert a protective function against depression primarily through the mediation of self-efficacy \(Milgrom, Martin, & Negri, 1999; Teti & Gelfand, 1991\) and “promote\[s\] a positive self-evaluation in parenting…mediating the stress of the experience” \(Reece, 1993, p. 97\).)\).
1.4.3.4.1.4. Con: [Postpartum depression](https://www.pennmedicine.org/news/news-blog/2016/january/shedding-more-light-on-postpar)(Kim thinks it’s helpful when celebrities share their experiences in the hopes that they will help other women seek the help they need. “Women are afraid of being shamed and judged so they will not discuss their PPD and upsetting anxious thoughts,” Kim said. “They are so afraid we will take their child or hospitalize them but most of the time that's not necessary, especially with proper and timely diagnoses and early intervention. Women are so relieved to hear these scary thoughts are common – and that there’s help.”) is increasingly discussed, with new interventions to help treat the condition \([p. 9](https://mhealth.jmir.org/2018/2/e38/PDF)(This study demonstrates that a mobile intervention providing\npeer support and supplementary self-help tools as an adjunct\ntreatment for women with PPD is feasible and acceptable and suggests that this intervention might also be clinically helpful.)\).
1.4.3.4.2. Con: In many places, the duration of parental leave offered to women is [significantly greater](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2020/feb/11/gender-pay-gap-shared-parental-leave-finland)(As things stand, fathers get two weeks’ paternity leave at £148.68 \(24% don’t even qualify for that\), compared with statutory maternity pay at 39 weeks for women, including six weeks’ “enhanced pay”. According to the lobby group, Families Need Fathers, that’s a 96% “gender support gap”.) than that offered to men. This gives them a meaningful advantage in spending time and [bonding](https://www.newamerica.org/better-life-lab/reports/paid-family-leave-how-much-time-enough/gender-equality/)(Other studies have found that when fathers take leaves of two weeks or more, they’re more likely to be involved in direct child care nine months after birth, and more hands-on throughout a child’s life) with their newborn child.
1.4.3.4.2.1. Con: As well as allowing time for bonding with their child, maternity leave is designed to help women cope with the [biological stresses](https://www.beswicks.com/maternity-paternity-parental-leave/)(It is specifically designed to help a woman to cope with the latter stages of pregnancy, recuperate after the birth and care for and feed her newborn baby.) of the latter stages of pregnancy and the post-birth recovery. This is something men do not have to contend with.
1.4.3.4.2.2. Pro: Even when available, men in the US routinely face [stigma and shame](https://nypost.com/2021/11/03/paternity-leave-and-the-unspoken-pressure-of-men-taking-it/)(Men have faced sharp stigmas and an “unspoken pressure” when making a decision on paternity leave,\n\[...\]\nMen who want to take their allotted time off — even when the most common corporate policy for paternity leave is just two weeks, compared with 12 for moms — are faced with criticism and contempt, Woodward said, citing a recent conversation with a senior-level executive father who wanted to be home around the birth of his child.\n\n“It obviously wasn’t welcomed by his peers and there was talk about impact on career progression,” Woodward told The Post. He added that these kinds of judgements — and thinly veiled threats — are common in a “broader culture” that shames hands-on dads, particularly in male-dominated industries such as engineering, construction, IT and portions of finance and banking.) for taking paternity leave.
1.4.3.5. Pro: Some feminists have [opposed](http://www.sheknows.com/living/articles/1120821/drafting-women) equality in the draft.
1.4.3.5.1. Con: Feminists have advocated for the [inclusion of women](https://now.org/resource/issue-advisory-women-and-the-draft-moving-two-steps-closer-to-equality/)(The exclusion of women from the registration process was first challenged in the 1981 case Rostker v. Goldberg, 453 U.S. 57 \(1981\). Prominent feminist organizations, including the National Organization for Women, submitted briefs to the Court in an effort to emphasize the inherently sexist nature of this exclusion.) in the draft for decades, including in [military combat roles](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2014/apr/06/feminism-women-army-combat-roles).
1.4.3.5.2. Con: [Some feminists argue](https://truthout.org/articles/expanding-the-military-draft-is-not-feminism-abolishing-draft-registration-is/)(We are a generation that understands that no matter how hard the military tries to co-opt feminism and progressive ideals, war will never be a part of a framework for imagining equity because the first casualty of war is always human dignity. As draft-age people, the only military draft system reform we support is the complete abolition of compulsory military service.) that the draft strips people of rights. Rather than fighting for it to include women, they fight for it to be eliminated altogether to make the world more fair.
1.4.3.5.2.1. Con: It could be reasonably argued that addressing the issue of inequality in the draft will make it easier to abolish \([p. 36](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/misc/R44452.pdf)(In addition, some polling data suggest that if women were required to register for the draft, it would significantly increase public opposition to reinstating the draft and could affect public support for engaging in any conflict that has the\npotential to escalate beyond the capability of the all-volunteer force.)\).
1.4.3.5.2.2. Pro: Feminism is not just about gender parity but rather autonomy and [justice](https://www.ippr.org/juncture-item/what-is-abolitionist-feminism-and-why-does-it-matter)(Abolitionist Feminism invites us to consider the world we want, and how to organise to build it. Seeking a world beyond prisons, Abolitionist Feminism focuses our attention on developing stronger communities and bringing about gender, race and economic justice. It encourages us to consider our approach to problems from a social justice rather than criminal justice perspective; systemically rather than individually.); it would be [illegitimate](https://nnomy.org/en/content_page/item/931-feminists-against-the-draft.html)(Feminists Against the Draft is a coalition of intersectional feminists and feminist allies who raise awareness about the military draft and oppose any attempts to expand Selective Service registration, with the ultimate goal of abolition of the draft. We believe a person’s desire to enter or oppose the U.S. military is hugely personal, we advocate for the rights of women and children domestically and abroad, and we emphasize the need for progress rather than “inclusion” for marginalized groups in unjust systems.) to apply oppressive systems to all people in the name of equality.
1.4.3.5.2.3. Pro: Many feminists disagree with nationalism, which often requires a military to defend and enshrine \([p. 2](https://eprints.soas.ac.uk/25539/1/al-ali-tas-reconsidering-nationalism-and-feminism-Nations-and-Nationalism.docx.pdf)(Many feminist academics and \nactivists have been categorical in judging nationalism to be antithetical to women’s liberation \(Enloe 1989; Parker and Yaeger 1992; McClintock 1996\). Western feminists, frequently in opposition to their own government’s national and international policies, tend to view nationalism as a vehicle to further patriarchy.)\). Given this, it would undermine their beliefs to advocate for the military in any manner.
1.4.3.5.3. Pro: Many people have claimed it is biased and outdated to require that [only men](https://www.generalassembly.ca/archive/we-can-do-it-but-we-dont-want-to)(The debate on including women in Selective Service is contentious and multifaceted. It involves conservative and religiously inclined views on the traditional roles of women, feminists stressing the importance of non-military contributions of women to the state, and Men’s Rights groups challenging the equality of a male only draft. Among the array of opinions, a feminist perspective must stress equality for both genders. In an age of gender equality under the law it is no longer justifiable to exclude women.) be eligible for conscription, yet many feminists do not to ameliorate this discrepancy.
1.4.3.5.4. Pro: While many prominent feminists argue against any draft, they also [oppose](https://hasbrouck.org/draft/women/feminism.html)(Women’s equality will not be achieved by including women in a draft system that forces civilians to participate in activities that are against their will and harm others in large numbers, such as war. The draft is not a women’s rights issue, as it does nothing to advance the cause of equality and functionally limits freedom of choice for Americans of all genders.\n\n\[Statement from CODEPINK submitted to the National Commission on Military, National, and Public Service, 24 September 2019\]) measures to draft men and women [equally](http://www.swarthmore.edu/library/peace/DG051-099/dg068.wcoc/dg068.wcochistory.htm)(Feminist proponents of the ERA fell into several camps. All supported the view that women were physically capable of military service. Feminist pacifists did not deny the ability of women for service, but did not want to support the possibility of extending the draft to another large segment of the population. The dilemma for many feminists became trying to deny that the intention of the ERA would be diluted by gender considerations in military service, while not recommending the extension of conscription for another segment of the population.). This allows men to continue to be exploited as the draft remains.
1.4.3.5.5. Con: The [military](https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/2021/oct/25/revealed-scale-of-abuse-and-sexual-harassment-of-women-in-uk-military) is often incredibly hostile to women; it would be a dereliction of their duty for feminists to advocate for women to be forced into service, even if it made society ostensibly equal.
1.4.3.5.5.1. Con: It is possible for feminists to advocate for fair and equal treatment in both the military and the draft.
1.4.4. Con: Current forms of feminism do not oppress or come to the detriment of men. Rather, their critiques of men's power and privileges can be alienating, as they target something often taken for granted.
1.4.4.1. Pro: Men are generally not accustomed to pushback from women; therefore, many men mistakenly associate feminism with oppressive actions that diminish their masculinity and livelihoods.
1.4.4.1.1. Pro: Women who assert themselves are often associated with being aggressive or bossy while men doing the same are seen as confident leaders. This [double standard](https://leanin.org/tips/mvp)(This bias often surfaces in the way women are described, both in passing and in performance reviews. When a woman asserts herself—for example, by speaking in a direct style or promoting her ideas—she is often called “aggressive” and “ambitious.” When a man does the same, he is seen as “confident” and “strong.”\n\nWhen you hear a woman called “bossy” or “shrill,” request a specific example of what the woman did and then ask, “Would you have the same reaction if a man did the same thing?”) often leads men to feel unduly oppressed.
1.4.4.1.2. Pro: As recently as the 1960s, women were [prohibited](https://edition.cnn.com/2014/08/07/living/sixties-women-5-things/index.html) from doing a number of activities that men could; men are likely to be uncomfortable within these situations, as historically they have held all the power.
1.4.4.1.3. Pro: Boys who are [disciplined](https://www.fatherly.com/health-science/mother-father-discipline-differences-science/)(In one of the first studies to tackle the topic in 1992, researchers tracked the disciplinary styles of over 100 parents with children in preschool. Based on the self-reported accounts of disciplinary styles moms and dads, results showed that when mothers used more harsh, coercive, and power-assertive forms of discipline, their kids displayed more aggression and were generally less popular with among their peers.) by their mothers in domineering ways often go on to be aggressive with their peers; this lack of an emotional schema to negotiate criticism from women may carry through to adulthood.
1.4.4.1.4. Con: Men and women make [equally good bosses](https://www.apa.org/research/action/boss)(For example, women's typically more mentoring, coaching style is more favorably received in female-dominated professions; men's more typically "command and control" style is well received in male-dominated professions.\n\nThus, all things being equal, men and women are equally effective.) provided they flex their leadership style to match the standard of their profession.
1.4.4.1.5. Con: Though men and women may currently enter debates with [different standards](https://www.theatlantic.com/sexes/archive/2013/04/men-and-women-tend-to-argue-about-different-things-in-different-ways/274807/) for engagement, these are likely to be socialised and may shift generationally, leading men to view feminism more positively.
1.4.4.2. Pro: [Third-wave feminism](https://link.medium.com/WToExBObWkb)(Third-wave feminism does, however, introduce the idea that males can be oppressed by females on the basis of gender and conceptualises transgender males as suffering oppression on the axis of gender \(interpreted as personal identity rather than hierarchy\), this privileges females over males and creates a feminist movement that centres and prioritises males; women do not suffer material oppression per se, rather the social category ‘woman’ is subject to oppression the corollary of this is that oppression is something one may identify themselves into or out of.) discusses the ways in which power can be used by all groups to enact oppression, including by women to harm men. This is far more holistic than prior theorisations of power.
1.4.4.2.1. Con: Third-wave feminism is often considered to be [toxic](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2014/nov/18/feminism-rosetta-scientist-shirt-dapper-laughs-julien-blanc-inequality), as it focuses on shaming sexist men rather than engaging with the source of these actions.
1.4.4.2.1.1. Con: Though some people could be considered to be toxic feminists, they do not constitute the majority; some argue that [toxic feminism](http://geekfeminism.wikia.com/wiki/Toxic_femininity) is not a real thing.
1.4.4.2.1.2. Pro: Influential feminists have [historically](https://menarehuman.com/killallmen/) been unapologetically [misandrist](https://misandry.tripod.com/id6.html); the newer waves now [frame](https://time.com/3101429/misandry-misandrist-feminist-womenagainstfeminism/)(But inherent in this word “misandry” is hatred. And inherent in phrases like “ban men” and “male tears” are cruelty and violence. If a man wore a tee shirt that said “misogynist,” even if he were a dyed-in-the-wool feminist, wearing it tongue-in-cheek, it would not be funny. It would be misguided.) it as "[ironic](https://slate.com/human-interest/2014/08/ironic-misandry-why-feminists-joke-about-drinking-male-tears-and-banning-all-men.html)(That reaction is part of the point: “I enjoy that it bothers the men who don’t get it,” one Misandrist Book Club member told me. “It’s a good way to weed out cool dudes from the dumb bros.” As Zimmerman puts it: “The men who get annoyed by misandry jokes are in my experience universally brittle, insecure, humorless weenies with victim complexes,” while the “many intelligent, warm, confident feminist men in my life … mostly get the joke immediately and play along. They’re not worried I actually want to milk them for their tears.”)."
1.4.4.2.1.3. Pro: Many third-wave feminists [cloak](https://www.digitalamerica.org/collecting-male-tears-misandry-and-weaponized-femininity-on-the-internet-jillian-horowitz/)(All of these sites of misandry trade on the bizarre assumption that women who hate men are necessarily unfeminine; thus, the consciously cartoonish expressions of femininity function as both an in-joke and a strategic maneuver. When paired with articulations of ironic violence or earnest rage \(or something in between\), “misandry” is not only emptied of the meaning ascribed to it by men’s rights activists, but simultaneously weaponizes feminist anger and the devalued trappings of femininity. It turns objects coded as feminine into threats. Misandry becomes potentially dangerous, and liberatory, in its re-direction.) distaste for men within cute and kitsch aesthetics, in order to exploit stereotypes and excuse [reductive](https://thoughtcatalog.com/chelsea-fagan/2013/02/white-girl-privilege-and-the-problem-with-blaming-all-men/)(But the idea of leveraging a universal hatred against men, or allowing ourselves to feel as though there is a clear divide in terms of gendered power, and that it falls distinctly on the men vs. women line, fuels a slippery slope of profound privilege denying. Because to pretend as though the 22-year-old white female blogger talking about her hatred of men from the comfort of her prepaid dorm at an Ivy League school does not hold many tangible privileges over, say, the undocumented male worker who is cleaning the bathroom stalls of her building at night, is ludicrous. There are countless privileges she has over him, and countless points of access she has in our society that he will never see.) politics.
1.4.4.3. Con: Nearly 30% of men feel that feminist progress towards equality has come at the [detriment to men](https://www.cnbc.com/2020/07/13/nearly-30percent-of-men-say-gains-toward-gender-equality-has-come-at-their-expense.html).
1.4.4.3.1. Pro: A quarter of Republican women agree that progress towards gender equality has come [at the expense](https://www.pewresearch.org/social-trends/2020/07/07/a-century-after-women-gained-the-right-to-vote-majority-of-americans-see-work-to-do-on-gender-equality/)(About four-in-ten Republican men \(38%\) say women’s gains have come at the expense of men, compared with 25% of Republican women, 19% of Democratic men and 12% of Democratic women.) of men.
1.5. Con: Feminism's propensity to point out sexism where it does not exist eclipses other sociocultural issues.
1.5.1. Con: Society has been structured so as to privilege men over others. Feminism is legitimate in pushing through social reforms on widespread issues resulting from biases that [disproportionately](https://eu.usatoday.com/story/opinion/2020/09/23/we-must-bold-confront-economic-inequality-women-column/5850981002/)(Women have been disproportionately hurt by job losses during the pandemic. From February to May, 11.5 million women lost their jobs compared with 9 million men, triggering a “shecession” – an economic downturn where job and income losses are affecting women more than men.\n\nThe majority of job losses have been concentrated in sectors dominated by women: leisure and hospitality, education, health care and service. These jobs tend to be lower paying and have less flexibility or benefits, exacerbating many inequalities in the workforce.) affect women - these changes benefit many groups.
1.5.1.1. Pro: Justice-based forms of feminism are good for many marginalized groups, as they focus on ways to expose and alter harmful dynamics that are embedded within power structures \([p. 151](https://scholarship.law.uc.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?article=1012&context=fac_pubs)(These social justice feminists focused on labor reform, first\nin seeking reduced working hours and better working conditions\nand later a minimum wage. As discussed above, this agenda\nplaced these feminists squarely at odds with the National Women's Party's advocacy for an Equal Rights Amendment in the 1920s. As McGuire explains, the social justice feminists had turned their efforts to protecting women workers, with an eye toward expanding workplace protections to all employees.")\).
1.5.1.1.1. Con: Justice-based forms of feminism are not particularly common in the current era of [neoliberal](https://theconversation.com/how-neoliberalism-colonised-feminism-and-what-you-can-do-about-it-94856)(The movement for gender equality, then, is increasingly entangled with neoliberalism, which has mobilised feminism to advance political goals and enhance market value. Yet, at the same time, a different form of feminism has also unexpectedly gained popularity....\nI call this neoliberal feminism, since it recognises gender inequality \(differentiating itself from post-feminism, which focuses on individual women’s “empowerment” and “choice”, yet repudiates feminism\) while simultaneously denying that socioeconomic and cultural structures shape our lives.) [individualistic](https://www.bitchmedia.org/article/the-limits-of-my-body-my-choice)(In a recent piece for Vogue, Molly Jong-Fast spelled out that frustration. “We are on the precipice of the end of Roe and the beginning of a period of Republican legislation of women’s bodies, but this change comes steeped in irony,” she writes. “The same group that wants to make it impossible for you to end your pregnancy is furiously insistent that showing proof of vaccination should be illegal.” While the right’s unrelenting campaign to criminalize abortion is both infuriating and inhumane, it’s about time that feminists reframe the language we use to defend abortion. “My body, my choice” is highly individualistic and—in the end—fails to convey the ways we’re bound up with each other.") feminist action. The former group is often [harmed](https://blogs.exeter.ac.uk/genderatwork/2021/03/29/choice-feminism-in-the-age-of-instagram/)(Women should simply be empowered in their choices and all such empowerment is deemed feminist under the choice feminist banner.\n\nIt can be seen as arising out of criticisms levelled at feminism; that it is too radical, too exclusionary, and too judgemental \(Ferguson 2010\). Choice feminism, instead, does not really challenge society. It ensures that everyone can be included in feminism \(we wouldn’t want to lose any allies!\). It also guarantees that people cannot be judged since all choices are valid and, therefore, not open to moral indignation. Choice feminism is, thus, increasingly used by women in order to present their empowerment as feminist.) by the latter, as group action and critical social engagement are derided.
1.5.1.1.2. Pro: Native Americans [integrated](http://www.academia.edu/1330316/Decolonising_Feminism_Aboriginal_Women_and_the_Global_Sisterhood_) feminist advocacy strategies into many of their equal rights and anti-bigotry movements \([pp. 485-486](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/pdf/10.1177/2332649220908608)(Indigenous feminist theories seek to root out systems of colonialism, heteropatriarchy, and racism that serve settler nations and societies, with poignant implications for Indigenous, Black, and other women of color, youth, and queer/two-spirit persons \(Arvin et al. 2013\).3 Examining how these forces may be interruptible \(Simpson 2014\), Indigenous feminisms provide critical tools to understand reproductions of, and resistances to, uneven social relations taking place in progressive attempts at coalitional environmental partnerships.)\).
1.5.1.2. Pro: [Womanhood](https://philosophynow.org/issues/69/Becoming_A_Woman_Simone_de_Beauvoir_on_Female_Embodiment)(“One is not born, but rather becomes, a woman”\n...\nThe intertwinedness of body and mind helps explain women’s oppression. Women do not choose to think about their bodies and bodily processes negatively; rather they are forced to do so as a result of being embedded in a hostile patriarchal society. On this view the body is not just the thing we can prod and poke, it is shaped by a plethora of perceptions: if we feel bad about it, it becomes a ‘bad thing’; if we feel good about it, it becomes a ‘good thing’. But the way we think about it is not a matter of free choice unless we live in a society which gives space for that freedom.) becomes a salient aspect of political identity to organise around under feminism. This is effective as it targets more people than class or race would.
1.5.1.2.1. Con: Womanhood is not a monolith, nor is it treated as such by feminists. This limits the persuasiveness of identity as a rallying element.
1.5.1.2.1.1. Pro: [Wittig](https://www.dukeupress.edu/monique-wittig-1) argues that lesbians are not women due to their [unique social positioning](https://www.awid.org/news-and-analysis/we-were-never-gender-binary-its-time-reclaim-radical-lesbian-feminism)(Monique Wittig, a feminist theorist and self-identified radical lesbian, argued in her formative essay, The Straight Mind \(1979\), that “lesbians are not women”. The category of woman, she explained, has a meaning only in relation to the category of man, within a heterosexual system of thought and economy. This is everything but gender binary thinking.) that moves them outside of gender binaries. Analysing how gender is socially maintained is a [core aspect](https://www.weforum.org/agenda/2019/07/gender-where-feminist-movements-and-lgbti-movements-meet/) of feminist theory.
1.5.1.2.1.2. Con: Whilst womanhood is not monolithic, its [performative](https://aeon.co/ideas/gender-is-dead-long-live-gender-just-what-is-performativity)(Rather, Butler insisted that gender resides in repeated words and actions, words and actions that both shape and are shaped by the bodies of real, flesh-and-blood human beings. And crucially, such repetitions are rarely performed freely.\n\nWhat’s at stake in performativity stretches into the minutiae of the everyday. I was recently on a road trip with a group of friends, and one woman observed that she always lets her partner, a man, drive her car instead of doing so herself. Such an acquiescence feels feminine, she said. The question Butler would want us to ask is: does my friend do this because she is a woman, or does the act itself contribute to making her so?) elements fill a [referential function](https://aeon.co/ideas/how-playing-wittgensteinian-language-games-can-set-us-free)(These do something with words: soliciting, warning, forbidding. But Wittgenstein wanted to expose how ‘words are deeds’, that we do something every time we use a word. Moreover, what we do, we do in a world with others.\n\nThis was not facile word-nerdery. Wittgenstein was intent on bringing out how ‘the “speaking” of language is part of an activity, or form of life’. In Philosophical Investigations \(1953\), he used the example of two builders. A brickie calls ‘Slab!’ and his helper brings it. What’s going on here? The helper who responds is not like a dog reacting to an order. We are humans, the ones who live together in language in the particular way that we do, a way that involves distinctive social practices.) that allow people to build upon similarities. It is this amalgam of experiences that becomes salient and is mobilised by feminists to [great effect](https://theconversation.com/women-marching-worldwide-revive-a-long-sought-dream-global-feminism-71777).
1.5.1.2.2. Pro: Feminism has brought hundreds of thousands of women from all demographics and walks of life [together](http://content.time.com/time/specials/packages/article/0,28804,2088114_2087975_2087967,00.html) in [protests](http://content.time.com/time/specials/packages/article/0,28804,2088114_2087975_2087970,00.html) and [marches](http://content.time.com/time/specials/packages/article/0,28804,2088114_2087975_2087969,00.html), united by a common goal.
1.5.1.2.3. Con: Many feminist protests and marches lack a coherent cause or goal, as there are many different perspectives on womanhood and equality.
1.5.1.2.3.1. Con: [Protests](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/oct/30/pro-choice-supporters-hold-biggest-ever-protest-against-polish-government) often have [clear goals](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2020/12/29/argentina-senate-to-debate-a-bill-that-could-legalise-abortion)(“The feminist movement has worked with all political parties for all the laws that have to do with women’s rights,” Alanis told Al Jazeera. “We deserve to have a law that accompanies women at the hour of deciding to terminate a pregnancy.”) as, by nature, they react to [social issues](https://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/women/miss-world-protest-1970-womens-liberation-feminists-b1759081.html).
1.5.1.2.3.2. Pro: The [1968 white-women-led protest](https://www.morningsidecenter.org/teachable-moment/lessons/1968-miss-america-protest-and-its-significance-today) against Miss America clashed with the [counter pageant](https://www.history.com/this-day-in-history/the-first-black-miss-america-pageant-takes-place) hosted by Black women. One group sought to abolish pageants whilst the other wanted to expand beauty standards.
1.5.1.2.3.3. Pro: The [Women's March](https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2018/01/women-march-protests-thousands-rally-trump-180120195621901.html) featured participants who marched for many different reasons; some protested the defunding of Planned Parenthood, others unequal pay, and some the environment.
1.5.1.3. Con: Feminism has been claimed by groups that have incompatible methods and goals, hindering social reform.
1.5.1.3.1. Pro: As there is no body that regulates feminist thought, there are often [ideological incompatibilities](https://mic.com/articles/47955/feminism-defined-a-detailed-look-at-one-of-the-most-controversial-labels-today#.XHbXkcPIw) within movements. This can be [misused](https://www.irishtimes.com/opinion/women-can-t-be-told-anything-anymore-for-fear-of-offence-1.3252456) to justify intolerance.
1.5.1.3.2. Pro: Radical feminism prioritises the [breakdown](https://www.thoughtco.com/what-is-radical-feminism-3528997)(Radical feminism is a philosophy emphasizing the patriarchal roots of inequality between men and women, or, more specifically, the social domination of women by men. Radical feminism views patriarchy as dividing societal rights, privileges, and power primarily along the lines of sex, and as a result, oppressing women and privileging men.\n\nRadical feminism opposes existing political and social organization in general because it is inherently tied to patriarchy. Thus, radical feminists tend to be skeptical of political action within the current system and instead tend to focus on culture change that undermines patriarchy and associated hierarchical structures.) of social structures in order to remake them in a more equitable manner.
1.5.1.3.3. Pro: Liberal feminism encourages [equitable access](https://www.thoughtco.com/liberal-feminism-3529177)(Liberal feminism tends to rely on the state to gain equality—to see the state as the protector of individual rights.\n\nLiberal feminists, for example, support affirmative action legislation requiring employers and educational institutions to make special attempts to include women in the pool of applicants, on the assumption that past and current discrimination may simply overlook many qualified women applicants.) to existing power structures. It leverages legal systems in order to achieve equality, leaving the structure, its integration in society, and core aspects of social control remaining.
1.5.1.3.4. Con: Social reform comes from fostering [open dialogue](https://www.snhu.edu/about-us/newsroom/social-sciences/what-is-social-change)(When we listen respectfully to others who have different opinions and life experiences than our own, we take the first step in listening; we accept that there are myriad perspectives and points of view on most issues of concern. If we truly want to be a participant in real change, we cannot stop at acceptance, but we must have conversations that push and pull, that asks us to give and take. And if we are willing to do that, we can find those points of agreement and come together on them. We needn't concede those points that define our values but find ways to work together towards positive change that reflects our shared values. It is the art of principled compromise that has the power to create a more lasting change.) and giving people the tools to think critically about society; feminism could never make change if it was dogmatic and offered only one view.
1.5.1.3.4.1. Pro: People are often [driven](https://fs.blog/facts-are-not-enough/)(When we’re faced with a choice between being correct or being accepted, more often than not we choose the latter. Think of the last time you were with friends for dinner and someone said something that you not only disagreed with but was also factually incorrect. Did you correct them? Or did you sit there quietly, keeping your knowledge to yourself because you didn’t want to confront the person? It’s dangerous to argue in a group setting.) by social acceptance and seek to align their beliefs as such. If feminists are dogmatic then they may alienate allies and make themselves unpersuasive.
1.5.1.3.4.2. Con: By allowing the movement to be aligned with many divergent political stances, feminism has facilitated its co-option by forces that seek to [undermine](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2013/oct/14/feminism-capitalist-handmaiden-neoliberal)(I fear that the movement for women's liberation has become entangled in a dangerous liaison with neoliberal efforts to build a free-market society. That would explain how it came to pass that feminist ideas that once formed part of a radical worldview are increasingly expressed in individualist terms. Where feminists once criticised a society that promoted careerism, they now advise women to "lean in". A movement that once prioritised social solidarity now celebrates female entrepreneurs. A perspective that once valorised "care" and interdependence now encourages individual advancement and meritocracy.\n\nWhat lies behind this shift is a sea-change in the character of capitalism. The state-managed capitalism of the postwar era has given way to a new form of capitalism – "disorganised", globalising, neoliberal. Second-wave feminism emerged as a critique of the first but has become the handmaiden of the second.) its overall goal.
1.5.1.3.5. Con: By normalising different perspectives on how to solve issues and [encouraging experimentation](https://blogs.lse.ac.uk/usappblog/2016/08/08/why-political-disagreements-over-how-the-world-works-may-be-easier-to-solve-than-those-over-goals/)(The second difference we should look for is more “bottom up experimentation” with belief disagreement, or experimentation driven by the people charged with actually implementing change. If bureaucrats at the Environmental Protection Agency think we should control pollutants with a market-based permit system, even a very liberal Congress should let them try it out. If a new police chief wants to try body cameras to improve community relations, even a skeptical mayor should give them a free hand. Why is this? First, people are always more motivated to implement change that they “believe in.” Second, people are more easily persuaded that they are wrong when actually given the chance to try out their ideas and see them fail first-hand.), feminists may be able to persuade more people of their legitimacy.
1.5.1.3.5.1. Pro: Encouraging dialogue with the aim of perfect consensus hinders action and causes a loss of morale; this has been [weaponised](https://hbswk.hbs.edu/item/are-you-sabotaging-your-own-company)(During World War II, the predecessor to the US Central Intelligence Agency produced a secret field manual detailing how “citizen-saboteurs” could disrupt the operations of enemy organizations...\n“Advocate ‘caution.’ Be ‘reasonable’ and urge your fellow-conferees to be ‘reasonable’ and avoid haste, which might result in embarrassments or difficulties later on.”\n“Be worried about the propriety of every decision. Raise the question of whether such action as is contemplated lies within the jurisdiction of the group or whether it might conflict with the policy of some higher echelon.”) by those who oppose change historically, and should not be embedded as a normative practice by activist movements.
1.5.1.3.5.2. Con: Feminists should not encourage divergence as contradictions often [undermine](https://www.theguardian.com/news/2018/nov/29/why-we-stopped-trusting-elites-the-new-populism)(The problem today is that, across a number of crucial areas of public life, the basic intuitions of populists have been repeatedly verified. One of the main contributors to this has been the spread of digital technology, creating vast data trails with the latent potential to contradict public statements, and even undermine entire public institutions. Whereas it is impossible to conclusively prove that a politician is morally innocent or that a news report is undistorted, it is far easier to demonstrate the opposite. Scandals, leaks, whistleblowing and revelations of fraud all serve to confirm our worst suspicions. While trust relies on a leap of faith, distrust is supported by ever-mounting piles of evidence. And in Britain, this pile has been expanding much faster than many of us have been prepared to admit.) trust, particularly when scandals arise. Such strategies harm feminism in the long term.
1.5.2. Pro: As feminism is [polarising](https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2017/12/the-partisanship-of-feminism/548423/)(Since Trump’s election and the recent wave of sexual-harassment allegations, this partisan divide appears to have grown. In January, when PerryUndem asked whether “most women interpret innocent remarks as being sexist,” Republican women were 11 points more likely than Democratic men to say yes. When PerryUndem asked the question again this month, the gap had more than doubled to 23 points. A year ago, Democratic men were 30 points more likely than Republican women to strongly agree that “the country would be better off if we had more women in political office.” The gap is now 45 points.) and muddies the water around critical cultural issues, it is less capable of making material change than other movements.
1.5.2.1. Pro: Public interest in changing patriarchal structures is limited, as the issue does not have the same appeal as other social dilemmas.
1.5.2.1.1. Con: People are not offended by the knowledge that they are more wealthy and better fed than others. Instead, they react negatively when they are framed as responsible for the issue \([p. 1](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5641360/pdf/fpsyg-08-01770.pdf)(Thus, it is important to understand how people perceive injustices, how they react to them, how they give meaning to them, and also how they try to cope with them. The just-world theory \(e.g., Lerner, 1977, 1980\) emphasizes the adaptive function of the beliefs in a just world \(BJW\) to cope with injustices and inequalities. Usually, this contains aspects of believing that the world is a generally just place or that it is at least just for oneself or for others. Such coping or meaning-making mechanisms \(among others\) include cognitive re-evaluations of unjust events and justice-repairing through own just reactions, as well as negative and anti-social tendencies, norm-breaking behavior, and victim-blaming \(e.g., Dalbert, 2009; Hafer and Sutton, 2016\); the latter is especially relevant regarding persons with a strong general BJW.)\).
1.5.2.1.2. Pro: Privileged people are likely to be [defensive](https://slate.com/technology/2014/05/not-all-men-how-discussing-womens-issues-gets-derailed.html) when made aware of sexism, as they experience guilt and a sense of [persecution](https://www.harpersbazaar.com/uk/culture/a35457093/why-ive-given-up-on-talking-to-men-about-sexism/)(The men I have these discussions with don’t seem interested in genuinely understanding the female experience and how it is made more difficult by men, instead they are concerned only with convincing me \(or themselves?\) that they are one of the good ones. I can see the defensive hackles rising the moment the F word \(not that one, feminism\) is even mentioned in passing. There is a barrier of denial and often attempts to tell you, the woman, the person who is experiencing sexism, that you've got it wrong.). This limits the capacity of feminism to make change.
1.5.2.1.3. Con: Many support gender equality, and are [optimistic](https://www.pewresearch.org/global/2020/04/30/worldwide-optimism-about-future-of-gender-equality-even-as-many-see-advantages-for-men/) about achieving it in the future.
1.5.2.1.4. Pro: Most definitions of feminism include a recognition of political activism that some may [dislike](https://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/women/millennials-feminist-dont-identity-poll-refinery29-activism-a8492271.html)(Commenting on the survey results to The Independent, Dr Katherine Twamley, senior lecturer in sociology at University College London, says that while feminism does mean equality, many people may "affiliate the term feminist with ‘man-hating'.”\n\nSome people, she continues, "typify feminists as ‘shouty’ and ‘aggressive’, and do not see themselves nor want to be seen in that way.), even if they otherwise agree with the cause's central tenets.
1.5.2.1.4.1. Con: Women benefit from feminism, even when they don't support it. For example, at one stage, [90% of women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Association_Opposed_to_Woman_Suffrage#/media/File:Household_Hints.jpg) opposed women's suffrage, though it now enables more choice in democratic society.
1.5.2.1.4.2. Pro: Young women often perceive feminism as being for angry, [bra-burning lesbians](https://www.theguardian.com/world/2007/oct/24/gender.pop) \([pp. 5-6](http://etheses.lse.ac.uk/111/1/Scharff_Young_women's_disidentification_with_feminism.pdf)(Feminists were overwhelmingly portrayed and constructed as unfeminine, man-hating, and lesbian. Although the respondents could not name any concrete examples of feminists who corresponded to this stereotype, the construction of 'the feminist' haunted their accounts.)\). This alienates them from the movement as they don't wish to face those negative associations.
1.5.2.1.4.3. Pro: [Polls](https://www.vox.com/2015/4/8/8372417/feminist-gender-equality-poll) in the US suggest that as few as 18% of women call themselves feminists. This is despite more than two-thirds of women in the country supporting equality of the sexes.
1.5.2.1.4.3.1. Pro: Older women are [far less likely](https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2020/07/07/61-of-u-s-women-say-feminist-describes-them-well-many-see-feminism-as-empowering-polarizing/)(Majorities of women across age groups say “feminist” describes them at least somewhat well, but those ages 50 to 64 are the least likely to say it describes them very well. Only 12% in this age group say this, compared with 27% of women ages 18 to 29, 19% of women ages 30 to 49 and 20% of women 65 and older.) to support feminism than newer generations.
1.5.2.1.4.3.2. Con: Recent statistics indicate that as many as [61%](https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2020/07/07/61-of-u-s-women-say-feminist-describes-them-well-many-see-feminism-as-empowering-polarizing/) of US women identify as feminists.
1.5.2.2. Con: Feminism has [facilitated](https://www.britannica.com/topic/feminism/The-suffrage-movement) historical progress for gender parity, therefore any [polarisation](https://www.caixabankresearch.com/en/economics-markets/public-sector/political-polarisation-phenomenon-should-be-everyones-lips)(The degree of political polarisation in a society is a key variable that quantifies the extent to which public opinion is split into two opposing extremes. This is a very important variable to take into account: the greater the polarisation, the more difficult it is to generate a broad consensus amon groups with different views in order to undertake reforms that allow society to achieve progress. As such, a high degree of polarisation can lead to irreconcilable positions, making it difficult to reach agreements.) caused by the movement is likely to be minimal.
1.5.2.2.1. Con: Feminism's history does not justify its evolution into a modern [divisive force](https://time.com/3028827/women-against-feminism-gets-it-right/). There is no reason to believe that the positive actions of the past will be replicated in the future.
1.5.2.2.2. Pro: There is an international network of feminist [activism](http://www.unwomen.org/en/news/stories/2019/3/compilation-womens-activism-thats-changed-the-world) used to combat injustice. This can be used to share best practices and methods of persuading people.
1.5.2.2.3. Pro: There is a whole body of feminist [literature](https://www.harpersbazaar.com/culture/art-books-music/g19412213/best-feminist-books-every-woman-must-read/) and theory which can inform activists and help them to side-step the kinds of poor messaging that facilitate polarisation.
1.5.2.2.4. Con: Effective system change can be [motivated](https://www.givingwhatwecan.org/what-is-effective-altruism/)(Effective altruism is:\n \(i\) the use of evidence and careful reasoning to work out how to maximize the good with a given unit of resources, tentatively understanding ‘the good’ in impartial welfarist terms, and\n \(ii\) the use of the findings from \(i\) to try to improve the world.\n\nThe first part of the definition \(i\) refers to effective altruism as an intellectual project \(or ‘research field’\); and the second part \(ii\) refers to effective altruism as a practical project \(or ‘social movement’\).\n\nThe effective altruism community \(the 'social movement'\) is a collection of people and organisations who use their resources \(e.g. money, time, social capital\) on the project of trying to effectively improve the world.) through close monitoring and considerate donation. This is not exclusive to feminism, so change is possible through many approaches.
1.5.2.3. Con: Young women increasingly engage with various forms of feminism on social media, spreading ideas through their offline networks \([p. 4](https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/pdf/10.1177/2056305119867442)(Girls and women use digital platforms to explore their emerging feminist identities \(Keller, 2015, 2016\), create feminist solidarity and collectivities \(Keller et al., 2018; Retallack et al., 2016\), cultivate new modes of feminist cultural critique \(Rentschler & Thrift, 2015\), challenge normative beauty and body standards \(Pham, 2015\), and learn, as well as teach, feminist history \(Keller, 2015\).)\). This innovative approach can facilitate change, by passing polarisation.
1.5.2.3.1. Con: The [Instagram infographic industrial complex](https://lithiumagazine.com/2020/09/14/unpacking-the-instagram-infographic-industrial-complex/) and general [memeification](https://www.nupoliticalreview.com/2020/11/03/no-justice-for-black-women-the-memeification-of-breonna-taylor/) of social issues may dilute their importance, encouraging idle sharing over actions that bring change.
1.5.2.3.2. Pro: Social media activism [encourages](https://www.berghahnjournals.com/view/journals/girlhood-studies/11/2/ghs110205.xml?pdfVersion=true)(In these and other recent examples, teen feminists are troubling what Sinikka Aapola et al. \(2005\) think of as engrained constructions of youth, particularly girls, as lacking in political agency. Social media are opening spheres of political participation previously defined, as Anita Harris \(2010\) has pointed out, strictly through formal processes like voting in elections. Indeed, the fourth wave of feminism is characterized by its digital collectivity and youth-driven presence, as Sowards and Renegar \(2006\) detail. Additionally, Retallack et al. write that, despite the ostensible neoliberalized depoliticization of contemporary society, through digital politics “a renewed and collectivized feminism has re-entered political and civic life” \(2016: 5\) and is increasingly present in schools.) young women to create communities. This mobilisation is incredibly important as it encourages civic engagement amongst the [traditionally disenfranchised](https://blogs.lse.ac.uk/politicsandpolicy/young-women-face-gender-specific-challenges-that-limit-their-political-participation/).
1.5.2.4. Pro: Despite feminist campaigns against [rape culture](https://www.marshall.edu/wcenter/sexual-assault/rape-culture/), some people still consider it to be a [myth](https://www.irishtimes.com/opinion/flawed-notion-of-rape-culture-is-lacking-in-logic-1.3283053).
1.5.2.4.1. Con: Some [ignore](https://www.aljazeera.com/features/2021/11/2/what-we-fear-as-women)(Anna Bull from the 1752 Group explained that in her experience universities refuse to join the dots.\n\n“They are mistaking the nature of sexual harassment because they’re not understanding that multiple people are going to be targeted at the same time,” she says, adding: “We have to kind of work on the assumption that even if only one person reports, that other students and staff are probably being targeted, either at the same time or in subsequent years.”) allegations of sexual misconduct/assault or [defend](https://www.harpersbazaar.com/culture/politics/a13090746/women-defend-men-sexual-assault/) the accused, [instead of making changes](https://www.buzzfeednews.com/article/ryanmac/tech-men-accused-sexual-misconduct-new-jobs-metoo)(That frustration was shared by many of the women, who felt that some of the tech leaders now making comebacks don’t seem genuinely repentant and lack self-recognition for what they’ve done or who they’ve hurt. Chou suggested some of the accused men making comebacks are paying lip service to diversity and inclusion because of the optics and to “brandwash” their names. In one instance, a man with public allegations of sexual misconduct offered to donate $5 million to a nonprofit focused on improving diversity that one of the women was advising, but only on the condition that his gift be made public.) that could mitigate future harm.
1.5.2.4.1.1. Pro: Due to the legal principle of "innocent until proven guilty," it is [common](https://www.theguardian.com/society/2013/apr/13/rape-sexual-assault-frances-andrade-court)(Other rape and sexual assault victims who have tried, with various degrees of success, to take cases to court are familiar with the distressing experience of having their evidence torn apart. Usually when you report a crime, you expect to be believed. Victims of burglary do not have to prove that they have been burgled or to justify their behaviour before the burglary. With rape and sexual assault allegations, victims still find themselves subjected to hostile questioning.) for victims in rape trials to be considered untruthful until proven otherwise.
1.5.2.4.1.2. Pro: Rapists, especially upper-class white men, receive [minimal punishment](https://www.cosmopolitan.com/uk/reports/a32777894/white-privilege-brock-turner-george-floyd/)(Following a trial, Turner was found guilty of the following charges: assault with intent to rape an intoxicated woman; sexually penetrating an intoxicated person with a foreign object; and sexually penetrating an unconscious person with a foreign object. As if the unusually light sentence wasn't concerning enough, he was then released three months early, in September 2016, for 'good behaviour'.) despite the overwhelming amount of evidence against them.
1.5.2.4.1.3. Con: Often people push for removing those accused of sexual misconduct from their workplace, yet this flies in the face of HR [best practices](https://www.thebalancecareers.com/how-to-address-an-employee-sexual-harassment-complaint-1916862).
1.5.2.4.1.4. Con: While reactions to sexual assault claims can be mishandled, [campaigns](https://www.scotland.police.uk/what-s-happening/news/2021/october/police-scotland-launches-new-campaign-urging-men-to-call-time-on-sexual-crime/) to change cultural norms and prevent harm are increasingly common and undermine the possible norms of rape culture.
1.5.2.4.2. Pro: Feminists inflate sexual assault statistics in order to promote the idea of rape culture.
1.5.2.4.2.1. Con: A third of university age men did not [recognise](http://www.telegraph.co.uk/men/thinking-man/11362194/Why-students-dont-understand-what-counts-as-rape.html) rape without the label, and said that they would commit those acts if there were no consequences. This indicates a culture where rape is normalised.
1.5.2.4.2.1.1. Pro: Films like [Revenge of the Nerds](https://variety.com/2020/film/news/revenge-of-the-nerds-reboot-lucas-brothers-1234854322/)(The upcoming version won’t be a remake of the 1984 comedy, which hasn’t aged all that well and has been criticized in recent years for depictions of rape. This may create a cognitive disconnect between the term rape and the actions involved.
1.5.2.4.2.2. Con: Only a [small minority](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-45565684) of sexual assault accusations are proven to be false.
1.5.2.4.2.2.1. Pro: Sexual assault reporting is [incredibly difficult](https://www.abc.net.au/triplej/programs/hack/false-rape-allegations-myths/13281852)(The idea that someone might make up an allegation to 'get back' at someone?\n\n"How true is that, when most of these cases aren't being reported and even for those that are reported, something like 2 per cent end up with a successful conviction," said Dr Fileborn.\n\n"So is that worth the payoff? It's illogical to suggest that survivors are somehow getting some benefit from from making a false report - it's completely odds with what we know about the reality of reporting and disclosing sexual violence."\nFear of not being believed makes it harder for victims to come forward.), regardless of how commonly it is discussed in the media. This discourages false reporting.
1.5.2.4.2.2.2. Con: [Two to ten percent](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-45565684)(Over the past 20 years, only 2-10% of rape accusations...are proven to be fake, argue the authors of a 2010 US study.\n\nThat figure does not include any unsubstantiated accusations where an investigation was unable to prove a sexual assault occurred, so an accurate figure for the total remains unknown.\n\nOther studies have figures in the same range. The FBI has put the number of "unfounded" rapes - those determined to be false after investigation - at 8%.) may be a small percentage of overall sexual assault allegations, yet it is still significant when people consider the scale of harm to those falsely accused.
1.5.2.4.2.2.3. Pro: [Very few](https://www.thecut.com/2021/09/book-excerpt-the-right-to-sex-by-amia-srinivasan.html)(In the U.K. Home Office study, the police judged 216 of 2,643 complaints false. In those 216 cases, the complainants had named a total of 39 suspects; six of these suspects were arrested, and charges were brought against two of them; in both cases, the charges were eventually dropped. So, in the final analysis, bearing in mind that the Home Office counted only a third as many false accusations as the police, just 0.23 percent of rape reports led to a false arrest, and only 0.07 percent of rape reports led to a man being falsely charged with rape; none resulted in wrongful conviction.) false sexual assault allegations are acted upon by police, and even fewer have legal consequences.
1.5.2.4.2.2.4. Con: Only about [3.3% of reported rapes](https://www.aljazeera.com/opinions/2020/5/7/why-do-so-few-rapes-result-in-a-conviction)(In 2017-18, there were 54,045 rapes reported and 2,635 convictions – a conviction rate of 4.9 percent. The following year, there were 58,657 rapes reported and 1,925 convictions – a conviction rate of just 3.3 percent.) result in a felony conviction in the United Kingdom.
1.5.2.4.2.3. Pro: Feminists suggest that one in four women on US college campuses have been raped, though this is disputed, and may be as low as [one in fifty](https://www.aei.org/carpe-diem/new-justice-department-study-reveals-1-52-6-college-women-victims-rapesexual-assault/)(What might be the most important statistic...is that only about 1 in 41 women were victims of rape or sexual assault \(threatened, completed and attempted; and reported and unreported\) while in college for four years during the entire period investigated from 1995 to 2013, based on this analysis:\n\n6.1 women per 1,000 = “1 in 163.9 women” per year, and over four years attending college would then be = “1 in 41 women” while in college. \n\nBecause the victimization rate has been trending downward, that same analysis using data from the last four years \(2010 to 2013\) reveals that 1 in 52.6 women have been sexually assaulted or raped in recent years.).

1.5.2.4.2.5.
