1.5.2.4.2.5.1. Con: In a 2021 survey, [97%](https://www.openaccessgovernment.org/97-of-women-in-the-uk/105940/)(An investigation by UN Women UK found that 97% of women aged 18-24 have been sexually harassed, with a further 96% not reporting those situations because of the belief that it would not change anything) of UK women aged between 18-24 reported sexual harassment. Only [67%](https://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/women/percentage-women-feminist-young-womens-trust-survey-a9208051.html)(More than two thirds \(67 per cent\) of women aged 18-24 in the UK now identify as feminist, the equivalent to almost 1.8 million women.) identify as feminists, so this is unlikely to be inflated through collusion.
1.5.2.4.2.5.2. Pro: Companies that sell rape prevention devices encourage [fear](https://theconversation.com/anti-rape-devices-may-have-their-uses-but-they-dont-address-the-ultimate-problem-123011) and an [individualised](https://www.gawker.com/culture/true-crime-is-rotting-our-brains)(A study conducted by the University of Pennsylvania found that fear of crime and violence on television have both increased over time, despite crime rates declining, and that women reported more fear of crime on surveys than men. True crime runs on heightened emotion and fear, convincing people, and especially women, that every stranger is a possible murderer...“Be aware of your surroundings and don’t trust strangers” is not particularly helpful advice for avoiding the one scenario in which women are most likely to actually be murdered: by their partner. It’s victim blaming dressed up in empowerment; no one questions someone killed in a car accident, but if a woman is murdered her story becomes a precaution.) response to crime. This undermines change in the long term.
1.5.2.4.3. Pro: There is no discussion of "[murder culture](https://www.newstatesman.com/culture/2013/09/how-are-rape-jokes-different-murder-jokes-let-me-count-ways)" or other cultures related to crime as they are accepted by society. Were people to accept the prevalance of rape then the focus could move from proving a rape culture exists to ameliorating the issue.
1.5.2.4.4. Con: The trivialisation of 'rape' to become a flippant term may lead to a [normalisation](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0747563216304642) of [victim blaming](https://choma.co.za/articles/438/rape-culture-the-dangers-of-victim-blaming)(Victim blaming is when a victim of rape is told to take responsibility for the crime, or that both the victim and the rapist should be equally blamed, which is wrong and creates the false idea that rape is something the victim is responsible for or something people can easily avoid.) which forms a [significant part](https://eu.savannahnow.com/story/opinion/2021/05/11/rape-culture-ingrained-society-through-media-jokes-and-victim-blaming-sexual-assault-perpetrator/4995784001/)(Blaming victims for traumatic experiences not only worsens their trauma but also discourages others from speaking out. Some even begin blaming themselves.\n\nIn order to take a stand against rape culture, society needs to stop victim blaming. Changing mindsets, policymaking, and holding perpetrators accountable for their actions is the only way that this problem can be tackled.) of rape culture.
1.5.2.4.4.1. Pro: During the [Belfast Rape Trial](http://www.irishtimes.com/news/crime-and-law/inside-court-12-the-complete-story-of-the-belfast-rape-trial-1.3443620?mode=amp), the alleged victim was asked if she had been staring at the defendant on the night of the incident - a clear example of victim blaming.
1.5.2.4.4.2. Con: There are a number of pejorative terms used by members of society that do not [normalize](https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2021/11/china-academic-freedom-cultural-revolution-cancel-culture/620777/) harmful actions or behaviors, though they may not be reclamatory per se \([p. 3](https://www.researchgate.net/profile/Robin-Jeshion/publication/337944356_Pride_and_Prejudiced_On_the_Reclamation_of_Slurs/links/5df6e6474585159aa4808395/Pride-and-Prejudiced-On-the-Reclamation-of-Slurs.pdf)(Acts of reclamation strive for a reversal of social norms by breaking established linguistic conventions on an expression or representation that manifests and whose use reinforces those norms. Typically, the norms systematically oppress or stigmatize a group. In initial acts of reclamation, speakers intentionally break and alter the linguistic conventions to reverse the oppressive social norms the \nrepresentations manifest. Imitators of the initial reclaimers may lack such intentions yet their uses may still ‘be part of the movement’, as Cassie Herbert aptly notes. \(Herbert 2015, 135\) But in all the speech acts in \(1\)-\(4\), the speakers do not morph or even aim to morph any linguistic conventions at all. So even though Queen Lattifah’s song absolutely contributes to the feminist empowerment norm-shifting that reclamation of ‘bitch’ strives for, \(2\) is not a reclamatory act because it leaves prevailing linguistic conventions governing ‘bitch’ intact.)\).

1.5.2.4.4.4. 1.5.2.4.4.5. Pro: Having entered the [pop culture lexicon](https://www.youthkiawaaz.com/2014/04/using-rape-slang-glorifies-horrific-culture/) as a slang term - referring to an act of aggression or destruction against a person or group of people - the word 'rape' is often [trivialised](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2013/nov/13/trivialising-rape-endangers-women-ranjit-sinha). It is commonly used in male-dominated spaces like sports or video game competitions.
1.5.3. 1.5.3.1. Pro: In many cases where feminists identify sexism, it is often [very difficult](https://slate.com/human-interest/2014/05/yesallwomen-in-the-wake-of-elliot-rodger-why-its-so-hard-for-men-to-recognize-misogyny.html) for anyone unaccustomed to perceiving these issues to notice.
1.5.3.1.1. 1.5.3.1.3. Pro: Often patriarchy is [embedded](https://usa.streetsblog.org/2019/08/29/all-the-ways-u-s-transport-system-is-biased-against-women/)(Transportation engineers — who by the way are overwhelmingly men — have long held up work commuting as the standard by which to base planning decisions.\n\nBut women make many more trips than men daily, and they commute shorter distances on average. According to the American Enterprise Institute, they spend 31 percent less time commuting in the U.S. then men. In addition, they are often responsible for more caregiving and retail trips.\n\nU.S. transport planning has for ages privileged long trips over short. Big highway expansion projects that serve suburban commuters over more small scale projects that facilitate safer, faster short-distance travel.) within bureaucratic systems, which can be difficult to notice as being harmful, as their decision making standards are often implicit.
1.5.3.2. Con: Actions can be interpreted as sexist, regardless of intent. This speaks to the world view of the interpreter instead of the nature of the action itself.
1.5.3.2.1. Pro: People often have [priors](https://oxford.universitypressscholarship.com/view/10.1093/oso/9780198869153.001.0001/oso-9780198869153-chapter-4)(The expectation that rules will be act-based might be explained as a prior that is itself the result of earlier learning. In particular, given that most rules that people have learned are act-based rules, the prior for act-based rules might be acquired through a process of overhypothesis construction.) that they use to evaluate the intent, [context](https://link.springer.com/chapter/10.1057/9780230375093_4)(A deictic sentence such as: ‘I am hungry’ would be characterized by having a context-dependent meaning in the sense that the complete meaning conveyed by using the sentence varies systematically with the context of use \(and requires knowledge of the context\). In contrast, a non-deictic sentence such as: ‘Ice floats on water’ would be characterized by having a context-independent meaning in the sense that the meaning conveyed by using the sentence does not vary with the context of use \(and does not require knowledge of the context\). The study of context-dependent meaning is then said to belong to pragmatics, while the study of context-independent meaning belongs to semantics, which studies meaning in abstraction from the context of use.), and meaning of others; the assumed meaning may be quite [different](https://www.washingtonexaminer.com/weekly-standard/cultural-disconnect)(Cultural Disconnect may be defined as a phenomenon that occurs when people begin to talk past each other because they have been formed, and informed, by different cultures and are not fully aware of the fact. For long, painful moments, people who have been Culturally Disconnected continue to make points and ripostes in what they take to be a shared language, when, after all, they have ascribed different meanings to words belonging to a common vocabulary.) from the original intention.
1.5.3.2.2. Con: Actions can be sexist [without intent](https://www.theguardian.com/sustainable-business/2016/sep/02/unconscious-bias-most-women-believe-sexism-still-exists-but-most-men-disagree)(Double standards are so embedded in our culture we often don’t recognise when we’re reinforcing them. For instance, expecting our daughters to show more self-control and politeness than our sons \(after all, “boys will be boys”\). Or judging women who fail to retain their youthful looks and figure far more harshly than we judge men. Or the idea we have about boys and girls “natural” capabilities and in the workplace, where men tend to be promoted more on potential and women more on performance. Even worse when high-performing women are passed over due to untested assumptions such as “she’ll probably have babies soon and won’t want the pressure!”); this may arise through miscommunication, cultural misunderstanding, or the normalisation of sexism socially, not necessarily from the interpreter.
1.5.3.2.3. Con: Action [matters more](https://blogs.scientificamerican.com/psysociety/e2809cbut-i-didne28099t-mean-ite2809d-why-ite28099s-so-hard-to-prioritize-impacts-over-intents/)(As long as we continue to engage with societal issues in which there is an agent with intentions and a patient receiving the consequences of those actions, we must all struggle to tease apart these issues of intent and impact. We must all focus on how actions that harm others -- regardless of intent -- need to be addressed, not pushed under the rug because the agent "didn't mean" to do anything wrong.) than intention, especially when associated with systematic disadvantage. Oppressive actions may be carried out with the best intentions.
1.5.3.3. Pro: Some have a vested interest in ignoring the patriarchy, which leads them to disregard feminists' evidence for sexism.

People tend to seek consistency in their attitudes and perceptions, so this conflict causes feelings of unease or discomfort.\n\nThis inconsistency between what people believe and how they behave motivates people to engage in actions that will help minimize feelings of discomfort. People attempt to relieve this tension in different ways, such as by rejecting, explaining away, or avoiding new information.) belief that the system was working for them, which has been upended.

Pro: Justifications for maintaining the patriarchy are [deeply embedded](https://www.theguardian.com/books/2019/nov/02/smashing-the-patriarchy-why-theres-nothing-natural-about-male-supremacy)(According to a variety of high-profile figures \(mainly male, mainly psychologists\), bolstered by professorships and no shortage of disciples, there are important biological reasons for why men and women have different roles and status in our society...\n\nAnd yet, only a tiny percent \(between 0 and 8%\) of individual men and women turn out to have a typically “male” or “female” brain. 1.5.3.4. 1.5.3.4.2. Pro: Calls to victimhood have become mechanisms for the subversion of power by hegemonic groups, disrupting activisms that previously undermined them \([p. 4](http://eprints.lse.ac.uk/107926/1/Introduction_to_special_issue._The_logic_of_victimhood.pdf)(One key feature of this contemporary public discourse is the reversal of victimhood claims, so that those who speak out on the injustices they have suffered are now accused as oppressors by those in positions of power \(Cole, 2007\). Even though the link between claims to suffering and positions of power can never be completely fixed, we argue that victimhood today operates as a ‘master’ signifier, a dominant communicative logic that relies on auxillary vocabularies – of injured white masculinity, celebrated survivorship or heroic sacrifice – to reclaim power for the powerful and retrench existing hegemonic arrangements in liberal polities. Whether it is authoritarian populists, networked misogynists or imperialist state actors, this logic of weaponized victimhood is, we contend, a crucial site of political struggle and, as such, a scholarly terrain of urgent interrogation.)\).

For example, many medical professionals in the US believe that black patients are less susceptible to pain, and less likely to comply with medical advice than white patients. The quick-fire judgements of police officers are also very fraught; some research suggests that US police instinctively see darker faces as being more criminal. 1.5.4.3.1.1.1. Pro: Up until relatively recently, [inheritance](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.1002/9781118430873.est0290)(Primogeniture is an inheritance rule that assigns the entire family estate to the first son. In Europe primogeniture emerged in the thirteenth century and kept spreading up to the eighteenth century. It was most common among the feudal nobility and whenever land represented the primary source of wealth. It predominated in England, Scandinavia, and parts of France, Germany, Spain, and Italy. Outside Europe, it was adopted in Japan and the southern American colonies, while partition prevailed in sub-Saharan Africa and Islamic regions. The French revolution abolished primogeniture and during the nineteenth century most European countries followed suit.) in Europe was passed to the eldest male heir under a system known as primogeniture. 1.5.4.3.1.2.1. This result is a consequence of two findings: \(i\) part-time wages are lower than full-time wages, and \(ii\) the majority of part-time workers are women. In aggregation, this brings down the average female wage, leading to a larger aggregate gender wage gap. This was further linked to a differential selection by gender into full-time and part-time work, with women of higher earnings potential being overrepresented in the pool of part-time workers, resulting in no gender pay gap in the part-time worker category. Policies targeted at encouraging full-time employment for women should therefore reduce the gender wage gap.), feminists may lead people away from overall system reform.

1.5.4.3.2.3. Pro: Religions, like [Sikhism](https://www.bbc.co.uk/bitesize/guides/zjq9dxs/revision/8)(Many Sikhs believe in the oneness of humanity. This is the belief that all humans are equal because they were all created by Waheguru. Sikhs also believe that Waheguru is present in every individual as the atma or divine spark. This means that they believe all humans should be treated respectfully and that they should not try to convert other people to Sikhism. This belief is called egalitarianism.), [Christianity](https://theconversation.com/explainer-why-some-churches-teach-that-women-are-separate-but-equal-64305)(Some critical scholarship supports an alternative position known as “egalitarianism”. Those who hold to the egalitarian position regard women and men as fully equal, and believe there should be no gender-based restrictions upon which roles women can exercise in families, societies, or churches.\n\nNew Testament scholar Ben Witherington III argues that the passages in 1 Timothy and 1 Corinthians quoted above were intended to correct particular problems in the specific churches they were addressed to, and should not be regarded as a ban on women speaking in churches for all time.\n\nOthers emphasise the precedence of other texts, such as Paul’s statement in Galatians 3:28 that there is “neither male nor female” in the faith.), and [Judaism](https://www.timesofisrael.com/the-jewish-egalitarian-revolution-that-almost-was-in-renaissance-italy/)(What is most remarkable, said Marx, the Rabbi Aaron D. Panken Professor of Liturgy and Midrash, is that in his choice of language, scribe Farissol uniquely addressed the high-status Hebrew-literate female owners of these prayer books and applied and adapted the liturgy to their needs.\n\nThrough these prayer books and other texts of the era, we encounter other surprisingly egalitarian roles filled by women: female scribes, a poetess who translated liturgy from Hebrew to Italian, and the owners of Farissol’s works, who praised God for being made women, and not men.), often have egalitarian interpretations; these could be co-opted by egalitarians to encourage change, even in a secular society.
1.5.4.3.3. Con: [Egalitarianism](https://www.genderscilab.org/blog/gender-equality-does-not-equal-gender-neutrality)(Taking implicit attitudes into account is important because even if we hold egalitarian beliefs, we may still have sexist implicit associations that may influence our behavior.15 As an example of how implicit bias likely matters for women in STEM, consider the finding that faculty in Biology, Chemistry, and Physics at six highly-ranked research-intensive universities in the United States rated a male applicant for a lab manager position as more competent and hirable than a woman with an identical CV, proposed a higher starting salary for him, and offered him more mentoring.13 This hiring scenario highlights how implicit attitudes about gender and science continue to have repercussions for women \(and other folks, though in different ways\) in the United States, a fairly high-GGGI country.) may be unfocussed, and therefore blind to the ways in which gender shapes the treatment of people. Without a movement to address gendered disparities, they could be ignored.
1.5.4.3.3.1. Pro: Women have historically been regarded as an [object of exchange](https://psychcentral.com/lib/women-as-property-an-existential-challenge-in-psychotherapy-part-2#1) between men. If women didn't organise around gender, it would be difficult to make changes to these systems.
1.5.4.3.3.2. Con: It is unclear why womanhood is a unique aspect of identity that could not be covered by race or [class sensitive approaches](https://newrepublic.com/article/154996/myth-class-reductionism)(Black, female, and trans people tend to be disproportionately working class. So any measure to advance broad downward economic redistribution—from Medicare for All to a $15 hourly minimum wage—can’t coherently be said to thwart the interests of women, racial minorities, or other identity groups. What’s more, this brand of class denialism artificially separates race, gender, and other ascriptive identities from the basic dynamics of American capitalism. True, African Americans, Latinos, and women are disproportionately poor or working class due to a long history of racial and gender discrimination in labor and housing markets—conditions that have worsened alongside the postwar deindustrialization of American cities. But this means that these populations would benefit disproportionately from initiatives geared to improve the circumstances of poor and working-class people in general.).
1.5.4.3.4. Con: Due to the changes that feminism has driven, women are now [increasingly](https://www.theguardian.com/global-development/2014/sep/29/women-better-off-far-from-equal-men) able to climb to the top of society. This campaigning is necessary to reduce sexism.
1.5.4.3.4.1. Pro: Feminist support enables and empowers female politicians to be [more effective](https://gsdrc.org/document-library/quotas-add-women-and-stir/)(Women political representatives are most effective where a strong and engaged local feminist movement supports them, and where they have a strong sense of representing a constituency.) in their roles, improving life for many women.
1.5.4.3.4.1.1. Pro: Boston [elected](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2021/nov/03/michelle-wu-boston-mayor-first-woman-person-of-color) its first woman of color as mayor, mainly through the support of the progressive feminist movement. Her policies may greatly [improve](https://www.wgbh.org/news/politics/2021/09/23/michelle-wu-wants-to-change-more-than-policies-in-boston-shes-aiming-to-change-its-politics-too)(Recently, Boston officials declared a plan to transfer some people experiencing homelessness from Mass. and Cass to live in a hotel in Revere, a move that was met with resistance from that city's mayor. Wu said she supports plans that would decentralize services across the city and neighboring municipalities, but said she would be more transparent about her plans as mayor.\n...\n"I have said that, in my first 100 days, an immediate priority will be ensuring that we're reviewing every parcel of city-owned land, every building where we could retrofit supportive housing quickly and then work to very quickly set up ferry service so that we can reactivate the island for treatment as well," she said.) life for Bostonians.
1.5.4.3.4.1.2. Con: Female politicians may [attempt](https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2020/jan/24/hillary-clinton-feminist-icon-jessa-crispin) to sell themselves as feminist icons, despite not contributing to the movement, which may distort voter perceptions to negative ends.
1.5.4.3.4.1.3. Pro: Empowering women to take political roles may make societies [more caring](https://www.kcl.ac.uk/news/women-political-leaders-key-to-more-equal-and-caring-societies) and healthier.
1.5.4.3.4.1.4. Con: Right-wing female candidates often pander to women voters, appearing to [espouse](https://edition.cnn.com/2020/08/26/opinions/republican-fake-feminism-might-work-filipovic/index.html) feminist ideals in order to garner more votes.
1.5.4.3.4.2. Con: Women hold fewer positions of power because of their life choices, rather than systemic discrimination. Therefore, feminism has not corrected any injustice by changing preferences.
1.5.4.3.4.2.1. Pro: Though feminists suggest that there is a wage gap, its existence is [disputed](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/christina-hoff-sommers/wage-gap_b_2073804.html) and is unlikely to have come from sexist origins.
1.5.4.3.4.2.1.1. Con: [EU figures](http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/index.php/Gender_pay_gap_statistics) show an \(unadjusted\) average 16.2% gap \(2016, gross hourly earnings\).
1.5.4.3.4.2.1.2. Pro: [Childbearing](https://www.vox.com/2018/2/19/17018380/gender-wage-gap-childcare-penalty), which contributes significantly to the pay gap, is determined by physiology and not influenced by historic or societal sexism.
1.5.4.3.4.2.1.3. Con: A [2018 survey](https://www.americanprogress.org/issues/women/reports/2020/03/24/482141/quick-facts-gender-wage-gap/)(Analyzing the most recent Census Bureau data from 2018, women of all races earned, on average, just 82 cents for every $1 earned by men of all races.3 This calculation is the ratio of median annual earnings for women working full time, year round to those of their male counterparts, and it translates to a gender wage gap of 18 cents. When talking about the wage gap for women, it is important to highlight that there are significant differences by race and ethnicity. The wage gap is larger for most women of color.) of women in the US indicated that on average they earn 18 cents less per dollar than their male peers.
1.5.4.3.4.2.1.4. Con: Factors such as role or hours are [determined](https://ec.europa.eu/info/policies/justice-and-fundamental-rights/gender-equality/equal-pay/causes-unequal-pay-between-men-and-women_en) by societal or historical sexism, and continue to maintain or worsen the pay gap.
1.5.4.3.4.2.1.4.1. Pro: Women are [paid less](http://www.yalescientific.org/2013/02/john-vs-jennifer-a-battle-of-the-sexes/) for doing the same jobs with the same experience; the only difference therefore is due to sexism.
1.5.4.3.4.2.1.4.2. Pro: There may not be a huge gap when you compare men and women in the same job, but [female-dominated jobs](https://timewise.co.uk/article/article-real-reasons-behind-gender-pay-gap/)(We know that many of the more poorly-paid occupations are those traditionally done by women, requiring skills traditionally regarded as ‘feminine’, such as people skills and caring skills. So women ‘choose’ to work as nurses, teachers, or shop assistants, while men ‘choose’ to be surgeons, construction workers or engineers. The issue here is that we undervalue traditionally female skills – and that will take a while to change.\n\nBut there is also a perceived wisdom that women choose low-paid occupations because they offer more flexibility, or are more family-friendly. Again, the perception that it is a choice to prioritise children over paid work, rather than being due to a lack of viable alternatives, positions the gender pay gap as a fact of life, and releases employers from responsibility for changing it.), such as social care and nursing, are paid less than male-dominated fields.
1.5.4.3.4.2.1.4.3. Con: The gender pay gap is often conflated with the unadjusted pay gap. When all variables other than gender are controlled for, such as hours worked, occupation, education, the pay gap reduces \([p. 2](https://www.glassdoor.com/research/app/uploads/sites/2/2016/03/Glassdoor-Gender-Pay-Gap-Study.pdf)(Based on more than 505,000 salaries shared by full-time U.S. employees on Glassdoor, men earn 24.1 percent higher base pay than women on average. In other words, women earn about 76 cents per dollar men earn. This is consistent \nwith official sources that show women earn on average 75 to 80 cents per dollar earned by men. However, comparing workers with similar age, education and years \nof experience shrinks that gap to 19.2 percent. Further, comparing workers with the same job title, employer and location, the gender pay gap in the U.S. falls to 5.4 percent \(94.6 cents per dollar\). \n• We find a similar pattern in all five countries we examined: a large overall or “unadjusted” gender pay gap, which shrinks to a smaller “adjusted” pay gap once statistical controls are added.)\).
1.5.4.3.4.2.1.5. Pro: -> See 1.3.5.2.4.
1.5.4.3.4.2.1.6. Pro: Measures of the gender pay gap among recent college graduates show a reverse wage gap; women now [make 8% more](http://content.time.com/time/business/article/0,8599,2015274,00.html) than their male counterparts.
1.5.4.3.4.2.1.7. Pro: The gendered wage gap is thought to be between 4.8 and 7.1%, which is within one standard deviation. This is insignificant from a statistical standpoint \([p. 1](https://web.archive.org/web/20160327195224/http://www.hawaii.edu/religion/courses/Gender_Wage_Gap_Report.pdf)\).
1.5.4.3.4.2.2. Con: Both men and women are subject to [environmental forces](https://qz.com/911737/silicon-valleys-gender-gap-is-the-result-of-computer-game-marketing-20-years-ago/) which influence their decisions. With feminism, we can eliminate unfair targeting, and allow more people to enter into careers which previously they may not have considered.
1.5.4.3.4.2.3. Pro: Women were able to reach the top of society before feminism existed. Both [Cleopatra](https://www.history.com/news/10-little-known-facts-about-cleopatra) and [Maria Theresa](https://www.dw.com/en/what-made-austrias-maria-theresa-a-one-of-a-kind-ruler/a-37935974) were leaders of their respective states.
1.5.4.3.4.2.3.1. Con: Both [Cleopatra](https://www.smithsonianmag.com/history/who-was-cleopatra-151356013/) and [Maria Theresa](https://www.habsburger.net/en/persons/habsburg-emperor/maria-theresa) rose to power due to lineage. Their ascension had nothing to do with their successes.
1.5.4.3.4.2.3.2. Pro: Whilst historically women did not regularly reach the top of society, they still existed in [prominent positions](https://www.history.com/news/royal-mistress-power-england-france-prince-william), and were successful enough to benefit from [regal patronage](https://www.metmuseum.org/toah/hd/18wa/hd_18wa.htm)(Between 1780 and 1810, many French women painters reached impressive heights of artistic achievement and professional success. Despite a cap on the number of women admitted to France’s prestigious Académie Royale de Peinture et de Sculpture, and restrictions that barred women from the life drawing classes attended by young men aspiring to paint historical narratives, women ranked among the most sought-after artists in Paris in the 1780s. Three of the Académie’s four female members—Adélaïde Labille-Guiard \(1749–1803\), Anne Vallayer-Coster \(1744–1818\), and Élisabeth Louise Vigée Le Brun \(1755–1842\)—regularly exhibited at the biennial Salons.\n\nRoyal women were the most important patrons for many women artists.).
1.5.4.3.4.2.3.3. Pro: Historically, women could take on roles in [business](https://www.cam.ac.uk/citywomen), be [merchants](https://www.cambridge.org/core/journals/journal-of-british-studies/article/abs/female-merchants-women-debt-and-trade-in-later-medieval-england-12661532/E8F38B5B164098694C3C518B4AAF114F), and run [apothecaries](https://www.sciencehistory.org/distillations/womens-business-17th-century-female-pharmacists).
1.5.4.3.4.3. Con: The existence of women leaders in prominent and powerful positions is evidence that equality of opportunity has been achieved; feminism is no longer necessary.
1.5.4.3.4.3.1. Pro: Many companies [report](https://www.mckinsey.com/featured-insights/diversity-and-inclusion/ten-things-to-know-about-gender-equality)(The research finds that 87 percent of North American companies today report gender diversity is a top priority, compared with 74 percent in 2015, but this reported priority still needs to translate into more decisive action. Representation of women in the C-suite in North America has increased to 21 percent, from 17 percent in 2015.) that gender parity is a top priority for them, signalling further that equality of opportunity has either been achieved or will be soon.
1.5.4.3.4.3.2. Con: Given the [glass cliff](https://www.investopedia.com/terms/g/glass-cliff.asp) phenomenon, women in leadership do not signal gender parity; equality is only achieved when all positions have roughly equal gender representation.
1.5.4.3.4.3.3. Pro: A patriarchal status quo does not exist in many Western societies, as evidenced by women in positions of power. [Theresa May](https://www.civilserviceworld.com/professions/article/theresa-may-to-promote-women-as-she-becomes-prime-minister), [Hillary Rodham Clinton](https://www.wnycstudios.org/podcasts/takeaway/segments/266407-was-hillary-clinton-better-ambassador-secretary-state), and [Kamala Harris](https://www.npr.org/2020/11/07/930858267/game-changer-kamala-harris-makes-history-as-next-vice-president?t=1635775764602) demonstrate the heights women can achieve.
1.5.4.3.4.3.4. Con: The US senate is overwhelmingly male, with a sparse handful of current and former [female senators](https://www.senate.gov/senators/ListofWomenSenators.htm).
1.5.4.3.4.3.5. Con: In 2017, there were [only 15](http://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2017/03/08/women-leaders-around-the-world/)(There are 15 female world leaders currently in office, eight of whom are their country’s first woman in power, according to our analysis of data from WEF and other sources.) female world leaders in office in the world, eight of whom were their country’s first woman in power.
1.5.4.3.4.4. Pro: [More women](http://www.equilar.com/reports/48-associated-press-ceo-pay-study-2017.html) are in C-suite positions in Fortune 500 companies than ever before.
1.5.4.3.4.4.1. Pro: Even the increased number of women on boards represents [just 6%](http://www.equilar.com/reports/48-associated-press-ceo-pay-study-2017.html) of C-suite positions, speaking to the level of past inequality and the success of feminism in correcting inequality.
1.5.4.3.4.4.2. Con: Many changes facilitated by feminism are too slow. [In the G7](https://www.grantthornton.global/en/insights/articles/women-in-business-2016/), just 22% of senior roles are occupied by women and 39% of companies have no women at all in senior roles.
